Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Third Principle: Imam A'zam's Saying Preferred
States the rule for preferring Imam A'zam's saying over Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the third principle of tasheeh ranking and apply it when deciding between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in conflict.

Core Idea
When two authenticated rulings conflict, Imam Abu Hanifa's saying prevails over his students' if authentication is equal.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, a mufti often encounters conflicting rulings that have both been authenticated (tasheeh) by later scholars. The 'Principles of Tasheeh' provide a ranking hierarchy to resolve such conflicts. This lesson introduces the third principle: when authentication quality is equal, the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa himself is given precedence over the sayings of his principal disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), as well as other early companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting sayings
Determine that one saying is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and the other to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and/or Muhammad) or another early companion.
2
Verify authentication (tasheeh) status
Check that both sayings have been authenticated by later scholars using similar wording (e.g., both marked 'asahh' or 'mukhtar') and that the correcting scholars are of equal rank.
If authentication wording or corrector rank differs, this principle does not apply.
3
Apply the third principle
If both sayings are equally authenticated, give preference to the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa.
4
Document the ruling
Record the preferred ruling and the basis for the preference (the third principle) in the fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیسرا اصول : امام اعظم کا قول راج ہوگا جب دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے ایک امام اعظم کا قول ہو اور دوسرا قول صاحبین یا امام اعظم کے دیگر اصحاب کا ہو اور صحیح کے لئے ایک ہی طرح کے الفاظ استعمال کئے گئے ہوں، نیز تصحیح کرنے والے کا علمی مقام بھی یکساں ہو تو امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ کے قول کو ان کے اصحاب اور صاحبین کے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی۔
Third principle: The saying of Imam A'zam will be preferable. When among two conflicting corrected sayings, one is the saying of Imam A'zam and the other is the saying of the Sahibayn or other companions of Imam A'zam, and for the correction similar words have been used, and the scholarly status of the corrector is also equal, then the saying of Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa will have preference over the sayings of his companions and the Sahibayn.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This is a rasm rule (principle of ranking) used by the Hanafi mufti when faced with two conflicting rulings that have both been authenticated (tasheeh) by later scholars. If all other factors are equal (same type of authentication wording, same level of the corrector), then the statement attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa himself is given precedence over the statements of his two main disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) or other early followers. This reflects the foundational authority of the Imam within the madhhab.

Key Terms
امام اعظم (Imam A'zam): Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, the founder of the Hanafi school.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal students of Abu Hanifa.
تصحیح شدہ (tashih shuda): Rulings that have been authenticated by later scholars as correct transmissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two corrected sayings conflict, both equally authenticated, one from Imam Abu Hanifa and one from the Sahibayn, which saying is preferred?
A) The saying of the Sahibayn
B) The saying of Imam Abu Hanifa
C) The saying that is easier for the people
D) The saying from Zahir al-Riwayah

Key Takeaway
The third principle: when authentication is equal, the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is preferred over the Sahibayn.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Fourth Principle: Zahir al-Riwayah Preferred
Establishes priority of Zahir al-Riwayah over non-Zahir transmissions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fourth principle of Rasm al-Mufti to identify which of two conflicting correct sayings is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When two equally corrected sayings conflict, the one from Zahir al-Riwayah is preferred.

You have learned that in the Hanafi madhhab, fatwa is based on the most reliable transmission. This lesson presents a key rule from the Rasm al-Mufti tradition: when two corrected sayings are equal in authentication, the one found in Zahir al-Riwayah takes precedence. Understanding this hierarchy ensures that fatwa outcomes rest on the strongest sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
You have two conflicting sayings on a legal issue, each corrected (declared sahih) by authoritative scholars.
The conflict must be real and not resolvable by other means.
2
Verify equal authentication
Check that the correctors used similar wording (e.g., 'sahih') and have equal scholarly status.
If one correction uses a stronger term like 'asahh' or the scholar is more authoritative, the rule may not apply.
3
Check source of each saying
Determine which saying is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) and which is in non-Zahir (nawadir).
Zahir al-Riwayah books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat.
4
Apply the rule
Prefer the saying from Zahir al-Riwayah; it becomes the operative (mufta bihi) ruling.
This rule is definitive in the Hanafi school when conditions are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھا اصول: ظاہر الروایہ کا قول راج ہوگا (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٤٥) جب دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے ہر قول کی تصحیح کے لیے ایک ہی طرح کے الفان صیح[؟] استعمال کئے گئے ہوں، نیز تصحیح کرنے والے کا علمی مقام بھی یکساں ہو اور ایک قول ظاہر الروایہ میں اور دوسرا قول غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو تو ظاہر الروایہ کا قول دیگر اقوال کے مقابلہ میں رائج ہوگا۔
Fourth principle: The saying of Zahir al-Riwayah will be preferable. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 145) When among two conflicting corrected sayings, for the correction of each saying similar words [؟] have been used, and the scholarly status of the corrector is also equal, and one saying is in Zahir al-Riwayah and the other is in non-Zahir al-Riwayah, then the saying of Zahir al-Riwayah will be prevalent in comparison to other sayings.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This rule prioritizes the canonical transmission. Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the core of the Hanafi madhhab (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.). Non-Zahir al-Riwayah includes rare or weaker transmissions (like those of Hasan ibn Ziyad). When both sayings are equally authenticated, the one from Zahir al-Riwayah is taken.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing the most reliable transmissions.
غیر ظاہر الروایہ (ghayr Zahir al-Riwayah): Nawadir: rare or less authenticated transmissions not in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two corrected sayings are equally authenticated, and one is from Zahir al-Riwayah and the other from non-Zahir al-Riwayah, which is preferred?
A) The non-Zahir al-Riwayah saying
B) The Zahir al-Riwayah saying
C) The saying of Imam Abu Hanifa
D) The saying of the Sahibayn

Key Takeaway
When equally corrected, the saying from Zahir al-Riwayah is mufta bihi.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Fifth Principle of Rasm al-Mufti: Priority of Matn Over Commentaries
Establishes the rule for preferring matn over shuruh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fifth principle of rasm al-mufti to resolve conflicting rulings between matn and sharh sources by identifying equal authentication and preferring the matn.

Core Idea
When equally authenticated, the matn prevails over commentaries because its author committed to the correct position.

A mufti often encounters contradictory rulings from different Hanafi sources. The fifth principle of rasm al-mufti provides clear guidance: when two equally authenticated conflicting sayings are found, one in a matn and the other in a commentary or fatwa collection, the matn takes precedence. This is because the authors of the mutun intentionally confined themselves to the most reliable position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting rulings
Find two rulings that give different answers on the same issue. Note the exact wording and the sources. Both must be tahqiq (corrected) versions.
If only one ruling is present, no conflict exists.
2
Check equal authentication
Ensure both sayings are equally authenticated: same wording of correction, same scholarly rank of the corrector.
If one is more authenticated, that one is followed, and the principle does not apply.
3
Classify each source type
Determine which is a matn (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqayah) and which is a sharh (commentary) or fatawa collection.
Matn are concise, authoritative texts; shuruh expand and may include multiple views.
4
Apply the preference
The saying from the matn is taken over the other, because the matn author committed to recording only the correct position.
This principle is part of the broader tarjih hierarchy in rasm al-mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پانچواں اصول : متون کا قول شروح کے مقابلہ میں راج ہوگا جب دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے ہر قول کی تصحیح کے لیے ایک ہی طرح کے الفاظ استعمال کئے گئے ہوں، نیز تصحیح کرنے والے کا علمی مقام بھی یکساں ہو اور ایک قول متون اور دوسرا قول شروح وفتاوی میں ہو تو متون والے قول کو شروح اور فتاوی کے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، کیوں کہ متون کے مصنفین نے صحیح قول لکھنے کا التزام کیا ہے۔
Fifth principle: The saying of the matn (original text) will be preferable over commentaries. When among two conflicting corrected sayings, for the correction of each saying similar words have been used, and the scholarly status of the corrector is also equal, and one saying is in the matn and the other saying is in commentaries and fatwas, then the saying from the matn will have preference over the saying of commentaries and fatwas, because the authors of the matn have committed themselves to writing the correct saying.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This rule gives priority to the concise authoritative texts (mutun) such as al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, al-Wiqayah, etc., over their commentaries (shuruh) and fatwa collections. The reasoning is that the authors of these matn works specifically undertook the responsibility of including only the correct position. When both sources are equally authenticated, the matn is followed.

Key Terms
متون (mutun): Concise authoritative works in Hanafi fiqh, e.g., al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah.
شروح (shuruh): Commentaries on the matn works, often expanding on various positions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a ruling in a matn conflicts with a ruling in a commentary, and both are equally authenticated, which is preferred?
A) The commentary
B) The matn
C) The fatwa collection
D) The later text

Key Takeaway
When equally authenticated, the matn (original text) is always given precedence over commentaries and fatwa collections in resolving conflicting Hanafi rulings.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner

Sixth Principle: Senior Fuqaha Sayings Preferred
Establishes priority of senior jurists' agreement over lower-rank scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the sixth principle of Rasm al-Mufti to resolve conflicts between two authenticated rulings by identifying the agreement of senior Hanafi jurists.

Core Idea
Senior jurist consensus outweighs minor scholar support in tarjih.

When two sayings are both reported as correct within the Hanafi school, how does a mufti decide? This lesson introduces a key tarjih rule: the agreement of senior jurists (akabir fuqaha) such as Imam Tahawi, Imam Sarakhsi, and Imam Abu Layth al-Samarqandi gives their endorsed saying preference over a saying supported only by lesser-known scholars. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for issuing reliable fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting sayings
First, confirm that two authenticated (musahhah) sayings exist on the issue. They must be correctly attributed within the madhhab.
If only one saying is available, no conflict.
2
Determine the supporters of each saying
For each saying, list the Hanafi jurists who have declared it as sound (sahih). Classify these jurists by their rank: senior (akabir) or lesser (without explicit senior rank).
Senior jurists include later authorities like Tahawi, Sarakhsi, Abu Layth, and others recognized by the school.
3
Check for senior consensus
Examine whether the senior jurists are unanimous in supporting one of the sayings. If they agree, that saying becomes preferred (rajih).
Consensus means agreement, not necessarily a large number—even a few seniors can tip the scale.
4
Apply the preference
If senior consensus exists, the mufta bihi is the saying endorsed by them. If no such consensus, other tarjih principles must be used.
This principle is not about majority count but about the authority weight of the supporters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھٹا اصول: اکابر فقہاء کا قول راجح ہوگا (شرح عقود رسم المفتى : ١٤٥) جب دو متعارض صحیح شد و اقوال میں سے ایک قول کی صحت پر اکابر اور مشہور و معروف فقہاء مثلا امام طحاوی، امام سرخسی اور امام ابواللیث سمرقندی وغیرہ کا اتفاق ہواور دوسرے قول پر ان سے کمتر درجہ کے فقہاء کا اتفاق ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس کی صحت پر اکابر فقہاء کا اتفاق ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٤٥)
Sixth principle: The saying of the senior jurists will be preferable. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 145) When from two conflicting corrected sayings, there is agreement on the correctness of one saying by the senior and famous jurists, such as Imam Tahawi, Imam Sarakhsi, and Imam Abu Layth al-Samarqandi etc., and the other saying is agreed upon by jurists of lower rank than these, then preference will be given to the saying whose correctness is agreed upon by the senior jurists.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This rule deals with the hierarchy of scholars within the Hanafi school. If two conflicting rulings have been authenticated, and one is confirmed by the consensus (or collective agreement) of senior, well-known Hanafi scholars like Imam Tahawi, Imam Sarakhsi, and Imam Abu Layth, while the other is only backed by lesser-known scholars, then the one supported by the seniors takes precedence.

Key Terms
اکابر فقہاء (akabir fuqaha): Senior, authoritative Hanafi jurists from later generations (e.g., Tahawi, Sarakhsi, Abu Layth).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sixth principle, which saying is preferred when two authentic sayings conflict?
A) The saying supported by the majority of all Hanafi jurists
B) The saying supported by the agreement of senior jurists (akabir fuqaha)
C) The saying from the earlier time period
D) The saying that is easier to act upon

Key Takeaway
When two authentic sayings conflict, the one endorsed by senior Hanafi jurists is preferred over one supported only by lesser scholars.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Ninth Principle: Ease for People Preferred
Establishes preference for ease in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ninth principle of rasm al-mufti to identify the preferable ruling when two equally authenticated rulings conflict over ease vs hardship.

Core Idea
When two equally authenticated rulings conflict, prefer the one that brings ease to people.

The Hanafi tradition recognizes that Shari'ah was revealed to bring ease and remove hardship. This principle guides the mufti when facing conflicting rulings that are both authentically transmitted. In such cases, the ruling that facilitates people's affairs is given weight, reflecting the maqasid al-shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting rulings
Determine that both rulings are equally authenticated (mu'tamad, not weak vs strong). If not equally authenticated, the stronger prevails regardless of ease.
2
Assess relative ease and hardship
Compare which ruling brings suhulat (ease) and which brings haraj (hardship) for the people. Consider the practical impact on the community.
3
Apply the preference
Prefer the ruling that brings ease, given that both are equally authentic. This is based on the Shari'ah's temperament of taysir.
4
Consider scope and exceptions
This principle applies only when both rulings are equally authenticated. If one is stronger in riwayah, ease does not override strength. Also, it does not permit choosing a weak narration for convenience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نواں اصول بسہولت والا قول راجح ہوگا دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ایک قول میں لوگوں کے لئے سہولت اور آسانی ہو اور دوسرے قول میں لوگوں کے لئے حرج اور تنگی ہو تو شریعت کے مزاج و مذاق کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس میں آسانی ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى : ١٤٦ ، اصول الافتاء و آدابه: ٢٢٦)
Ninth principle: The saying that brings ease will be preferable. Among two conflicting corrected sayings, if one saying brings ease and convenience for the people and the other saying brings difficulty and restriction for the people, then, observing the temperament and spirit of the Shari'ah, preference will be given to the saying in which there is ease. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 146, Usul al-Ifta' wa Adabihi: 226)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This rule is rooted in the Qur'anic and Sunnah principle that Shari'ah is based on ease and removal of hardship. When two equally authenticated rulings conflict, the mufti should prefer the one that brings ease (suhulat) to the people over the one that causes difficulty (haraj). This reflects the maqasid al-shari'ah and the Hanafi commitment to applying the spirit of the law.

Key Terms
سہولت (suhulat): Ease, convenience, lack of hardship in a ruling.
حرج (haraj): Hardship, difficulty, restriction that a ruling may impose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two equally authenticated rulings conflict, one bringing ease and the other hardship, which is preferred?
A) The one bringing hardship
B) The one bringing ease
C) The one from the senior fuqaha
D) The one from the matn

Key Takeaway
Among equally authenticated rulings, the mufti must prefer the one that brings ease, reflecting the Shari'ah's spirit of taysir.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Seventh Principle: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Establishes preference rule for conflicting corrected statements based on istihsan vs qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of istihsan over qiyas when tarjih is needed among corrected statements, and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
Istihsan prevails over qiyas in tarjih of conflicting corrected statements, but exceptions exist.

When two corrected statements clash, which one should a mufti prefer? This lesson introduces the seventh principle of Rasm al-Mufti: istihsan overrides qiyas. However, the rule is not absolute; several exceptions require qiyas to be followed instead. Understanding both the rule and its exceptions is crucial for sound fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the principle
Commit to memory: Istihsan prevails over qiyas in tarjih of corrected statements.
This is the default rule.
2
Learn the reasoning
Understand why: istihsan has greater strength (quwwa) than qiyas, as stated in the passage.
The strength is based on its suitability and weight in the school.
3
Identify the exceptions
Know that there are cases where qiyas is preferred over istihsan (راجح قیاسی مسائل). The number varies by scholar.
Al-Nasafi counted 2; Mufti Mansurpuri counted 26.
4
Apply the principle
In a conflict, first check if the case is an exception. If not, prefer istihsan. If it is, follow qiyas.
Always verify with authoritative lists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتواں اصول : استحسان قیاس پر راج ہوگا

دو متعارض تصحیح شد و اقوال میں سے جس قول کی بنیاد استحسان پر ہوگی اس قول کو قیاس والے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، کیوں کہ قیاس کے مقابلہ میں استحسان کے اندر زیادہ قوت ہوتی ہے، پس اسی کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی لیکن چند مسائل ایسے ہیں جہاں استحسان کو چھوڑ کر قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٤٥) واضح ہو کہ راجح قیاسی مسائل کی تعداد علامہ ناطفی کی الاجناس میں اار بیان کی گئی ہے، جبکہ امام نجم الدین النسفی کے یہاں ایسے مسائل کی تعداد ۲ رہے۔ (اعضا ۱۲۹) نوٹ: حضرت اقدس مفتی سلمان منصور پوری نے انتہائی تحقیق اور تلاش بسیار کے بعد فتوی نویسی کے رہنما اصول (صفحه ۲۳۴۰ تا ۲۵۴ ) میں ان مسائل کی تعداد ۲۶ / بیان کی ہے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کی دل نشیں وضاحت بھی کی ہے۔
Seventh principle: Istihsan will prevail over qiyas.

Among two conflicting corrected statements, whichever statement is based on istihsan will have preference over the statement based on qiyas, because in comparison to qiyas, istihsan has greater strength; thus it gets preference. However, there are a few issues where qiyas will be acted upon leaving aside istihsan. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 145) It is clear that the number of preferred qiyas issues has been mentioned by Allamah al-Natifi in his book al-Jinas as 'aar' [unclear], while Imam Najm al-Din al-Nasafi mentioned such issues as 2. (A'da 129) Note: His Holiness Mufti Salman Mansurpuri, after thorough research and extensive investigation, has mentioned the count of these issues as 26 in his book Fatawa Nawisi ke Rehnama Usul (pp. 2340-254) and also provided a delightful explanation for each of them.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh principle of tarjih (preference) in the context of conflicting corrected statements (tasḥīḥ shuda aqwāl) in Hanafi fiqh. The principle states that if one statement is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference) and the other on qiyās (analogy), the statement based on istiḥsān is given preference because it carries greater legal weight. However, this is a general rule; there are exceptions where qiyās is actually preferred over istiḥsān. The passage then notes the counts of such exceptional cases according to different scholars: Allamah al-Nāṭifī in his work al-Jinās, Imam Najm al-Dīn al-Nasafī, and later Mufti Salmān Manṣūrpūrī who listed 26 such issues with detailed explanations. These exceptions show that the rule is not absolute, and a mufti must know both the rule and its exceptions.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of ijtihad that gives preference to a ruling that is more suitable for people or for legal reasoning over strict analogy.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction; drawing a legal ruling for a new case based on an existing ruling from the revealed sources due to shared illah.
تصحیح شدہ اقوال (taṣḥīḥ shuda aqwāl): Statements or rulings that have been authenticated and deemed correct by later Hanafi jurists from among the transmitted opinions of the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the seventh principle of tarjih, when two conflicting corrected statements exist, what determines preferred status?
A) The statement based on qiyas is preferred.
B) The statement based on istihsan is preferred.
C) Both are equal; the mufti may choose.
D) The statement that is more recent is preferred.

Key Takeaway
The seventh principle of Rasm al-Mufti: istihsan prevails over qiyas, but exceptions exist and must be learned.

Eighth Principle: Anfa‘ lil-Waqf
Preference rule for waqf based on benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the eighth principle of tarjih to identify the preferred opinion (mufta bih) in waqf-related disputes, evaluating benefit to the endowment and its beneficiaries.

Core Idea
In waqf, the opinion more beneficial for the endowment and its beneficiaries is preferred.

When a mufti encounters two conflicting corrected statements in waqf matters, he cannot simply choose arbitrarily. This lesson introduces a specific tarjih principle unique to endowments: the opinion that brings greater benefit to the waqf property, its beneficiaries, and the purpose of the endowment is to be preferred. This principle operationalizes the maqasid of preserving and maximizing charitable trusts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting opinions
Begin by recognizing that you are dealing with a waqf issue and that there are two (or more) corrected statements from the school. Ensure that both are authentically transmitted and reconciled as much as possible.
This principle only applies after the two statements are deemed equally credible and otherwise unresolved.
2
Evaluate benefit for the waqf
Analyse each opinion’s impact on three dimensions: the waqf property (shay’ al-mawqūf), the beneficiaries (mawqūf ‘alayhim), and the overall purpose of the endowment. Consider long-term sustainability, maintenance, and fulfillment of the waqif’s condition.
Benefit here means material and spiritual well-being, aligned with Sharī‘ah objectives.
3
Prefer the more beneficial opinion
Select the opinion that yields greater net benefit. This opinion becomes the rājih (preferred) and is the mufta bih (relied-upon) for fatwa.
If both are equally beneficial, other tarjīḥ principles apply.
4
Apply only to waqf matters
Confirm that this principle is specific to waqf. Do not extend it to general transactions or other areas of fiqh without proper analogy.
Common misunderstanding: using this principle for non-waqf cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آٹھواں اصول: انفع للوقف والا قول راجح ہوگا دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر کوئی قول واقف موقوف علیہم اور خودشیء موقوف کے لئے زیادہ نفع بخش ہو اور دوسرے قول میں یہ نفع موجود نہ ہوتو انفع للوقف والا قول راجح اور مفتی بہ ہوگا ۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٤٦)
Eighth principle: The statement that is more beneficial for the waqf will be preferred. Among two conflicting corrected statements, if one statement is more beneficial for the endowment, the beneficiaries, and the endowed property itself, and the other statement does not have this benefit, then the statement that is more beneficial for the waqf will be preferred and will be the mufta bih (relied-upon opinion). (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 146)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth principle of tarjih specifically applicable to issues of waqf (endowment). When a mufti encounters two conflicting corrected statements in waqf matters, he should choose the one that is more beneficial for the waqf itself, the beneficiaries (mawqūf ʿalayhim), and the endowed property (shay' al-mawqūf). This principle aligns with the general maqasid of preserving and maximizing the benefit of endowments, which is a key objective of Islamic property law. The preference is based on the legal reason (talil) of maslahah for the waqf.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): An Islamic endowment; a charitable trust in which property is dedicated for religious or charitable purposes.
انفع للوقف (anfaʿ lil-waqf): More beneficial for the waqf, considering the property, beneficiaries, and purpose of the endowment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Waqf
C) Zakat
D) Talaq

Key Takeaway
The eighth principle of tarjih – prefer the opinion more beneficial for the waqf – guides muftis to preserve and maximize charitable endowments.

Tenth Principle: Strong Evidence Preference in Tarjih
Tarjih rule for conflicting corrected statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the tenth principle of tarjih: identify the stronger evidence between two conflicting corrected statements and determine which one is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Strong evidence (sahih/mashhur hadith) outweighs weak or absent hadith in tarjih.

When a mufti encounters two corrected statements from the madhhab, he cannot rely solely on the jurist's authority; he must also assess the strength of the underlying evidence. This principle guides him to prefer the statement backed by a sound and well-known hadith over one that relies on no hadith or a weak one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two corrected statements
Find two tasḥīḥ-corrected statements that conflict on the same issue. Label them Statement A and Statement B.
Corrected statements are those that have been selected as the relied-upon view in later works.
2
Analyze the evidence behind each
Determine the type of evidence (dalīl) supporting each statement. Check if the evidence is from the Quran, Sunnah (especially hadith), or other sources.
The principle specifically highlights hadith evidence, but can extend to other strong proofs.
3
Classify the strength of hadith evidence
For each hadith cited, classify it as ṣaḥīḥ (authentic) and mashhūr (well-known), or as ḍaʿīf (weak), or note if no hadith is present.
Mashhūr in Hanafi usage is a hadith with multiple chains, close to mustafīḍ.
4
Apply the preference rule
Prefer the statement whose evidence is a ṣaḥīḥ and mashhūr hadith. If one statement has such proof and the other does not, the former is mufta bihi. If both or neither have strong hadith, other tarjih factors apply.
This principle does not override tasḥīḥ; it only resolves conflicts among equally corrected statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دسواں اصول: قومی دلیل پر مبنی قول رائج ہوگا
جب دو تعارض تصیح شدہ اقوال میں سے ایک قول کی بنیاد صحیح اور مشہور ومعروف حدیث پر ہو اور دوسرے قول کی بنیا دسرے سے کسی حدیث ہی پر نہ ہو یا کسی ضعیف سند والی حدیث پر اس کی بنیاد ہو تو ترجیح اس قول کو حاصل ہوگی جس کی بنیاد مضبوط دلیل پر ہو۔
شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ١٤٦،٩٤ ، اصول الافتاء و آدابه : ٢٢٦)
Tenth principle: The statement based on strong evidence will be preferred. When there are two conflicting corrected statements, if one statement is based on a sound and well-known hadith, and the other statement is not based on any hadith at all or is based on a hadith with a weak chain of transmission, then preference will be given to the statement that is based on strong evidence. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 146, 94, Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the tenth principle of tarjih, which prioritizes the strength of evidence (dalīl). When a mufti finds two conflicting corrected statements, he should assess the proofs behind them. The statement that is supported by a ṣaḥīḥ (authentic) and mashhūr (well-known) hadith is given preference over one that has no hadith evidence or relies on a ḍaʿīf (weak) hadith. This principle emphasizes that even in tarjih among corrected statements, the mufti must consider the underlying textual evidence, not just the authority of the jurist who made the statement. It also shows that a corrected statement that lacks strong scriptural backing is less reliable.

Key Terms
حدیث مشہور (ḥadīth mashhūr): A hadith that is well-known among scholars, transmitted by multiple chains, though not necessarily mutawatir.
ضعیف (ḍaʿīf): Weak hadith; a hadith whose chain of transmission or text is defective, making it less reliable for legal proof.
قول رائج (qawl rā'ij): The prevalent or preferred statement among later Hanafi scholars, often the mufta bihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qiyas
B) Istihsan
C) A sound and well-known hadith
D) The majority opinion of scholars

Key Takeaway
When two corrected statements conflict, the mufti must prefer the one supported by strong evidence, specifically a ṣaḥīḥ and mashhūr hadith.

Eleventh Principle: Favoring the Poor in Zakat Conflicts
Preference rule in zakat issues favoring the poor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the eleventh principle of tarjih (al-ʾanfaʿ li-l-fuqarāʾ) to resolve conflicting zakat rulings when both statements are equally preferred.

Core Idea
When two zakat rulings are equally preferred, choose the one more beneficial for the poor.

In Hanafi iftaa, muftis often face conflicting statements within the school. The eleventh principle of tarjih provides a tie-breaker specifically for zakat matters: when two corrected statements (aqwāl muṣaḥḥaḥa) are equivalent in authority—same wording for tasḥīḥ and same scholarly rank—the mufti should prefer the statement that best serves the interests of the poor and needy (fuqarāʾ wa masākīn). This principle reflects the central maqṣad of zakat: fulfilling the needs of the poor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting statements
Determine the two zakat rulings that are both considered 'muṣaḥḥaḥ' (corrected) in the Hanafi school.
These may be from different Hanafi authorities or different narrations.
2
Check equality of preference
Verify that both statements have been given preference using the same wording (e.g., 'wa ʿalayh al-fatwā') and that the jurists who gave preference are of equal scholarly standing.
If one statement has stronger evidence or higher authority, the principle does not apply.
3
Assess benefit to the poor
Evaluate which statement yields a more beneficial outcome for the fuqarāʾ and masākīn. Consider practical effects: earlier distribution, higher amount, or easier access.
The benefit is assessed from the perspective of the recipients, not the payer.
4
Apply the rule
Select the statement that is more beneficial. This becomes the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the case.
Document the reasoning in the fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گیارہواں اصول: الفع للفقراء کا قول رائج ہوگا
زکوۃ کے باب میں اگر دو مختلف اقوال کو ایک ہی طرح کے الفاظ سے ترجیح دی گئی ہو اور ترجیح دینے والے فقہاء کی علمی حیثیت بھی برابر ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جو فقراء و مساکین کے لیے زیادہ مفید ہو۔ (اصول الافتاء وآدابه بتغيير: ٢٢٦)
Eleventh principle: The statement that is more beneficial for the poor will be preferred. In the chapter of zakat, if two different statements have been given preference with the same kind of words, and the scientific status of the jurists who gave preference is also equal, then the statement that is more beneficial for the poor and needy will get preference. (Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu with modification: 226)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh principle of tarjih, which is specific to the chapter of zakat. When a mufti faces two conflicting corrected statements in zakat matters, and both statements have been given equal preference by scholars of equal standing (same wording for tasḥīḥ, same scholarly rank), then the mufti should choose the statement that is more beneficial for the poor and needy (fuqarā' wa masākīn). This principle reflects the maqṣad of zakat, which is to fulfill the needs of the poor. The condition of equality in wording and scholarly rank ensures that this rule does not override stronger evidence; it applies only when the two statements are otherwise equivalent.

Key Terms
فقراء (fuqarā'): Poor people eligible for zakat; according to Hanafi fiqh, those who possess less than the nisab.
مساکین (masākīn): Needy people; in Hanafi classification, those who have some resources but insufficient to meet basic needs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) When one statement is based on a weak hadith
D) When the statement is more beneficial for the waqf

Key Takeaway
The eleventh principle of tarjih directs the mufti to prefer the zakat ruling more beneficial to the poor when conflicting statements are equally authoritative.

Preferring the Statement That Drops Hudud
Preference rule favoring statements that drop hudud punishments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the twelfth principle of tarjih to prefer the statement that drops the hadd when faced with equally corrected conflicting statements.

Core Idea
When statements are equal, the one that drops the hudud prevails.

In the Hanafi tradition of ifta, a mufti often encounters conflicting corrected statements from the madhhab. The twelfth principle of tarjih provides a clear rule: if two statements are equally corrected in wording and the scholars who corrected them are of equal rank, the mufti must choose the statement that leads to the non-application of a fixed punishment (ḥadd). This aligns with the overarching Sharia maxim that ḥudūd are dropped by doubts (al-ḥudūd tuhdaru bi al-shubuhāt).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
Identify that you have two conflicting statements that have both been 'corrected' (tasḥīḥ) with identical wording and by scholars of equal standing.
This principle only applies when the corrections are perfectly matched.
2
Assess equality
Verify that the wording of the correction is the same and the correcting scholars are of equal rank. If either differs, a different tarjih principle may apply.
Equality in both wording and rank is a strict condition.
3
Identify the statement that drops the hadd
Among the two statements, determine which one results in the non-application of the ḥadd punishment (e.g., it recognizes a doubt that waives the penalty).
The statement that avoids the penalty is to be preferred.
4
Apply the preference
Give preference (tarjīḥ) to that statement and issue the fatwa accordingly.
The ruling is now muftā bihi.
5
Confirm with the underlying maxim
Recall that this preference is rooted in the general principle: 'Ḥudūd are dropped by doubts.' This ensures that in borderline cases, the benefit of doubt goes to the accused.
The maxim is a major pillar of Hanafi criminal jurisprudence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بارہواں اصول حدود کو ساقط کرنے والا قول راجح ہوگا متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح ایک ہی جیسے الفاظ سے کی جائے اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا مقام و مرتبہ بھی یکساں ہو تو ان میں سے جو قول حدود شرعیہ کو ساقط کرنے والا ہو اس کو دوسرے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، اس لیے کہ شبہات کی بناء پر حدود شرعیہ ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں۔ (اصول الافتاء وآدابه : ٢٢٦)
Twelfth principle: The statement that drops the hudud will be preferred. Among conflicting corrected statements, if each statement has been corrected with the same words and the positions of the jurists who made the correction are also equal, then the statement that drops the prescribed hudud punishments will have preference over the other statement, because on the basis of doubts, the prescribed hudud punishments are dropped. (Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the twelfth principle of tarjih, which applies specifically to cases involving ḥudūd (fixed corporal punishments). When two conflicting corrected statements are equal in terms of the wording of tasḥīḥ and the rank of the scholars, the mufti should prefer the statement that leads to the non-application (sāqiṭ) of the ḥadd punishment. The reason is that in Islamic law, ḥudūd are suspended in cases of doubt (shubuhāt). This principle is derived from the famous legal maxim: 'Ḥudūd are dropped by doubts' (الحدود تدرأ بالشبهات). It ensures that in borderline cases, the benefit of doubt goes to the accused, aligning with the Sharia's emphasis on mercy and caution in applying severe penalties.

Key Terms
حدود (ḥudūd): Fixed punishments prescribed by Sharia for certain crimes, such as theft, fornication, and drinking alcohol.
شبہات (shubuhāt): Legal doubts or ambiguous circumstances that can prevent the application of hudud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the scholars of correction are of equal rank

Key Takeaway
When two corrected statements are equal in wording and scholar rank, the mufti must prefer the one that avoids the hadd, in line with the maxim that hudud are dropped by doubts.

Thirteenth Principle: Prohibition Preference
Preference rule favoring statements indicating prohibition over permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the thirteenth principle of tarjih and apply the maxim 'When halal and haram coincide, prohibition takes precedence' to a set of equally corrected statements.

Core Idea
When equally corrected statements conflict, prefer the one indicating prohibition over permissibility.

This lesson covers a key tarjih principle from the Hanafi school: when two equally authenticated and corrected statements contradict each other, the mufti must give preference to the statement that indicates prohibition over the one indicating permissibility. This cautious approach is rooted in the well-known legal maxim that when halal and haram are mixed, the prohibition side is given weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The principle applies only when the conflicting statements are both equally corrected (tasḥīḥ) with the same wording and the jurists who corrected them are of equal rank.
If the tasḥīḥ or ranks differ, other tarjih principles apply.
2
Recall the underlying maxim
The basis is the famous Hanafi maxim: 'When halal and haram come together, the prohibition is given precedence' (إذا اجتمع الحلال والحرام غلب الحرام).
This maxim reflects a cautious approach in fiqh.
3
Apply to a hypothetical case
Suppose two equally corrected fatwas exist: one says a certain sale is permissible (ḥillat), the other says it is prohibited (ḥurmat). The mufti should prefer the prohibition opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیرہواں اصول : حرمت والا قول راجح ہوگا
متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح ایک ہی جیسے الفاظ سے کی جائے اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا مقام و مرتبہ بھی یکساں ہو تو ان میں سے جس قول میں حرمت کا پہلو ہو اس قول کو حلت والے قول پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی، کیوں کہ فقہ کا مشہور قاعدہ ہے: جب حلال و حرام کا اجتماع ہو جائے تو حرمت والے پہلو کو ترجیح دی جائے گی۔
اصول الافتاء و آدابه: ٢٢٦)
Thirteenth principle: The statement that indicates prohibition will be preferred. Among conflicting corrected statements, if each statement has been corrected with the same words and the positions of the jurists who made the correction are also equal, then the statement that contains the aspect of prohibition will have preference over the statement that contains permissibility, because there is a famous rule in fiqh: When halal and haram come together, the aspect of prohibition is given preference. (Usul al-Ifta wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the thirteenth principle of tarjih, which gives preference to statements indicating prohibition (ḥurma) over those indicating permissibility (ḥilla). This applies when the conflicting corrected statements are equal in the wording of tasḥīḥ and the scholarly rank of the correctors. The basis is the well-known Hanafi legal maxim: 'When halal and haram coincide, the aspect of prohibition is given precedence' (إِذَا اجْتَمَعَ الْحَلَالُ وَالْحَرَامُ غُلِّبَ الْحَرَامُ). This principle reflects a cautious approach in fiqh, especially in matters where there is a potential overlap of permissible and forbidden elements. It ensures that in doubtful cases, the mufti opts for the safer ruling that avoids transgression.

Key Terms
حرمت (ḥurmat): Prohibition; a ruling that deems an action unlawful.
حلت (ḥillat): Permissibility; a ruling deeming an action lawful.

D) The statement drops a hadd punishment

Key Takeaway
The thirteenth principle directs the mufti to prefer prohibition over permissibility when two equally corrected and equally authoritative statements conflict.

The Fourteenth Principle: Preferring Based on Public Interest
Rule for tiebreaking among corrected opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fourteenth principle to prefer an opinion based on maslahah when all other tarjih factors are equal.

Core Idea
When all other criteria are equal, the mufti chooses the opinion that better serves public interest.

This final principle in the series addresses a practical scenario: when two opinions are corrected with identical wording by scholars of equal rank, the mufti faces a tie. The fourteenth principle resolves this by looking beyond the textual correction to the underlying benefit. Drawing on al-Ashbah and al-Bazzaziyyah, the rule instructs the mufti to prefer the opinion that aligns with public interest (maslahah) and custom ('urf). This reflects the Hanafi method of istihsan, where secondary considerations can tip the balance when primary evidence is inconclusive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mufti has two opinions that are both 'corrected' (musahhah) with identical phrasing by scholars of equal rank. All other tarjih factors (wording, scholar rank) are equal.
Correction (tas-hih) is the authentication of a transmitted opinion within the school.
2
Confirm other factors are equal
Ensure that no other preference criteria exist, such as stronger textual evidence, more direct transmission, or higher scholarly authority.
This principle is the last resort; it only activates when prior tarjih methods fail to differentiate.
3
Apply the maslahah/'urf test
Examine which opinion better serves public interest or aligns with established custom. This can be based on general benefit or common practice.
Maslahah here is restricted to situations where no explicit nass is contradicted.
4
Cite supporting authority
The rule is supported by al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir (citing al-Bazzaziyyah) and appears in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
This indicates the rule is from the later fatwa literature, not the foundational texts.
5
State the ruling
The mufti gives fatwa according to the opinion that contains maslahah or is based on 'urf.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) rule for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چودہواں اصول مصلحت پر مبنی قول راج ہوگا
دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح یکساں الفاظ سے کی گئی ہو اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا رتبہ بھی برابر ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس کی بنیاد مصلحت اور عرف وغیرہ پر ہو، چنانچہ الاشباہ میں بزازیہ کے حوالہ سے منقول ہے کہ مفتی اس قول پر فتوی دے گا جس میں کوئی مصلحت ہو۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٦٩)
Fourteenth Principle: The opinion based on maslahah (public interest) will be preferred. Among two conflicting corrected opinions, if each opinion is corrected with similar wording and the rank of the correcting scholars is equal, then preference will be given to the opinion based on maslahah, custom ('urf), etc. Accordingly, it is narrated in al-Ashbah from al-Bazzaziyyah that the mufti will give fatwa according to the opinion in which there is some maslahah. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 169)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This final principle introduces consideration of public interest (maslahah) and custom ('urf) as a tarjih factor. When all other criteria are equal, the mufti selects the opinion that better serves the people's welfare. The text cites al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir and al-Bazzaziyyah, indicating the use of juristic preference (istihsan) in fatwa selection. This aligns with the Hanafi reliance on custom and public benefit as secondary sources.

Key Terms
مصلحت (maslahah): Public interest or benefit; a consideration in juristic preference.
عرف (urf): Custom or common practice of the people; considered as a basis for preference when not contradicting a clear text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fourteenth principle, when two corrected opinions are equal in wording and scholar rank, what should a mufti consider?
A) The opinion of the majority of scholars.
B) The opinion that is more convenient for the judge.
C) The opinion based on public interest (maslahah) or custom.
D) The opinion that is older.

Key Takeaway
When all tarjih factors are equal, the mufti prefers the opinion that better serves public interest ('urf and maslahah).

The Fourteenth Principle: Preference for Maslahah-Based Sayings
Rule for preferring a saying based on public interest when conflicting corrected sayings are equal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourteenth principle of rasm al-mufti, apply it when two sayings are equally corrected, and explain how conflicting grounds of preference are resolved through mufti's discretion.

Core Idea
When corrected sayings are equal, maslahah tips the scale — but if grounds conflict, the mufti's judgment governs.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, not all grounds of preference are absolute. This lesson introduces a key rule: when two equally corrected sayings conflict, the one grounded in public interest (maslahah) and custom (urf) is preferred. However, as Mufti Taqi Usmani explains, these grounds can conflict, and no universal rule resolves that—the mufti must rely on his juristic aptitude.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for applying the rule
The rule applies only when two sayings are equally corrected with the same wording and the correcting scholars are of equal rank. If these conditions are not met, other grounds may dominate.
The condition of equality is crucial.
2
Recognize the role of maslahah and urf
When conditions are equal, the saying aligning with public interest (maslahah) and custom (urf) is preferred. This ensures fatwa remains relevant to societal needs.
3
Understand the limitation: conflicting grounds
Grounds of preference can conflict (e.g., Zahir al-Riwayah vs. Imam's own statement). In such cases, no universal rule applies; the mufti must use his sound judgment (dhawq sahih) and juristic aptitude.
The mufti may choose caution or ease based on circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چودہواں اصول: مصلحت پر مبنی قول راج ہوگا
دو متعارض تصحیح شدہ اقوال میں سے اگر ہر قول کی تصحیح یکساں الفاظ سے کی گئی ہو اور تصحیح کرنے والے علماء کا رتبہ بھی برابر ہو تو اس قول کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی جس کی بنیاد مصلحت اور عرف وغیرہ پر ہو، چنانچہ الاشباہ میں بزازیہ کے حوالہ سے منقول ہے کہ مفتی اس قول پر فتوی دے گا جس میں کوئی مصلحت ہو۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ١٦٩)

مشائخ کی ترجیحات میں تطبیق سے متعلق ایک اہم فائدہ
شیخ الاسلام حضرت مفتی تقی عثمانی صاحب اپنی مایہ ناز کتاب اصول الافتاء وآدابه میں فرماتے ہیں کہ ان تمام وجوہ ترجیح کو فقہاء نے بیان کیا ہے اور وہ ایک قول کو دوسرے قول پر ترجیح دینے کے لیے ان کا استعمال کرتے رہتے ہیں، لیکن یہ سب ایسے قواعد کلیہ نہیں ہیں کہ ان پر تمام حالات میں عمل کیا جاسکے، اس لئے کہ بسا اوقات خود ان مرجحات کے ما بین تعارض ہو جاتا ہے، بایں طور کہ اسباب ترجیح میں سے کوئی سبب ایک قول کی ترجیح چاہتا ہے اور دوسرا سبب دوسرے قول کی ترجیح چاہتا ہے (مثلاً کسی قول کا ظاہر الروایہ میں ہوتا اس کی ترجیح کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اور اس کے مقابل دوسرے قول کا امام صاحب کا قول ہونا اس قول کی ترجیح کا تقاضا کرتا ہے، اب کس سبب کی بنیاد پر ان اقوال کو ترجیح دی جائے گی یہ ایک مشکل امر ہے) لہذا اس صورت میں ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ بیان کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے جس پر ہر جگہ عمل کیا جا سکے، تو ایسی مثالوں میں معاملہ مفتی کے ذوق صحیح اور ملکہ فقہیہ کے سپر د کر دیا جاتا ہے جو ان متعارض وجوہ ترجیح میں سے ایک کا انتخاب کر لیتا ہے، بسا اوقات مفتی اس امر کی ضرورت محسوس کرتے ہیں کہ سد ذرائع ہو تو و احتیاط والے قول پر فتوی دیتے ہیں اور کبھی مفتی کے سامنے ایسا مسئلہ آتا ہے جس میں ابتلاء عام ہوتا ہے تو وہ اس قول پر عمل کرتے ہیں جس میں لوگوں کے لیے سہولت ہوتی ہے۔ (اصول الافتاء و آدابه: ٢٢٦)
Fourteenth Principle: The saying based on public interest will be preferred.
If there are two conflicting corrected sayings, and each saying has been corrected with the same wording, and the rank of the correcting scholars is also equal, then preference will be given to that saying which is based on public interest and custom etc. Accordingly, in al-Ashbah it is narrated from al-Bazzaziyya that the mufti will give fatwa on the saying in which there is some public interest. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 169)

An important benefit related to reconciling the preferences of the scholars.
Shaykh al-Islam, Hadrat Mufti Taqi Usmani, in his monumental book Usul al-Ifta' wa Adabuhu, says: The jurists have explained all these grounds of preference and they use them to prefer one saying over another. But all these are not such universal rules that can be applied in all circumstances, because sometimes there is conflict among these very grounds of preference, in that one ground of preference calls for the preference of one saying and another ground calls for the preference of another saying (for example, a saying being in Zahir al-Riwayah requires its preference, while in contrast, another saying being the statement of Imam Sahib requires its preference; now on which ground these sayings will be preferred is a difficult matter). Therefore, in such a case it is not possible to state a universal rule that could be applied everywhere. So in such examples, the matter is left to the correct taste and juristic aptitude of the mufti, who selects one of these conflicting grounds of preference. Sometimes the mufti feels the need that if there is prevention of means, he gives fatwa on the saying of caution; and sometimes such a problem comes before the mufti in which there is general affliction, so he acts upon the saying in which there is ease for the people. (Usul al-Ifta' wa Adabuhu: 226)
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents the fourteenth principle of rasm al-mufti: when the mufti faces two conflicting sayings that have been equally corrected by scholars of equal rank, he should prefer the one that aligns with public interest (maslahah) and custom (urf). The text cites al-Ashbah quoting al-Bazzaziyya that the mufti gives fatwa on the saying containing maslahah. This is a crucial rule because it grounds legal preference in the objectives of the Shariah rather than just textual strength.

Then the passage adds an important nuance from Mufti Taqi Usmani: these grounds of preference are not absolute universals. They can conflict among themselves—for example, one saying might be in Zahir al-Riwayah (strong transmission) but another might be the direct statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. In such cases, no single universal rule can resolve the conflict. Instead, the matter is entrusted to the mufti's sound judgment (dhawq sahih) and his juristic aptitude (malakah fiqhiyyah). The mufti may choose the cautious saying if blocking means (sadd al-dhara'i) is needed, or the lenient saying if there is general hardship (ibtilaa' 'aam). Thus, this principle does not mechanically dictate preference but empowers the mufti with discretion guided by higher objectives.

Key Terms
مصلحت (maslahah): Public interest or benefit that is in harmony with the objectives of Shariah
مرجحات (murajjihaat): Grounds or factors that give preference to one saying over another
ذوق صحیح (dhawq sahih): Sound legal taste or judgment developed through rigorous study of fiqh
ملکہ فقہیہ (malakah fiqhiyyah): Juristic aptitude or faculty of legal reasoning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the scope of the fourteenth principle (preference for maslahah-based saying)?
A) It applies whenever a saying is based on public interest, regardless of other factors.
B) It applies when two sayings are equally corrected and the correcting scholars are of equal rank.
C) It applies only when the saying is from Imam Abu Hanifa.
D) It applies only when the saying is in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Takeaway
When two sayings are equally corrected, prefer the one based on public interest and custom; but if grounds of preference conflict, the mufti must use his sound judgment.

The Mufti’s Duty: Issuing Fatwa Only from Reliable Books
Rule requiring mufti to know book reliability before fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify reliable books in the Hanafi madhhab and apply Ibn Abidin’s rule when evaluating fatwa sources.

Core Idea
A mufti must verify a book’s reliability before issuing fatwa; later abbreviated works may be invalid.

This fourth principle of Rasm al-Mufti warns against blind fatwa-giving. Ibn Abidin declares that many short later books are unreliable, making fatwa from them void. The mufti must know the hierarchy of Hanafi sources and distinguish between books that transmit all types of sayings and those that commit to only correct, relied-upon rulings.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the two categories of Hanafi books
Identify the difference between books that indiscriminately collect all sayings (without marking correctness) and those that commit to transmitting only the relied-upon (mu'tabar) sayings and flag weak ones.
This distinction is crucial for evaluating reliability.
2
Understand Ibn Abidin’s critique
Read the passage where Ibn Abidin states that fatwas relying solely on books like Sharh al-Niqayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir are invalid due to errors and extreme brevity.
Note that he calls these books 'an enigma' (mu'mah).
3
Apply the criterion
When issuing fatwa, first determine if the book is considered mu'tabar by the later authorities. If not, cross-check the ruling with more authoritative sources (e.g., Zahir al-Riwayah or reliable compendiums).
Never rely solely on a single later work without verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھا اصول: معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا
فقہ حنفی کی بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن میں ظاہر الروایہ اور غیر ظاہر الروایہ، اقوی اور قوی صحیح اور غیر صحیح، راج اور غیر راج الغرض ہر قسم کے اقوال کو جمع کر دیا گیا ہے، ان کتابوں میں کوئی ایسی علامت بھی مذکور نہیں ہے جس سے ان اقوال کے مابین صحت و فساد اور قوت و ضعف کے اعتبار سے تمیز کیا جا سکے، اس کے برعکس بعض کتابیں ایسی بھی ہیں جن کے مصنفین نے اس بات کا التزام کیا ہے کہ وہ اپنی کتابوں میں صرف ظاہر الروایہ اور مذہب کے صحیح و معتمد قول کو نقل کرتے ہیں اور جہاں ضعیف قول لکھنے کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے تو اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ بھی کر دیتے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دیتے وقت مفتی کے لئے اس بات سے واقف ہونا انتہائی ضروری ہے کہ جس کتاب سے وہ فتوی دے رہا ہے فقہ حنفی میں اس کا مقام و مرتبہ کیا ہے؟ علماء نے اس کو معتبر کتابوں میں شمار کیا ہے یا اسے غیر معتبر قرار دیا ہے۔
علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں: میں کہتا ہوں کہ جب تم اس بات کو جان لیے ہو کہ راجح قول کی پیروی کرنا واجب ہے اور ترجیح دینے والوں کے احوال سے بھی واقف ہو چکے ہو، تو یہ بھی جان لو کہ ہمارے زمانہ کے اکثر لوگ جو متاخرین کی کتابوں میں سے محض ایک کتاب کی طرف مراجعت کر کے فتوی دیتے ہیں تو اس فتوی کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے، خاص طور سے جب وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہو، جیسے کہ علامہ قہستانی کی شرح النقایه، علامہ حصکفی کی الدرالمختار، علامہ ابن نجیم کی الاشباہ والنظائر اور ان جیسی کتابیں، کیوں کہ عبارتوں کے انتہائی مختصر ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ کتابیں ایک معمہ بن گئی ہیں، نیز ان کتابوں میں بہت سے مقامات پر عبارت نقل کرنے میں غلطی بھی ہوئی ہے، (بعض مسائل میں) مرجوح قول کو راجح قرار دیا گیا ہے، بلکہ ان اقوال کو بھی راج قرار دیا گیا ہے جس کا ہمارے مذہب کے ائمہ میں سے کوئی بھی قائل نہیں ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی ۵۴۰)
Fourth Principle: Giving fatwa from reliable books.
In Hanafi fiqh, some books are such that they collect all kinds of sayings: Zahir al-Riwayah and non-Zahir al-Riwayah, stronger and strong, correct and incorrect, preferred and non-preferred, etc. In these books, there is no such sign mentioned by which one can distinguish between these sayings in terms of correctness and corruption, strength and weakness. On the contrary, there are some books whose authors have committed themselves to transmit only Zahir al-Riwayah and the correct, relied-upon saying of the madhhab, and where there is a need to write a weak saying, they also point out its weakness. Therefore, when giving fatwa, it is extremely necessary for the mufti to know what the rank and position of the book from which he is giving fatwa is in Hanafi fiqh: have the scholars considered it among the reliable books or have they declared it unreliable?
Allamah Ibn Abidin Shami says: I say that when you have come to know that following the preferred (rajih) saying is obligatory, and you have become familiar with the conditions of those who prefer, then also know that most people of our time who give fatwa by merely referring to a single book from among the books of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) — that fatwa has no validity, especially when that book is unreliable, such as Allamah Qahistani's Sharh al-Niqayah, Allamah Haskafi's al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Allamah Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, and books like them, because due to the extreme brevity of the expressions, these books have become an enigma. Also, in many places in these books, there have been errors in quoting expressions; in some issues, the less preferred (marjuh) saying has been declared preferred (rajih); rather, even such sayings have been declared preferred which none of the imams of our madhhab held. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 540)
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth principle: the mufti must issue fatwa from reliable books. It first distinguishes between two categories of Hanafi books: (1) those that indiscriminately collect all types of sayings without marking which is authentic, and (2) those that restrict themselves to transmitting only the relied-upon sayings of the madhhab and clearly note when a weak saying is included. The mufti must know the status of the book he uses.

Then comes a strong warning from Allamah Ibn Abidin. He declares that fatwas based solely on books of the later scholars (like Sharh al-Niqayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir) are invalid if those books are considered unreliable. The reason: these books, due to extreme brevity, have become 'an enigma' (mu'mah). They contain errors in quotation, have elevated marjuh (weak) sayings to rajih (strong), and even include opinions not held by any Hanafi imam. Therefore, a mufti must not blindly rely on such books; he must have sufficient knowledge of the madhhab to discern authentic rulings from the original sources (Zahir al-Riwayah) or from later reliable compilations that properly indicate the strength of each saying.

Key Terms
معتبر کتابیں (mu'tabar kutub): Books that are considered reliable in the Hanafi madhhab, typically those that transmit only the correct and relied-upon sayings
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the most authoritative source of Hanafi rulings
مرجوح (marjuh): The less preferred or weaker opinion within the madhhab
راجح (rajih): The preferred or stronger opinion within the madhhab

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin, what is the status of a fatwa that is based solely on a book like Sharh al-Niqayah or al-Durr al-Mukhtar?
A) It is valid as long as the mufti understands the book.
B) It is valid because these books are widely used.
C) It has no validity and is considered invalid.
D) It is valid only if the book is endorsed by a living scholar.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must know the reliability of the books he uses; fatwa from unreliable later books is invalid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Fourth Principle: Giving Fatwa from Reliable Books
Rasm al-mufti rule on source reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the criteria for reliable Hanafi fatwa books and apply the principle that a mufti must verify the authority of his source before issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
Fatwa must be based on mu'tamad opinions from reliable books, not on any work indiscriminately.

This lesson presents the fourth principle of fatwa-giving according to Hanafi usul al-iftaa. It distinguishes between books that compile all opinions without discrimination and those that transmit only the relied-upon (mu'tamad) position. The mufti must know the status of the book he uses. A warning from Ibn Abidin cautions against relying on later works that may contain errors or present weak opinions as strong. This principle ensures that fatwas are sound and consistent with the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two categories of Hanafi books
Identify that some books contain a mix of Zahir al-Riwayah and non-Zahir al-Riwayah, strong and weak opinions, without marking them. Others commit to transmitting only the reliable (mu'tamad) opinions and indicate weakness when necessary.
This distinction is crucial for selecting a valid source.
2
Recognize the mufti's obligation
A mufti must know the rank and reliability of the book he uses. He should not issue fatwa from any book without knowing its status in the tradition.
Ibn Abidin emphasizes that fatwa from unreliable books has no validity.
3
Analyze Ibn Abidin's warning
Ibn Abidin criticizes reliance on books like Sharh al-Nuqayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair because their brevity leads to errors and they sometimes present weak (marjuh) opinions as strong (rajih), even ones not held by any Hanafi imam.
This warning applies specifically to those who use a single later work without verification.
4
Apply the principle
When preparing a fatwa, first verify the source book: is it considered mu'tamad? Does it only contain Zahir al-Riwayah? Have later scholars relied on it? Only then proceed to extract the ruling.
Consult the hierarchy of Hanafi texts: Zahir al-Riwayah → Nawadir → Fatawa Mutakhkhirin.

چوتھا اصول معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا شن عقود رسم المفى ا فقہ حنفی کی بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن میں ظاہر الروایہ اور غیر ظاہر الروایہ، اقوی اور قوی صحیح اور غیر صحیح، راج اور غیر راج الغرض ہر قسم کے اقوال کو جمع کر دیا گیا ہے، ان کتابوں میں کوئی ایسی علامت بھی مذکور نہیں ہے جس سے ان اقوال کے مابین صحت و فساد اور قوت و ضعف کے اعتبار سے تمیز کیا جا سکے، اس کے برعکس بعض کتابیں ایسی بھی ہیں جن کے مصنفین نے اس بات کا التزام کیا ہے کہ وہ اپنی کتابوں میں صرف ظاہر الروایہ اور مذہب کے صحیح و معتمد قول کو نقل کرتے ہیں اور جہاں ضعیف قول لکھنے کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے تو اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ بھی کر دیتے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دیتے وقت مفتی کے لئے اس بات سے واقف ہونا انتہائی ضروری ہے کہ جس کتاب سے وہ فتوی دے رہا ہے فقہ حنفی میں اس کا مقام و مرتبہ کیا ہے؟ علماء نے اس کو معتبر کتابوں میں شمار کیا ہے یا اسے غیر معتبر قرار دیا ہے۔ علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں: میں کہتا ہوں کہ جب تم اس بات کو جان لیے ہو کہ راجح قول کی پیروی کرنا واجب ہے اور ترجیح دینے والوں کے احوال سے بھی واقف ہو چکے ہو، تو یہ بھی جان لو کہ ہمارے زمانہ کے اکثر لوگ جو متاخرین کی کتابوں میں سے محض ایک کتاب کی طرف مراجعت کر کے فتوی دید یتے ہیں تو اس فتوی کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے، خاص طور سے جب وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہو، جیسے کہ علامہ قہستانی کی شرح النقایه ،علامہ حصکفی کی الدرالمختار ،علامہ ابن نجیم کی الاشباہ والنظائر اور ان جیسی کتابیں، کیوں کہ عبارتوں کے انتہائی مختصر ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ کتابیں ایک معمہ بن گئی ہیں، نیز ان کتابوں میں بہت سے مقامات پر عبارت نقل کرنے میں غلطی بھی ہوئی ہے، ( بعض مسائل میں ) مرجوح قول کو راجح قرار دیا گیا ہے، بلکہ ان اقوال کو بھی راج قرار دیا گیا ہے جس کا ہمارے مذہب کے ائمہ میں سے کوئی بھی قائل نہیں ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی ۵۴۰)
Fourth principle: Giving fatwa from reliable books. Some books of Hanafi fiqh contain all kinds of statements: Zahir al-Riwayah and non-Zahir al-Riwayah, stronger and strong, correct and incorrect, preferred and non-preferred. In these books there is no indication to distinguish between them in terms of soundness and weakness or strength and weakness. On the contrary, there are some books whose authors have committed to only transmit the Zahir al-Riwayah and the correct and reliable statement of the madhhab, and where it is necessary to write a weak statement, they also indicate its weakness. Therefore, it is extremely necessary for a mufti when giving a fatwa to know what rank and status the book he is relying on has in Hanafi fiqh: do scholars count it among reliable books or have they declared it unreliable? Allamah Ibn Abidin Shami says: I say that when you know that it is obligatory to follow the preferred (rajih) opinion and you are aware of the states of those who give preference, then also know that in our time most people who give fatwa by referring to only one book among the later works have no validity in their fatwa, especially when that book is unreliable, such as Allamah Quhistani's Sharh al-Nuqayah, Allamah Haskafi's al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Allamah Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, and similar books. Because due to extreme brevity of expressions, these books have become enigmatic, and also in these books in many places there is error in transmitting expressions, and in some issues the preponderated opinion is declared as preponderant, rather even those opinions are declared preponderant which none of the Imams of our madhhab holds. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, 540)
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth principle of fatwa-giving, which deals with the necessity of using reliable books. The author explains that there are two categories of Hanafi fiqh books: those that compile all types of opinions without distinguishing between strong and weak, and those that only contain the relied-upon (mu'tamad) opinions and indicate weakness where present. A mufti must know the status of the book he uses. Then a quote from Ibn Abidin warns against blindly relying on any single later work, especially those like Sharh al-Nuqayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, because their extreme brevity leads to errors and sometimes they present weak opinions as strong. This establishes the rule that a mufti should only issue fatwas from books that are known to be reliable and contain the correct Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted opinions from Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani that are well-known and reliable.
معتمد قول (mu'tamad qaw): The relied-upon opinion in the Hanafi madhhab that is considered authoritative for fatwa.
مرجوح قول (marjuh qaw): A preponderated opinion that is weaker and not relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fourth principle, what is the main reason that books like Sharh al-Nuqayah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar are considered unreliable for direct fatwa?
A) They are too old and outdated.
B) Their extreme brevity leads to errors and they may present weak opinions as strong.
C) They are not written by Hanafi scholars.
D) They contain only minority opinions.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must verify the reliability of his source book and only issue fatwa from works that contain the mu'tamad (relied-upon) opinions of the Hanafi madhhab.

The Fifth Principle: When an Unreliable Book Becomes Reliable
A principle of mufti methodology with four remedial scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four scenarios where a previously unreliable Hanafi fiqh book becomes acceptable for fatwa, and apply them to new cases.

Core Idea
An unreliable book regains authority when its specific cause of unreliability is removed.

This lesson explains the fifth principle of Rasm al-Mufti, which allows fatwa from a book previously considered unreliable, provided the underlying cause has ceased. The passage gives four distinct scenarios: rarity resolved, author's status clarified, excessive brevity compensated by detail on a particular issue, and finding the original source. Understanding this principle is essential for muftis to avoid discarding valid rulings unnecessarily.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of unreliability
From the passage, the main causes are rarity, unknown author, excessive brevity, and unknown source. Determine which cause applies to the book in question.
The cause must be explicit; not every defect can be remedied.
2
Verify that the cause has ceased
Check if the condition that made the book unreliable is no longer present. For rarity, a verified copy must be found. For unknown author, credible information about the author's scholarliness must emerge.
Any lingering doubt may prevent acceptance.
3
Confirm madhhab alignment or source traceability
Even if the cause is removed, the ruling must not contradict the established Hanafi position, or the original source (makhdh) of the ruling must be traceable to a reliable foundation.
This step is implicit in the passage and is emphasized by the quotes.

پانچواں اصول غیر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا شي عقود رسم المفر جس کتاب کو کسی سبب اور علت کی بنیاد پر غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں وہ علت ختم ہو جائے تو پھر اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، مثلا جس کتاب کو اس کے نایاب ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں اس کا تصیح اور ثابت نسخہ مل جائے تو اب وہ کتاب معتبر ہو جائے گی اور اس سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا، اسی طرح جس کتاب کو اس کے مصنف کے احوال مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں اس مصنف کی علمی حالت سے لوگ آشنا ہو جائیں تو اب ان کی کتاب سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا ، اسی طرح جن کتابوں کو غیر معمولی اختصار کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور اسی کتاب میں کسی مسئلہ کی بابت خوب تفصیل موجود ہو تو صرف اس مسئلہ کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے وہ کتاب معتبر ہوگی، نیز غیر معتبر کتابوں کا مصدر وماخذ مل جائے تو اس سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا۔ شیخ صالح الجنینی فرماتے ہیں: بر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب کہ اس کے مصدر ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اس کا علم ہو جائے اور اس کے ماخذ ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو اخذ کیا گیا ہے اس سے واقفیت ہو جائے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٥٦) علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدائمی لکھنوی فرماتے ہیں: غیر معتبر کتابوں میں جو مسائل مذکور ہیں اگر وہ معتبر فقہی کتابوں کے موافق ہوں تو ان پر عمل کریں گے ورنہ انھیں ترک کر دیں گے، نیز ان مسائل کا اگر ما خذمل جائے تو ان پر عمل کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر وہ علت ختم ہو جائے جس کی وجہ سے وہ
Fifth principle: Giving fatwa from unreliable books. A book which is declared unreliable due to some cause that later ceases, then there is no harm in giving fatwa from it. For example, a book declared unreliable due to its rarity, but later a corrected and established copy is found, then that book becomes reliable and giving fatwa from it is permissible. Similarly, a book declared unreliable because the circumstances of its author are unknown, but later people become acquainted with the author's scholarly state, then giving fatwa from his book becomes permissible. Similarly, books declared unreliable due to excessive brevity, but in that same book there is detailed treatment of a particular issue, then only with respect to that issue the book becomes reliable. Also, if the source and origin of an unreliable book is found, then giving fatwa from it is permissible. Shaykh Salih al-Junayni says: Giving fatwa from an unreliable book is permissible when its source (i.e., the book from which the issue was narrated) is known, and its origin (i.e., the book from which the issue was derived) is known. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, 56) Allamah Abu al-Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi says: The issues mentioned in unreliable books, if they conform to reliable fiqh books, we will act upon them; otherwise we will abandon them. Also, if the origin of these issues is found, there is no harm in acting upon them. Similarly, if the cause ceases due to which (the book was declared unreliable)...
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth principle, which gives exceptions to the rule of not using unreliable books. It lists several scenarios where an originally unreliable book becomes acceptable for fatwa: (1) the book was rare but a verified copy is found; (2) the author's scholarly standing was unknown but later becomes known; (3) the book is generally concise but provides detailed explanation for a particular issue; (4) the original source of the book's content is identified. The passage then quotes Shaykh Salih al-Junayni, who emphasizes that knowledge of the source (musdar) and origin (makhdh) of the issues makes it permissible to give fatwa from an otherwise unreliable book. Finally, Allamah Lakhnawi adds that if the rulings in an unreliable book agree with reliable fiqh books, they can be acted upon; otherwise, they are abandoned. The text ends abruptly, but the principle is clear.

Key Terms
علت (illah): The cause or reason that led to the book being declared unreliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the scenarios mentioned in the passage that allows an unreliable book to be used?
A) The book was rare, and a verified copy is found.
B) The author's scholarly status was unknown but later becomes known.
C) The book contains a fatwa from the Prophet's Companions.
D) The original source (makhdh) of the book's rulings is found.

Key Takeaway
The authority of a book in fatwa is not permanent; it can be reevaluated when the cause of its unreliability is removed.

Scholarly Conditions for Using Previously Unreliable Books
Scholarly conditions for using an unreliable book: knowledge of source/origin and conformity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the additional conditions set by Shaykh al-Junayni and Allamah al-Lakhnawi for using a previously unreliable book, and identify the practical implications of each.

Core Idea
Knowing the source (musdar) and origin (makhdh) of a ruling, or confirming its conformity with reliable books, legitimizes its use.

In this lesson, we examine two scholarly elaborations on the fifth principle. Shaykh Salih al-Junayni requires knowledge of the immediate source (musdar) and ultimate origin (makhdh) of the issues in the unreliable book. Allamah al-Lakhnawi adds that if the rulings in such a book conform to reliable Hanafi fiqh works, they may be acted upon; otherwise, they are to be abandoned. These conditions guard against relying on anomalous or incorrect rulings.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish musdar from makhdh
Musdar is the immediate book narrating the ruling; makhdh is the original authority from which it is derived. Both must be known for the book to be used.
This distinction ensures traceability of the ruling.
2
Apply the conformity test
If the ruling in the unreliable book matches a ruling in a reliable Hanafi source like al-Hidayah or al-Quduri, it can be accepted. If it conflicts, it must be abandoned.
This test is straightforward but requires knowledge of reliable sources.
3
Recognize the scope of exception
Both scholars emphasize that the exception does not give blanket permission; the ruling must be traceable or conforming.
The mufti must not use an unreliable book as a primary source without verification.

Key Terms
مصدر (musdar): The immediate source from which the issue is narrated or transmitted.
ماخذ (makhdh): The original source or authority from which the issue is ultimately derived.
