Fatwa from Non-Reliable Books: When Removal of the Cause Restores Reliability
Methodological rule on book reliability in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria for evaluating book reliability in fatwa, specifically identifying when a non-reliable book becomes acceptable for fatwa due to removal of its cause or knowledge of its source.

Core Idea
A book becomes reliable for fatwa when the specific cause of its unreliability is removed or its source is known.

This passage establishes a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-iftaa: a book's unreliability is not permanent; it depends on a removable cause (illah). When that cause is remedied, the book can be used. This lesson walks through the conditions, examples, and the first two causes of unreliability, providing a critical framework for every mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Read the opening sentence: a book declared non-reliable due to a cause becomes reliable when that cause is removed. This is the overarching rule.
The cause ('illah) is key; it can be rarity, unknown author, extreme brevity, etc.
2
Examine the Three Examples of Cause Removal
The text gives three examples: (1) rarity – when an authentic copy is found; (2) unknown author – when his scholarly status becomes known; (3) extreme brevity – but if a specific issue is detailed, that issue alone is reliable.
Each example shows a specific illah and its remedy.
3
Understand the Additional Condition: Source and Origin
The passage adds that if the immediate source (masdar) and origin (ma'khadh) of an issue in a non-reliable book are identified, fatwa from that book becomes permissible.
This provides a secondary route to reliability.
4
List the First Two Causes of Unreliability
The text lists ten causes; only the first two are given in this chunk: (1) unknown author, with examples like Sharh al-Kanz by Masakin; (2) book containing weak narrations, with examples like Quniyat al-Munyah.
These causes are specific defects that make a book non-reliable by default.
5
Reflect on the Practical Implication for a Mufti
A mufti must evaluate the cause of a book's unreliability and check if that cause has been removed before using the book for fatwa.
This principle prevents both undue rejection and careless acceptance of sources.

غیر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا
شي عقود رسم المفر
جس کتاب کو کسی سبب اور علت کی بنیاد پر غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں وہ علت ختم ہو جائے تو پھر اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، مثلا جس کتاب کو اس کے نایاب ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں اس کا تصیح اور ثابت نسخہ مل جائے تو اب وہ کتاب معتبر ہو جائے گی اور اس سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا، اسی طرح جس کتاب کو اس کے مصنف کے احوال مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور بعد میں اس مصنف کی علمی حالت سے لوگ آشنا ہو جائیں تو اب ان کی کتاب سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا ، اسی طرح جن کتابوں کو غیر معمولی اختصار کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جائے اور اسی کتاب میں کسی مسئلہ کی بابت خوب تفصیل موجود ہو تو صرف اس مسئلہ کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے وہ کتاب معتبر ہوگی، نیز غیر معتبر کتابوں کا مصدر وماخذ مل جائے تو اس سے فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا۔ شیخ صالح الجنینی فرماتے ہیں:
بر معتبر کتابوں سے فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب کہ اس کے مصدر ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اس کا علم ہو جائے اور اس کے ماخذ ( یعنی جس کتاب سے اس مسئلہ کو اخذ کیا گیا ہے اس سے واقفیت ہو جائے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٥٦)
علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدائمی لکھنوی فرماتے ہیں: غیر معتبر کتابوں میں جو مسائل مذکور ہیں اگر وہ معتبر فقہی کتابوں کے موافق ہوں تو ان پر عمل کریں گے ورنہ انھیں ترک کر دیں گے، نیز ان مسائل کا اگر ما خذمل جائے تو ان پر عمل کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر وہ علت ختم ہو جائے جس کی وجہ سے وہ
من المفتى فى حل مباد
شن عقود رسم المفى
کتاب غیر معتبر ہوئی تھی تو اب وہ کتاب معتبر ہو جائے گی۔(عمدة الرعايه: ٦٣/١) کتابوں کے غیر معتبر ہونے کے دس (۱۰) اسباب
فقہ حنفی میں کسی کتاب کے غیر معتبر ہونے کے درج ذیل اسباب ہوتے ہیں: پہلا سبب : مؤلف کا مجہول ہونا
بعض کتابوں کو ان کے مصنفین کے اسماء کے مجہول ہونے اور ان کی علمی لیاقت کے غیر معروف ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر معتبر قرار دیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ ما مسکین کی شرح الکنز ، علامہ قہستانی کی جامع الرموز فی شرح النقایہ اور قاضی جکن کی خزانة الروايات غیر معتبر کتابیں ہیں، کیوں کہ ان تینوں مصنفین کا علمی مقام مشہور و معروف نہیں ہے۔
حاشيه رسم المفتی : ٥٥ ، عمدة الرعايه : ٤٩ ، المذهب الحنفي: ٢٣٥/١)
:دوسرا سب کتاب کا ضعیف روایات پر مشتمل ہونا
بعض مصنفین ایسے ہیں جن کے علمی مراتب سے سبھی حضرات واقف ہیں، لیکن وہ اپنی کتابوں میں صحیح اقوال لکھنے کا التزام نہیں کرتے ہیں، بلکہ ہر طرح کی روایات واقوال کو جمع کر دیتے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دینے کے حق میں ان کی کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی ، چنانچہ علامہ زاہدی کی قنية المنيه ، علامہ ابوبکر بن على الحداد كي السراج الوهاج الموضح لكل طالب و محتاج اور علامہ فضل اللہ حمد بن ایوب صوفی کی الفتاوى الصوفيه غير معتبر کتابیں ہیں، کیوں کہ ان کتابوں میں بہت سے مقامات پر ضعیف اقوال نقل کئے گئے ہیں
اور ان کے ضعف کی جانب اشارہ بھی نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔
اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ۲۱۰ ، المصباح للراشدي : ٤٥٥ ، المذهب الحنفي: ۲۲۸/۱)
تیسرا سبب: عبارت کا انتہائی مختصر ہونا
بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن کی عبارتیں اس قدر مختصر ہیں کہ بسا اوقات مفتی کے لئے
Fifth Principle: Giving Fatwa from Non-Reliable Books
A book that has been declared non-reliable due to some cause and reason, and later that cause is removed, then there is no harm in giving fatwa from it. For example, a book declared non-reliable due to its rarity, and later a corrected and authentic copy is found, then that book becomes reliable and giving fatwa from it is permissible. Similarly, a book declared non-reliable because the author's circumstances are unknown, and later people become acquainted with the author's scholarly condition, then giving fatwa from his book is permissible. Similarly, books declared non-reliable due to extreme brevity, but within that book there is detailed discussion on a particular issue, then only that issue, when attributed, makes the book reliable. Also, if the source (masdar) and origin (ma'khadh) of non-reliable books are found, then giving fatwa from them is permissible. Shaykh Salih al-Jinini says: Giving fatwa from non-reliable books is permissible when its source (i.e., the book from which the issue was narrated) is known and its origin (i.e., the book from which the issue was derived) is recognized. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 56)
Allamah Abu al-Hasanat 'Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi says: The issues mentioned in non-reliable books, if they agree with reliable fiqh books, we will act upon them; otherwise we will abandon them. Also, if the origin of these issues is found, there is no harm in acting upon them. Similarly, if the cause due to which the book was declared non-reliable is removed, then that book becomes reliable. ('Umdat al-Ri'ayah: 1/63)
Ten Causes for Books Being Non-Reliable
In Hanafi fiqh, a book's non-reliability has the following causes:
First Cause: The Author Being Unknown
Some books are declared non-reliable due to the unknown names of their authors and their unrecognized scholarly competence. For example, Sharh al-Kanz by Masakin, Jami' al-Rumuz fi Sharh al-Nuqayah by Allamah Quhistani, and Khizanat al-Riwayat by Qadi Jakan are non-reliable books because the scholarly standing of these three authors is not well-known. (Hashiyah Rasm al-Mufti: 55, 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah: 49, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/235)
Second Cause: The Book Containing Weak Narrations
Some authors are those whose scholarly ranks are known to everyone, but they do not commit to writing correct statements in their books; rather, they collect all kinds of narrations and statements. Therefore, their books will be non-reliable for issuing fatwa. For instance, Quniyat al-Munyah by Allamah Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj al-Muwaddih li Kulli Talib wa Muhtaj by Allamah Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali al-Haddad, and al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah by Allamah Fadlallah Hamad ibn Ayyub al-Sufi are non-reliable books because weak statements are transmitted in many places in these books without indicating their weakness. (Usul al-Ifta' al-'Uthmani: 210, al-Misbah al-Rashidi: 455, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/228)
Third Cause: Extremely Concise Wording
Some books are those whose expressions are so brief that sometimes for the mufti...
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a methodological ruling (rasm al-mufti) concerning when a book that has been deemed 'non-reliable' (ghayr mu'tabar) can be used for fatwa. The author first lays down a general principle: if the specific cause (illah) that led to the book being considered unreliable is removed, then the book becomes reliable and fatwa from it is permissible. He provides three examples: (1) a book deemed unreliable due to rarity (nayab) — if an authentic copy is found, it becomes reliable; (2) a book deemed unreliable because the author is unknown — if the author's scholarly status becomes known, it becomes reliable; (3) a book deemed unreliable due to extreme brevity — but if it contains a detailed discussion on a particular issue, that issue alone can be relied upon. Additionally, if the original source (masdar) from which the book draws is identified, the book may be used. The author then quotes Shaykh Salih al-Jinini and Allamah al-Lakhnawi, who confirm these points and add that if a non-reliable book's contents agree with reliable fiqh works, they may be acted upon. The passage then lists the ten causes of a book's unreliability, but only the first two are fully given: (1) unknown author, with examples of specific books (e.g., Sharh al-Kanz by Masakin); (2) book containing weak narrations, with examples (e.g., Quniyat al-Munyah). The third cause (extremely concise wording) is introduced but the text cuts off. The passage thus provides a critical framework for evaluating the authority of secondary fiqh sources.

Key Terms
غیر معتبر کتاب (ghayr mu'tabar kitab): A book that is not accepted as a reliable source for issuing fatwa due to specific defects.
علت (illah): The specific cause or reason that makes a book non-reliable; once removed, the book becomes reliable.
مصدر (masdar): The original source from which an issue in a non-reliable book is narrated; knowing it allows fatwa.
مؤلف مجہول (mu'allif majhul): An author whose name or scholarly competence is unknown, causing his book to be non-reliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition can a book that was declared non-reliable due to the author being unknown become reliable?
A) If the author's name becomes known.
B) If the author's scholarly status becomes known.
C) If the book is verified by another known author.
D) If the book's rarity is resolved.

Key Takeaway
The unreliability of a book in Hanafi usul al-iftaa is conditional on a removable cause; once that cause is removed, the book becomes reliable for fatwa.

First Cause of Book Unreliability: Author's Obscurity
Introduces ten causes and details the first cause: unknown author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first cause of book unreliability in Hanafi ifta and identify examples of books considered unreliable due to obscure authorship.

Core Idea
A book whose author is unknown is unreliable for fatwa regardless of its content.

In Hanafi ifta, a mufti must distinguish reliable from unreliable sources. This lesson presents the first of ten causes: when the author's identity and scholarly competence are obscure, his work cannot be relied upon. We examine why and see concrete examples from the tradition.

Guided Path
1
State the first cause
The first cause of a book being non-reliable is the author being unknown (majhool). This means the author's name and scholarly competence are not well-known in the tradition.
This is a foundational principle of rasm al-mufti.
2
Understand the criterion
Obscurity implies that the author's identity is not established among Hanafi scholars OR his competence is unrecognized. Even if the book appears useful, it carries no authority for fatwa.
3
Identify the examples
The text names three books: Sharh al-Kanz by Ma Miskin, Jami' al-Rumuz by al-Qahistani, and Khazanat al-Riwayat by Qadi Jakan. Their authors' scholarly status is not well-known.
These are not authoritative sources for fatwa.
4
Grasp the implication
A mufti must verify the author's reliability before using a book. This protects the fatwa process from weak or unauthentic rulings.

The text gives examples of specific books whose authors are obscure, thus their works are not relied upon for fatwa. This is a rasm al-mufti principle: a book's authority depends on the author's known competence.

Key Terms
مؤلف کا مجہول ہونا (mu'allif ka majhool hona): The author's identity and scholarly competence are unknown or unrecognized.

Books with Weak Narrations Without Indication Are Unreliable
Details the second cause of book unreliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of books are unreliable for fatwa due to containing weak narrations without indication and apply this rule to assess a book's authority.

Core Idea
A book mixing weak narrations without distinction is unreliable for fatwa, regardless of the author's rank.

In this lesson, we examine the second cause that renders a book unreliable for issuing fatwa. Even if an author is well-known, if his work indiscriminately includes weak narrations without indicating their weakness, the mufti cannot rely on it. We will learn specific examples and the underlying principle that protects the integrity of fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Cause
Recognize that the second cause of book unreliability is the inclusion of weak narrations (da'if riwayat) without any indication of their weakness. This applies even to respected authors.
The cause is about the book's content, not the author's status.
2
Understand the Condition
The critical condition is that weak narrations are mixed with sound ones without distinction. If the author had indicated which narrations are weak, the book might be usable, but without that, it is unreliable.
This condition is key: lack of distinction makes the book useless for fatwa.
3
Recognize the Examples
Three specific books are given as examples: Qunyah al-Munyah by al-Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj by al-Haddad, and al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah by al-Sufi. These books are known to contain weak narrations without warning.
These are not just theoretical; they are real books that muftis should avoid.
4
Apply the Rule to Other Books
When evaluating any book for fatwa, check whether the author critically selects narrations or merely compiles everything. If the latter, the book is unreliable unless you can independently verify each narration.
This principle helps you assess any book, not just those listed.

دوسرا سبب: کتاب کا ضعیف روایات پر مشتمل ہونا
بعض مصنفین ایسے ہیں جن کے علمی مراتب سے سبھی حضرات واقف ہیں، لیکن وہ اپنی کتابوں میں صحیح اقوال لکھنے کا التزام نہیں کرتے، بلکہ ہر طرح کی روایات واقوال کو جمع کر دیتے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دینے کے حق میں ان کی کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی، چنانچہ علامہ زاہدی کی قنية المنيه، علامہ ابوبکر بن على الحداد كي السراج الوهاج الموضح لكل طالب و محتاج اور علامہ فضل اللہ حمد بن ایوب صوفی کی الفتاوى الصوفيه غير معتبر کتابیں ہیں، کیوں کہ ان کتابوں میں بہت سے مقامات پر ضعیف اقوال نقل کئے گئے ہیں اور ان کے ضعف کی جانب اشارہ بھی نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔
(اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ۲۱۰، المصباح للراشدي: ٤٥٥، المذهب الحنفي: ۲۲۸/۱)
Second cause: The book containing weak narrations. Some authors are well-known for their scholarly rank, but they do not commit to writing only correct statements; rather, they collect all kinds of narrations and statements. Therefore, their books are non-reliable for fatwa. For example, Qunyah al-Munyah by 'Allamah al-Zahidi, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj al-Muwaddih li Kulli Talib wa Muhtaj by 'Allamah Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali al-Haddad, and al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah by 'Allamah Fadl Allah Hamd ibn Ayyub al-Sufi are non-reliable books because in many places they quote weak statements without indicating their weakness. (Usul al-Ifta' al-'Uthmani: 210, al-Misbah li al-Rashidi: 455, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/228)
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is the second cause of book unreliability. Even if an author is known and respected, if his book mixes weak narrations with sound ones without distinguishing, it is not reliable for fatwa. The examples given are books that indiscriminately compile narrations, making it impossible to know which statements are authoritative.

Key Terms
ضعیف روایات (da'if riwayat): Narrations or statements that are not authentic according to hadith or fiqh standards, often included without critical assessment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Qunyah al-Munyah
C) al-Durr al-Mukhtar
D) Khazanat al-Riwayat

Key Takeaway
A book that mixes weak narrations without distinction is unreliable for fatwa, regardless of the author's fame.

Fatwa from Extremely Brief Books: When is it Permissible?
Presents the third cause with examples and an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a book with extremely brief expression can be used as a source for fatwa according to Hanafi usul al-iftaa.

Core Idea
A book with extremely brief expression is unreliable unless the mufti fully understands it without any doubt.

Among the causes that render a book unreliable for fatwa is extremely brief and unclear expression. The classical Hanafi texts give examples of famous commentaries that are so condensed that they may confuse a mufti. However, the rule is not absolute: if the mufti thoroughly comprehends the expression, he may rely on it. This principle balances the need for clarity with the practical reality that concise works can still be valuable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognize that the third cause is 'ibarat ka intihai mukhtasar hona' – the expression being extremely brief.
This is one of several causes that make a book non-reliable.
2
State the general rule
Books with extremely brief expressions are considered non-reliable (ghayr mu'tabar) because understanding them is difficult.
Examples: al-Nahr al-Fa'iq, Ramz al-Haqa'iq, al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
3
Apply the exception
The rule has an exception: if the mufti fully understands the expression and no doubt remains, giving fatwa from such a book is permissible.
This exception prevents wholesale rejection of concise but accurate works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیسرا سبب: عبارت کا انتہائی مختصر ہونا
بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن کی عبارتیں اس قدر مختصر ہیں کہ بسا اوقات مفتی کے لئے ان عبارتوں کا سمجھنا انتہائی مشکل امر ہو جاتا ہے اور عبارات کے صحیح مفاہیم تک ان کی رسائی نہیں ہو پاتی ہے، لہذا ایسی کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی، چنانچہ علامہ عمربن نجیم کی النهر الفائق شرح كنز الدقائق، علامہ بدرالدین عینی کی رمز الحقائق شرح کنز الدقائق اور علامہ حصلفى كى الدر المختار شرح تنویر الابصار غیر معتبر کتابیں ہیں، اس لیے کہ ان کتابوں کی عبارتیں انتہائی مختصر اور کافی پیچیدہ ہیں، لہذا ان کتابوں سے فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہو گا جب عبارت مکمل طور پر سمجھ میں آجائے اور کسی قسم کا خلجان باقی نہ رہے۔
(اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ٢١٤، المصباح للراشدي: ٤٦٠، المذهب الحنفى: ٢٢٦/١)
Third cause: The expression being extremely brief. Some books have expressions so brief that at times it becomes extremely difficult for a mufti to understand them and he cannot reach the correct meanings of the expressions. Therefore, such books are non-reliable. For example, al-Nahr al-Fa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq by 'Allamah 'Umar ibn Nujaym, Ramz al-Haqa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq by 'Allamah Badr al-Din al-'Ayni, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar Sharh Tanwir al-Absar by 'Allamah al-Haskafi are non-reliable books because their expressions are extremely brief and quite complex. Therefore, giving fatwa from these books is permissible only when the expression is fully understood and no doubt remains. (Usul al-Ifta' al-'Uthmani: 214, al-Misbah li al-Rashidi: 460, al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/226)
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This cause addresses books that are so concise that they cause confusion. The examples are well-known commentaries that are very brief. The text makes an exception: if the mufti fully understands the expression and has no doubt, he may use it. This principle balances the need for clarity with the existence of brief but accurate texts.

Key Terms
عبارت کا انتہائی مختصر ہونا (ibarat ka intihai mukhtasar hona): The expression is so brief and condensed that it hinders proper understanding of the legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, giving fatwa from a book with extremely brief expression is allowed when:
A) The mufti is a scholar
B) The expression is fully understood and no doubt remains
C) The book is by a known author
D) The book contains only sound narrations

Key Takeaway
Extremely brief books are unreliable unless the mufti achieves full comprehension without any doubt.

Fifth Cause: Author Declared Weak
Details the fifth cause and its exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of an author's reliability in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and apply the exception when a higher-ranking jurist certifies him.

Core Idea
An author personally declared weak renders his corpus unreliable — unless a greater jurist overrides that judgment.

In the Hanafi tradition, the reliability of a legal text is tied to the personal standing of its author. This lesson examines the fifth cause: when a jurist declares an author weak due to transmitting weak narrations, his entire book becomes suspect. But there is a crucial nuance: if a higher-ranked jurist affirms his reliability, the book is reinstated. We will unpack this principle and see how it applies in practice through the example of 'Allamah al-Zahidi and Ibn 'Abidin's critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
State the fifth cause: the author being declared weak by a jurist. Recognize that this is one of the causes that can undermine a book's reliability in the Hanafi school.
This cause focuses on the author's personal credibility, not the content itself.
2
Understand the consequence
The immediate consequence is that all books of that author are deemed non-reliable (ghayr mu'tabar). This is a blanket ruling based on the author's weakness.
3
Note the exception
If another jurist of higher scholarly rank declares the author reliable, the author's books become reliable again. The principle is that the opinion of the higher-ranking jurist prevails.
This exception prevents hasty rejection; it respects the hierarchy of scholarly authority.
4
Apply the example
Analyze Ibn 'Abidin's statement on 'Allamah al-Zahidi. Ibn 'Abidin says al-Zahidi transmits weak narrations, so in matters he alone mentions, he is not followed. But note: this does not mean al-Zahidi's entire corpus is always rejected; only unique reports lacking corroboration are affected.
The example of al-Zahidi's Qunyah al-Munyah illustrates the rule in action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پانچواں سبب: مؤلف کا ضعیف ہونا
جس مصنف کو کوئی فقیہ کسی سبب کی بنیاد پر ضعیف قراردیں تو ان کی تمام کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی لیکن اگر کسی دوسرے فقیہ نے ان کو معتبر مصنف قرار دیا ہو اور وہ دوسرا فقیہ علمی لحاظ سے پہلے سے بلند تر ہو تو پھر ان کی کتاب معتبر ہوگی، مثلا علامہ زاہدی کے بارے میں علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں کہ زاہدی ضعیف روایات کو نقل کرتے ہیں، لہذا جس مسئلہ کو وہ تنہا بیان کریں اس میں ان کی اتباع نہیں کی جائے گی، پس علامہ زاہدی کی قنیة
Fifth cause: The author being weak. If a jurist declares an author weak due to some reason, then all his books are non-reliable. But if another jurist has declared him a reliable author and that second jurist is higher in scholarly rank, then his book will be reliable. For example, regarding 'Allamah al-Zahidi, 'Allamah Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami says that al-Zahidi transmits weak narrations, so in a matter that he alone mentions, he is not to be followed. Thus, al-Zahidi's Qunyah...
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This cause is about the author's personal weakness. If a jurist deems the author unreliable (e.g., because he transmits weak narrations), his entire corpus is rejected. However, if a higher-ranking jurist considers him reliable, his books are accepted. The example is al-Zahidi, whose Qunyah al-Munyah is not relied upon for unique statements because he is known to report weak narrations.

Key Terms
مؤلف کا ضعیف ہونا (mu'allif ka da'if hona): The author is considered a weak authority, often because he transmits weak narrations or lacks scholarly rigor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is unknown
B) He transmits weak narrations
C) His book is too brief
D) He was declared weak by a lower jurist

Key Takeaway
The fifth cause teaches that a mufti must verify the author's personal reliability; a weak author's unique rulings carry no weight unless a higher authority endorses him.

Fourth Cause: Book Declared Weak by a Reliable Faqih
Rasm al-mufti rule: book weakness due to faqih's declaration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fourth cause of book unreliability: identify when a book is declared unreliable by a muhaqqiq faqih and state the exception regarding a higher-ranking faqih's contrary explicit statement.

Core Idea
A book becomes unreliable for fatwa if a verifying jurist declares it weak, unless a higher-ranking jurist explicitly contradicts.

This lesson covers the fourth cause that renders a book unreliable for fatwa under Hanafi rasm al-mufti. When a muhaqqiq faqih (a verifying jurist) declares a book weak, his judgment carries authority even without explanation. However, this is not absolute: a higher-ranking faqih can override the declaration. Understanding this hierarchy protects fatwa practice from both uncritical acceptance and arbitrary rejection of scholarly works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
A book declared weak by a muhaqqiq faqih or great scholar becomes unreliable (ghayr mu'tabar) for fatwa.
The declaration is effective even if no reason is given.
2
Determine the condition of authority
The scholar must be a muhaqqiq faqih or a great scholar ('alim kabir) – not just any scholar.
This ensures only competent jurists can affect the reliability of a book.
3
Recognize the exception
If another faqih of higher rank explicitly contradicts the declaration, the book remains reliable.
Higher rank (rutba) is determined by scholarly authority, not just age or fame.
4
Apply to the example
Mushtamil al-Ahkam was declared weak by Baraklawi and Lakhnawi, thus it is unreliable.
No higher-ranking faqih is known to have contradicted this evaluation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھا سبب : کتاب کو ضعیف قرار دینا
جس کتاب کو کوئی محقق فقیہ یا کوئی بڑا عالم دین کسی سبب کی بنیاد پر ضعیف قرار دیں تو وہ کتاب بھی غیر معتبر ہوگی ، خواہ انھوں نے ہمارے سامنے کوئی سبب بیان کیا ہو یا نہیں ، الا یہ کہ اس کے خلاف دوسرے فقیہ کی صراحت موجود ہو اور وہ رتبہ میں ان سے بڑھے ہوئے ہوں تو پھر اس کتاب کو معتبر مانا جائے گا، چنانچہ علامہ فخر الدین یحیی بن عبد اللہ رومی کی مشتمل الأحكام فى الفتاوى الحنفيه غير معتبر کتاب ہے، اس لئے کہ علامہ محمد بن پیر علی برکلی اور علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدالحی لکھنوی نے اس کتاب کو ضعیف قرار دیا ہے۔
(المذهب الحنفى : ۲۲٦/١)
The fourth cause: Declaring a book to be weak. That book about which any muhaqqiq faqih or a great scholar declares it to be weak on the basis of some reason, then that book will also be unreliable, regardless of whether they have stated a reason before us or not. Except that if a contrary explicit statement of another faqih exists and he is higher in rank than them, then that book will be considered reliable. For example, the book 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam fi al-Fatawa al-Hanafiyyah' of Allamah Fakhr al-Din Yahya ibn Abd Allah al-Rumi is unreliable, because Allamah Muhammad ibn Pir Ali Baraklawi and Allamah Abul Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi have declared this book to be weak.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage states the fourth cause that makes a book unreliable for issuing fatwa: a reliable faqih declaring the book to be weak. The key point is that the declaration of a muhaqqiq faqih (a verifying jurist) or a senior scholar is sufficient, even if no reason is given. However, if another faqih of higher rank explicitly contradicts the declaration, the book remains reliable. Example: 'Mushtamil al-Ahkam' was declared weak by Baraklawi and Lakhnawi. This rule ensures that fatwa books are based on scholarly authority and not personal opinion.

Key Terms
ضعیف (da'if): Weak; a book declared unreliable for fatwa by a competent scholar.
غیر معتبر (ghayr mu'tabar): Not reliable; not considered authoritative for issuing fatwa.
محقق فقیہ (muhaqqiq faqih): A verifying jurist, a high-level faqih who can evaluate books.
رتبہ (rutba): Rank; scholarly authority level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fourth cause, what condition allows a book declared weak by a faqih to still be considered reliable?
A) If the faqih gave no reason.
B) If another faqih of higher rank explicitly contradicts the declaration.
C) If the book is widely used.
D) If the author is famous.

Key Takeaway
A book's reliability for fatwa is determined by the evaluation of muhaqqiq fuqaha, with a hierarchy that allows higher-ranking scholars to override lower ones.

Fifth Cause: Author Declared Weak by a Faqih
Explains the fifth cause: author declared weak by a faqih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether an author is considered reliable based on faqih declarations, and apply the hierarchy rule.

Core Idea
An author is unreliable if a faqih declares him weak, unless a higher-ranking faqih affirms him.

In fatwa practice, not all books carry equal authority. The reliability of the author matters. This lesson explains the fifth cause: when a faqih declares an author weak, all his books become unreliable—unless a higher-ranking faqih overrides that judgment. We'll examine the rule and its application using the example of Allamah Zahidi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the general rule: if a faqih declares an author weak, all his books are unreliable.
This is the default position.
2
Identify the exception
If a higher-ranking faqih affirms the author's reliability, the books become reliable.
The hierarchy of faqihs is crucial.
3
Apply to the given example
Allamah Zahidi was declared weak by Ibn Abidin; no higher-ranking faqih contradicted, so Qunyah al-Munyah is unreliable.
The example confirms the rule's application.
4
Note the practical consequence
Muftis should not rely on such books for fatwa unless the author is rehabilitated by a higher authority.
This safeguards the integrity of fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پانچواں سبب : مؤلف کا ضعیف ہونا
جس مصنف کو کوئی فقیہ کسی سبب کی بنیاد پر ضعیف قراردیں تو ان کی تمام کتابیں غیر معتبر ہوں گی لیکن اگر کسی دوسرے فقیہ نے ان کو معتبر مصنف قرار دیا ہو اور وہ دوسرا فقیہ علمی لحاظ سے پہلے سے بلند تر ہو تو پھر ان کی کتاب معتبر ہوگی ،مثلا علامہ زاہدی کے بارے میں علامہ ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں کہ زاہدی ضعیف روایات کو نقل کرتے ہیں، لہذا جس مسئلہ کو وہ تنہا بیان کریں اس میں ان کی اتباع نہیں کی جائے گی ، پس علامہ زاہدی کی قنیة المنیه غیر معتبر ہے، کیوں کہ علامہ شامی جیسے عظیم فقیہ نے ان کو ضعیف قرار دیا ہے اور کسی دوسرے فقیہ نے علامہ شامی کے قول کی تردید بھی نہیں کی ہے۔
(المذهب الحنفي: ۲۳۸/۱)
The fifth cause: The author being weak. Any author whom a faqih declares weak on the basis of some reason, then all his books will be unreliable. But if another faqih has considered him a reliable author and that other faqih is higher in scholarly rank than the first, then his book will be reliable. For example, regarding Allamah Zahidi, Allamah Ibn Abidin al-Shami says that Zahidi transmits weak narrations, so in any issue that he alone mentions, he is not to be followed. Thus, Allamah Zahidi's 'Qunyah al-Munyah' is unreliable, because a great faqih like Allamah Shami declared him weak, and no other faqih has refuted the statement of Allamah Shami.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth cause: the author himself being declared weak by a faqih. It applies the same logic as the fourth cause: the declaration of a competent faqih is sufficient. However, if another higher-ranking faqih affirms the author's reliability, then the books are considered reliable. The example given is Allamah Zahidi, who was declared weak by Ibn Abidin because he transmitted weak narrations. Consequently, his book 'Qunyah al-Munyah' is not relied upon in fatwa. This rule maintains the integrity of fatwa by filtering out authors whose transmissions are not trustworthy.

Key Terms
مصنف (musannif): Author of a book.
ضعیف (مصنف) (da'if): Weak; here refers to a person considered unreliable in narration or scholarship.
معتبر مصنف (mu'tabar musannif): A reliable author whose books are considered authoritative.
قنیة المنية (Qunyah al-Munyah): A book by Allamah Zahidi, declared unreliable due to its author's weakness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The books are unreliable.
B) The books are considered reliable.
C) The decision is deferred.
D) The lower-ranking faqih's opinion is followed.

Key Takeaway
An author's reliability is assessed by faqih declarations; if a higher-ranking faqih affirms, the books become reliable.

Doubt in Book Attribution as a Cause for Unreliability
Rasm al-Mufti: rule on unreliable books due to doubtful nisbat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a book's attribution is in doubt and apply the rule that such books are unreliable for fatwa.

Core Idea
A book's attribution must be proven by an authentic chain; doubt makes it unusable.

Not every book bearing a scholar's name is actually his work. The sixth cause for declaring a book unreliable is doubt about its attribution. This lesson explains the rule and illustrates it with two classical examples, helping you evaluate sources critically for iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed author
Look at the book's title and determine who it is attributed to. For example, al-Makharij fi al-Hiyal is attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf.
2
Check the chain of transmission (sanad)
Investigate whether there is an authentic chain proving that the book was actually written by that author. The passage states that for al-Makharij, this chain is missing.
A book may have multiple attributions, increasing doubt.
3
Determine if doubt (shakk) exists
If the sanad is flawed, contradictory, or the author's authorship is disputed, doubt exists. For example, al-Makharij is also attributed to Imam Muhammad, showing inconsistency.
Even if the book is famous, doubt still invalidates it.
4
Conclude the book is unreliable
Once doubt is established, the book cannot be used as a source for fatwa. The mufti must avoid relying on it.
This rule protects the integrity of fatwa from unverified material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھٹا سبب : کتاب کی نسبت میں شک ہونا
بعض کتابوں کو اس لئے غیر معتبر قرار دیا گیا ہے کہ جن مصنفین کی طرف وہ کتابیں منسوب ہیں ان کی طرف ان کتابوں کی نسبت میں شک ہے اور ان کتابوں کا انھیں مصنفین کی کتابیں ہونا صحیح سند سے ثابت نہیں ہے، مثلا المخارج فی الحیل غیر معتبر کتاب ہے کیوں کہ یہ کتاب گرچہ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کی طرف منسوب ہے لیکن یہ نسبت صحیح نہیں ہے، جیسا کہ المذهب الحنفی میں اس کی صراحت کی گئی ہے، نیز مکتبہ قاہرہ سے یہی کتاب امام محمد بن حسن شیبانی کے نام سے شائع ہوئی ہے، اسی طرح شاہ عبدالعزیز محدث دہلوی کی طرف منسوب الفتاوی العزیزیہ بھی غیر معتبر کتاب ہے، اس لئے کہ شیخ الا سلام مفتی تقی عثمانی صاحب کے بقول یہ آپ کی تالیف نہیں ہے، بلکہ آپ کی وفات کے بعد ایک غیر معروف آدمی نے آپ کے فتاوی کو جمع کر دیا ہے اور اس نے اس کتاب میں ان فتاوی کا بھی اضافہ کر دیا ہے جو حضرت دہلوی سے منقول نہیں ہیں۔
(المذهب الحنفى : ۲۳۹/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ٢١٦)
The sixth cause: Doubt in the attribution of a book. Some books have been declared unreliable because there is doubt in their attribution to their authors, and that these books are the works of those authors is not proven by an authentic chain. For example, 'al-Makharij fi al-Hiyal' is an unreliable book because although it is attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, this attribution is not correct, as has been made clear in 'al-Madhhab al-Hanafi'. Also, from the Cairo library, this same book was published under the name of Imam Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Shaybani. Similarly, 'al-Fatawa al-Aziziyyah' attributed to Shah Abd al-Aziz Muhaddith Dihlawi is also an unreliable book, because according to Sheikh al-Islam Mufti Taqi Usmani, it is not his compilation; rather, after his death, an unknown person collected his fatwas and also added to this book fatwas that are not transmitted from Shah Dihlawi.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage explains the sixth cause: doubt about a book's proper attribution to its author. The rule is that if the chain of transmission (sanad) proving attribution is not sound, the book cannot be used for fatwa. The text gives two examples: (1) 'al-Makharij fi al-Hiyal' attributed to Abu Yusuf or Muhammad al-Shaybani — the attribution is uncertain, so the book is unreliable. (2) 'al-Fatawa al-Aziziyyah' attributed to Shah Abd al-Aziz — it was compiled after his death by an unknown person who added unverified material, so it is not reliable. This rule ensures that only books with verified authorship are used in iftaa.

Key Terms
نسبت (nisbat): Attribution, relation; the ascription of a book to its author.
شک (shakk): Doubt; uncertainty about the correct attribution.
سند (sanad): Chain of transmission; proof of attribution.
غیر معروف (ghayr ma'ruf): Unknown; not famous or recognized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes a book unreliable in the sixth cause?
A) The book is old and rare.
B) The author is unknown.
C) There is doubt about whether the book was actually written by its attributed author.
D) The book contains difficult language.

Key Takeaway
Doubt in a book's attribution to its author makes it unreliable for fatwa; verification through an authentic chain is essential.

Seventh Cause: Books from Non-Fiqh Disciplines Are Unreliable for Fatwa
Rasm al-mufti rule on unreliability of non-fiqh books for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a book is unreliable for fatwa due to being from a non-fiqh discipline and apply the exception when the same ruling is also found in dedicated fiqh works.

Core Idea
A book that mentions fiqh incidentally is not authoritative for fatwa unless the ruling is independently confirmed in fiqh works.

Not every book by a reputable scholar is suitable for issuing fatwa. This lesson explains the seventh cause of unreliability: books from disciplines other than fiqh—such as tafsir, hadith commentary, or usul al-fiqh—that mention fiqh issues only incidentally. A mufti must rely on dedicated fiqh texts; otherwise, the fatwa may be based on incomplete or secondary treatment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying principle
Recognize that fatwa authority requires the source to be primarily a fiqh work. Books from other disciplines that mention fiqh incidentally do not meet this standard.
The principle derives from the Hanafi emphasis on direct and authoritative transmission of fiqh rulings (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Analyze the examples given
Examine the three works cited: 'Umdat al-Qari (tafsir/hadith commentary), Mirqat al-Mafatih (hadith commentary), and Mubariq al-Azhar (hadith commentary). Understand why their treatment of fiqh is secondary.
These are respected works, but their primary purpose is not fiqh. Hence, they are not reliable for fatwa unless their fiqh content is corroborated.
3
Apply the exception
If the same fiqh issue is also transmitted in authoritative fiqh books, then the non-fiqh book may be used as a secondary reference. The key is independent confirmation.
This prevents rejecting a valid ruling simply because it appears in a commentary; the mufta bihi must be traceable to fiqh sources.
4
Consider the implication for fatwa practice
A mufti must verify every ruling against dedicated fiqh works before issuing a fatwa. Reliance on non-fiqh sources without verification is a methodological error.
This step reinforces the discipline of fatwa: the mufti is responsible for the authority of each source used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتواں سبب کتاب کا فقہ کے علاوہ دیگر فنون میں ہونا

جن کتابوں میں فقہی مسائل کو ضمنی طور پر ذکر کیا جاتا ہے، جیسے اصول تغییر ، شروح حدیث، اصول فقہ اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر فنون کی کتابوں میں کسی اصول کی وضاحت کرتے وقت فقہی مسائل کا تذکرہ ضمنا آجاتا ہے، تو اس مسئلہ کی بابت اس کتاب سے فتوی دینے کی حیثیت سے وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہوگی، چنانچہ علامہ بدرالدین معینی کی عمدۃ القاری شرح بخاری اور مرقاۃ المفاتیح شرح مشکوۃ المصابیح، نیز علامہ عبداللطیف بن عبدالعزیز بن ملک کی مبارق الازھار شرح مشارق الانوار سے فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ ان کتابوں میں فقہی مسائل کا تذکرہ ضمنا اور تبعا آیا ہے، البتہ اگر وہ مسئلہ فقہی کتابوں میں بھی اسی طرح منقول ہو تو پھر اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
المذهب الحنفي: ۲۳۰/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ۲۱۷)
Seventh cause: The book being in disciplines other than fiqh

Books in which fiqh issues are mentioned incidentally, such as in principles of tafsir, hadith commentaries, principles of fiqh, and other disciplines, when explaining a principle, fiqh issues may be mentioned implicitly. So regarding such an issue, that book will be unreliable for issuing a fatwa. Consequently, it is not permissible to give fatwa from ‘Umdat al-Qari (commentary of Sahih al-Bukhari) by ‘Allamah Badr al-Din al-‘Ayni, and Mirqat al-Mafatih (commentary of Mishkat al-Masabih), and also Mubariq al-Azhar (commentary of Mashaariq al-Anwar) by ‘Allamah ‘Abd al-Latif ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz ibn Malik, because in these books fiqh issues are mentioned incidentally and secondarily. However, if that same issue is also transmitted in fiqh books in the same manner, then there is no harm in issuing fatwa from them.
(al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/230, Usul al-Ifta' lil-‘Uthmani: 217)
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh reason that renders a book unreliable for fatwa: the book belongs to a discipline other than fiqh, such as tafsir, hadith commentary, or usul al-fiqh, and only mentions fiqh issues incidentally. The ruling is that such books are not to be used as primary sources for fatwa, because their treatment of fiqh is secondary and may not be as rigorous or authoritative. The text cites specific examples: ‘Umdat al-Qari, Mirqat al-Mafatih, and Mubariq al-Azhar. However, an exception is made: if the same fiqh issue is also found in recognized fiqh books, then it may be relied upon. This underscores the principle that fatwa must be derived from dedicated fiqh works, not from general works where fiqh is mentioned peripherally.

Key Terms
ضمنی (zimni): Incidental or secondary mention, not the primary focus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is never permissible under any circumstances.
C) It is permissible only if the same ruling is also found in a fiqh book.
D) It is permissible only in cases of necessity (darura).

Key Takeaway
A book from a non-fiqh discipline is unreliable for fatwa when it mentions fiqh issues incidentally; it becomes acceptable only if the ruling is independently verified in authoritative fiqh works.

Eighth Cause: Book Becoming Rare
Rule on using rare books in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a rare book (nayab) cannot be used for fatwa until a verified copy becomes accessible, and identify the conditions under which a previously rare book regains reliability.

Core Idea
A book is not authoritative for fatwa if no reliable copy exists — availability is a prerequisite.

In Hanafi ifta, a mufti must rely only on sources that are verifiable and accessible. This lesson addresses the situation when a book becomes rare (nayab) — no printed or manuscript copy is available. The ruling is clear: such a book cannot be used for fatwa until a verified copy emerges. We will explore the rule and its application through the example of al-Muhit al-Burhani.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of nayab
A book is considered nayab when no printed or manuscript copy is available. It may be mentioned in early works but is inaccessible for verification.
The rarity must be confirmed by a scholar with expertise in manuscripts.
2
Recognize the prohibition
Fatwa from a nayab book is not permissible because the text cannot be verified. The mufti cannot cite an unverifiable source.
This preserves the integrity of fatwa.
3
Identify the exception
Once a verified copy (printed or manuscript) becomes available with a sound chain, the book regains its reliability and fatwa is permissible.
The publication must be scholarly and the chain sound.
4
Apply to the example
Al-Muhit al-Burhani was once unavailable, so fatwa from it was prohibited. After its recent critical edition, it is now acceptable.
This demonstrates the dynamic nature of the corpus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آٹھواں سبب کتاب کا نایاب ہونا

بعض کتابیں ایسی ہیں جن کا نام متقدمین کی کتابوں میں ملتا ہے لیکن ان کا مطبوعہ یا مخطوطہ نسخہ اب دستیاب نہیں ہے، لہذا مخطوطات پر تحقیقی نظر ر کھنے والا کوئی عالم اگر کسی کتاب کو نایاب قرار دے تو پھر اس کتاب سے فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہوگا، مگر یہ کہ اس کا مطبوعہ یا مخطوطہ نسخہ صحیح سند سے دستیاب ہو جائے، مثلا بعض فقہاء نے الـمـحـيـط البـرهـانـي في الفقه النعمانی سے فتوی دینے سے منع کیا تھا، اس لئے کہ اس وقت اس کا مخطوطہ یا مطبوعہ نسخہ دستیاب نہیں تھا، جیسا کہ علامہ ابوالحسنات عبدالحی لکھنوی نے اس کی صراحت کی ہے لیکن اب یہ کتاب شیخ الاسلام مفتی تقی عثمانی کے بھانجے مولانا نعیم اشرف نور احمد عثمانی کی تحقیق کے ساتھ ادارۃ القرآن و العلوم الاسلامیہ کراچی پاکستان سے ۲۵ جلدوں میں شائع ہو چکی ہے، اس لئے اب اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
المذهب الحنفى: ۲۳۲/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: (٢١٥)
Eighth cause: The book becoming rare

Some books are such that their name is found in the books of early scholars, but their printed or manuscript copy is no longer available. Therefore, if a scholar who has research expertise in manuscripts declares a book to be rare, then issuing fatwa from that book will not be permissible, unless its printed or manuscript copy becomes available with a sound chain. For example, some jurists forbade issuing fatwa from al-Muhit al-Burhani fi al-Fiqh al-Nu‘mani because at that time its manuscript or printed copy was not available, as clarified by ‘Allamah Abu al-Hasanat ‘Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi. But now this book has been published in 25 volumes by Idarat al-Qur’an wa al-‘Ulum al-Islamiyyah, Karachi, Pakistan, under the research of Mawlana Na‘im Ashraf Nur Ahmad ‘Uthmani, the nephew of Shaykh al-Islam Mufti Taqi ‘Uthmani. Therefore, there is now no harm in issuing fatwa from it.
(al-Madhhab al-Hanafi: 1/232, Usul al-Ifta' lil-‘Uthmani: 215)
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth reason that renders a book unreliable for fatwa: it becomes rare (nayab), meaning that no copies (printed or manuscript) are available. The ruling is that fatwa from such a book is not permissible because it cannot be verified or consulted. However, if a reliable scholar with expertise in manuscripts confirms its rarity, then fatwa is suspended. Once a verified copy becomes accessible, the book regains its reliability. The example given is al-Muhit al-Burhani, which was once unavailable and thus avoided, but after its recent publication in a critical edition, it is now acceptable. This illustrates the dynamic nature of the corpus of reliable sources: availability and verification are key factors.

Key Terms
نایاب (nayab): A book that is not available in any printed or manuscript form, making it inaccessible for verification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Muhit al-Burhani
B) Al-Makharij fi al-Hiyal
C) Al-Fatawa al-'Aziziyyah
D) 'Umdat al-Qari

Key Takeaway
A book's authority for fatwa depends on its current availability and verification; rarity suspends its use until a reliable copy emerges.

Ninth Cause: Frequent Printing Errors
Introduction to a rasm al-mufti rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ninth cause of book unreliability in Hanafi ifta and apply the criterion of textual corruption due to printing errors.

Core Idea
A book with uncorrected printing errors from unqualified typists becomes unreliable for fatwa.

This lesson introduces the ninth reason that can disqualify a text for use in fatwa: the presence of numerous printing errors. The passage highlights a modern problem where typists are often not scholars, so mistakes persist across editions. Understanding this cause is essential for muftis to assess the reliability of printed sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognize that the ninth cause is 'frequent printing errors' (kathir aghlaat-e-taba'at). Note the context: modern computer typing by non-scholars.
This is a rasm al-mufti principle: textual corruption.
2
Analyze the problem
Understand that errors transfer from edition to edition if uncorrected. The typist's lack of scholarly training is the root cause.
The passage is incomplete; the full ruling is not given.
3
Apply the rule
In practice, if a book has many uncorrected errors, it cannot be relied upon for fatwa. Once a corrected edition appears, it becomes reliable again.
This application is inferred from general Hanafi principles.

Seventh Reason: Incidental Fiqh in Hadith Commentaries
Restricting fatwa to primary fiqh works, not hadith commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of books are permissible for fatwa and apply the rule that fiqh issues mentioned incidentally in hadith commentaries are not reliable unless verified in primary fiqh works.

Core Idea
Fatwa must be taken from dedicated fiqh works, not from hadith commentaries where fiqh is incidental.

The mufti must rely on primary fiqh manuals (kutub al-fiqh al-asliyyah) and not on secondary sources like hadith commentaries where fiqh rulings are mentioned only in passing. This lesson explains the rule and provides examples from classical Hanafi works.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the core prohibition: giving fatwa from hadith commentaries is not allowed because fiqh issues are mentioned incidentally and secondarily (zimnan wa taba'an).
Key phrase: 'zimnan wa taba'an'.
2
Recognize the examples
Learn the specific examples given: Sahih al-Bukhari, Mirqat al-Mafatih, and Mubariq al-Azhar. Note that these are hadith commentaries, not fiqh works.
These are common in the Indian subcontinent.
3
Understand the exception
If the same ruling is found in a standard fiqh book, then it is permissible to cite the hadith commentary as a supporting reference, but not as the primary source.
The exception confirms the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخاری اور مرقاۃ المفاتیح شرح مشکوۃ المصابیح، نیز علامہ عبداللطیف بن عبدالعزیز بن ملک کی مبارق الازھار شرح مشارق الانوار سے فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ ان کتابوں میں فقہی مسائل کا تذکرہ ضمنا اور تبعا آیا ہے، البتہ اگر وہ مسئلہ فقہی کتابوں میں بھی اسی طرح منقول ہو تو پھر اس سے فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
المذهب الحنفي: ۲۳۰/۱ ، اصول الافتاء للعثماني: ۲۱۷)
It is not permissible to give fatwa from Bukhari, Mirqat al-Mafatih (commentary of Mishkat al-Masabih), and also from Mubariq al-Azhar (commentary of Mashariq al-Anwar) by Allamah Abd al-Latif ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Malik, because these books mention fiqh issues incidentally and secondarily. However, if that issue is also narrated in fiqh books in the same way, then there is no harm in giving fatwa from it.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is a rasm rule in iftaa. The mufti must rely on primary fiqh works (kutub al-fiqh al-asliyyah), not on secondary references like hadith commentaries where fiqh rulings are mentioned only in passing. The examples given are Sahih al-Bukhari and the common hadith commentaries used in South Asia. The rule is that such books are not reliable sources for fatwa unless the same ruling can be verified in a standard fiqh manual. The citation provides sources from al-Madhhab al-Hanafi and Usul al-Ifta lil-Uthmani.

Key Terms
ضمنا و تبعا (zimnan wa taba'an): incidentally and secondarily, not as the main subject

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ninth Reason: Frequent Printing Errors
Rule on unreliability of error-ridden printed books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a printed book with typographical errors becomes unreliable for fatwa and apply the rule to assess textual reliability.

Core Idea
A book with frequent printing errors is unreliable until a correct edition is found.

This rule, part of Rasm al-Mufti, addresses a modern challenge: how should a mufti treat books that contain numerous typographical errors? Given that such errors can distort the meaning of legal texts, the mufti must verify the accuracy of the source before relying on it. This lesson establishes the criterion for textual reliability in the age of mass printing.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
Recognize that printing errors are common due to non-specialist typists and publisher negligence. These errors can persist across editions.
The rule targets situations where errors are 'kathir' (many).
2
Identify the consequence
Such errors can change the meaning of the text, potentially leading to incorrect fatwa.
3
Apply the rule
A book with many errors is unreliable until a corrected edition is obtained. The mufti must seek a reliable copy or verify the text.
The rule does not declare the book outright void, only unreliable until corrected.
4
Compare with author's intent
The author may have corrected and revised, but publishers may ignore that. The mufti should not assume the author's approval of the printed errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نواں سبب طباعت میں کثیر اغلاط کا ہونا
عصر حاضر میں کمپیوٹر کتابت کا رواج بہت بڑھ گیا ہے اور ٹائپنگ کرنے والے افراد عموما عالم یا محقق نہیں ہوتے ہیں، اس لئے کتابوں میں طباعت کی بہت سی اغلاط باقی رہ جاتی ہیں اور وہ غلطیاں ایک ایڈیشن سے دوسرے ایڈیشن میں منتقل ہوتی رہتی ہیں، مصنف کی ہزار خواہش اور تنبیہ کے باوجود کتب خانہ والے اپنے مفاد کے پیش نظر پہلا نسخہ ہی شائع کرتے رہتے ہیں، اس لئے اگر کسی کتاب میں طباعت کی بہت سی غلطیاں موجود ہوں تو وہ کتاب غیر معتبر ہوگی جب تک کہ اس کا دوسرا صحیح نسخہ نہ مل جائے۔
Ninth reason: The presence of many printing errors. In the present era, the use of computer typing has increased greatly, and the people doing typing are generally not scholars or researchers, therefore many printing errors remain in books, and those errors continue to be transferred from one edition to the next. Despite the author's thousand wishes and warnings, publishers continue to print the first edition for their own benefit. Therefore, if a book has many printing errors, it will be unreliable until another correct copy is found.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This rasm rule addresses modern challenges. A mufti must ensure the accuracy of the text he relies on. If an edition is riddled with errors, it cannot be trusted. However, if a corrected edition appears, it becomes reliable. The rule underscores the importance of textual integrity in iftaa.

Key Terms
طباعی اغلاط (tiba'ati aghlat): typographical errors introduced during printing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mufti must ensure the textual integrity of his sources; books with numerous printing errors are unreliable until a corrected edition is obtained.

Illegible Manuscripts and Fatwa Reliability
Rule on manuscript legibility for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that manuscripts with unclear handwriting are unreliable for fatwa until the text is verified with certainty.

Core Idea
A fatwa from an illegible manuscript is invalid until the text is verified with certainty.

This lesson addresses a critical practical issue: the legibility of manuscript sources. A mufti must ensure the text he relies on is accurate. Illegible handwriting or poor digital scans can lead to errors. The rule is simple—without certainty of the correct reading, the source is unreliable; with certainty, it is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recognize that some manuscripts have unclear or messy handwriting (kitabat ghayr wadiha). The mufti must assess whether the text can be read with confidence.
This is a common issue with scanned PDFs.
2
Determine the default ruling
The default ruling is that such manuscripts are unreliable (ghayr mu'tabar) for fatwa. A fatwa issued from an illegible source is invalid unless verified.
Certainty (yaqeen) is required.
3
Apply the exception
Once the mufti becomes certain of the correct reading—through comparison, expert review, or a clearer copy—the manuscript becomes reliable and fatwa is permissible.
The burden of verification lies on the mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دسواں سبب کتابت کا واضح نہ ہوتا
بعض مخطوطات ایسی ہیں جن کی کتابت واضح اور صاف نہیں ہے اور صحیح عبارت کی خواندگی انتہائی مشکل ہے، بالخصوص ایسی مخطوطات کی جب پی ڈی ایف فائل بنتی ہے اور انٹرنیٹ پر اس کو اپلوڈ کیا جاتا ہے تب تو اس کی خواندگی مزید مشکل اور پیچیدہ ہو جاتی ہے، خود بندہ کے موبائل میں ایسی بہت سی مخطوطات ہیں جن کی کتابت اس قدر غیر واضح ہے کہ صفحہ دو صفحہ پڑھنا بھی مشکل ہوتا ہے، لہذا ایسی کتابیں فتوی دینے کے حق میں غیر معتبر ہوں گی، مگر جب عبارت کی صحیح خواندگی کا یقین ہو جائے تو پھر فتوی دینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
المذهب الحنفى : ٢٣٤/١
Tenth reason: The handwriting being unclear. Some manuscripts have unclear and untidy handwriting, and reading the correct text is extremely difficult. Especially when PDF files are made of such manuscripts and uploaded on the internet, their readability becomes even more difficult and complicated. I myself have many such manuscripts on my mobile whose handwriting is so unclear that reading a page or two is difficult. Therefore, such books will be considered unreliable for the purpose of issuing fatwa. However, when one is certain of the correct reading of the text, then there is no harm in issuing fatwa.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This rasm rule addresses the problem of illegible manuscripts. The mufti must ascertain the correct text before relying on it. The ubiquity of low-quality digital scans exacerbates this issue. Only when the text is properly verified can it be used as a source. The citation is from al-Madhhab al-Hanafi.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitabat): handwriting or calligraphy of a manuscript

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can a mufti give a fatwa from a manuscript with unclear handwriting?
A) Never
B) Only after verifying the correct reading
C) Only if it is a PDF
D) Only if it is from a famous author

Key Takeaway
Manuscripts with unclear handwriting are unreliable for fatwa unless the mufti verifies the correct reading with certainty.

Seventh Principle: Tabaqat of Rulings (Zahir al-Riwayah)
Explains the mufti must know the three levels of Hanafi rulings, focusing on the first level: Zahir al-Riwayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three levels of Hanafi rulings, distinguish Zahir al-Riwayah from other categories, and apply the principle that Zahir al-Riwayah takes precedence in fatwa.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah from Imam Muhammad's six books carries the highest authority for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

In the Hanafi school, not all rulings carry the same weight. The mufti must be aware of a clear hierarchy: some rulings are well-attested (Zahir al-Riwayah), others are rare (Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah), and still others are later fatwas. This lesson unpacks the first and most authoritative level, enabling you to prioritize correctly when issuing a fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
List the three levels: Zahir al-Riwayah, Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, and Fatawa. The passage focuses on the first.
The other two levels are mentioned but not detailed here.
2
Define Zahir al-Riwayah
Understand that Zahir al-Riwayah consists of rulings transmitted from the three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) through well-known chains in Imam Muhammad's six books.
The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' means 'manifest transmission'.
3
Identify the six books
Name the six books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir.
These are the core texts of the school's Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Recognize the authority
Realize that these rulings have the highest authority due to reliable chains. A mufti must give them precedence over other categories when issuing a fatwa.
This ensures fatwas align with the strongest school positions.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يم المفتى فى حل من (۸۳) شي عقود رسم المفر ساتواں اصول مفتی کا مسائل احناف کے طبقات سے واقف ہونا فقہ حنفی کے بعض مسائل پر ظاہر الروایہ بعض مسائل پر غیر ظاہر الروایہ اور بعض مسائل پر فتاوی کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے اور یہ تینوں مسائل قوت کے اعتبار سے ایک دوسرے سے بڑھے ہوئے ہیں، لہذا فتوی دیتے وقت اس بات کا لحاظ رکھنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ جس قول پر وہ فتوی دے رہا ہے فقہ حنفی میں اس کا مقام و مرتبہ کیا ہے اور طبقات میں اس کی سندی حیثیت کیا ہے۔ مسائل احناف کے تین طبقات مشہور قول کے مطابق فقہ حنفی کے مسائل کے تین طبقات ہیں جو درج ذیل ہیں: پہلا طبقہ: ظاہر الروایہ مسائل کے پہلے طبقہ پر ظاہر الروایہ ، مسائل الاصول اور رولیۃ الاصول کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے اور اس طبقہ میں ان مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جو امام محمد کی چھ کتابوں یعنی مبسوط، جامع صغیر، جامع کبیر، زیادات، سیر صغیر اور سیر کبیر میں اصحاب مذہب سے منقول ہیں، چوں کہ یہ مسائل امام محمد سے مشہور و معروف طریقہ سے منقول ہیں اور ان مسائل کو نقل کرنے والے معتبر اور ثقہ افراد ہیں، اس لئے ان مسائل کو ظاہر الروایہ کہا جاتا ہے اور اسی لئے ان کی استنادی حیثیت دوسرے مسائل کی بہ نسبت زیادہ ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ اصحاب مذہب سے مراد احناف کے علماء ثلاثہ یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد ہیں، بسا اوقات اصحاب مذہب میں ان کے ساتھ امام زفر حسن بن زیاد اور ان کے علاوہ ان فقہاء کو بھی شامل کر لیا جاتا ہے جنھوں نے امام ابوحنیفہ سے علم فقہ حاصل کیا ہے، لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کے سلسلہ میں غالب اور مروج بات یہی ہے کہ وہ یا تو علماء ثلاثہ کا متفق علیہ قول ہوتا ہے یا ان میں سے کسی ایک کا قول ہوتا ہے۔
Seventh Principle: The mufti must be familiar with the categories of Hanafi rulings. Some rulings are called Zahir al-Riwayah, some Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, and some Fatawa. These three categories differ in strength. Therefore, when issuing a fatwa, it is necessary to consider the position and evidentiary status of the ruling in the school. According to the well-known view, there are three categories: First category: Zahir al-Riwayah. This category includes rulings transmitted from the imams of the school in Imam Muhammad's six books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. Because these rulings are transmitted from Imam Muhammad in a well-known, authentic manner by reliable narrators, they are called Zahir al-Riwayah. Thus, their authority is greater than other rulings. Note that 'imams of the school' refers to the three senior scholars: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Sometimes it includes Imam Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and other jurists who studied with Abu Hanifa. However, regarding Zahir al-Riwayah, the dominant and prevalent view is that it is either a consensus of the three imams or the opinion of one of them.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage explains the seventh principle for a mufti: he must know the hierarchical levels of Hanafi rulings. The strongest level is Zahir al-Riwayah—the well-attested transmissions from Imam Muhammad's six foundational books. These contain the rulings of the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and enjoy the highest authority. The mufti must rely on these first before considering weaker levels such as Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah (rare transmissions) or later Fatawa. This classification ensures that fatwas are based on the most authentic and representative positions of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The level of rulings transmitted via abundant, well-known chains from Imam Muhammad's six books, including the positions of the three senior imams.
اصحاب مذہب (Ashab al-madhhab): The founders of the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad; sometimes includes other early jurists.
علماء ثلاثہ (Ulama' al-thalathah): The three senior scholars: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the source of the rulings in the first category (Zahir al-Riwayah)?
A) The six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
B) The Fatawa of later Hanafi scholars
C) The personal opinions of any Hanafi jurist
D) The Quran and Sunnah directly without intermediary

Key Takeaway
The mufti must always start with Zahir al-Riwayah rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books when issuing a fatwa.

Zahir al-Riwayah: The Strongest Category of Hanafi Rulings
Defining the first and strongest category of Hanafi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sources of Zahir al-Riwayah and explain why it is the strongest category of Hanafi rulings.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah: the six books of Imam Muhammad, transmitted authentically from the three senior imams.

The mufti must know which rulings carry the highest authority. This lesson unpacks the first and most authoritative category: Zahir al-Riwayah. You will learn its definition, sources, and why it takes precedence over all other Hanafi narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its synonyms
Zahir al-Riwayah is also called Masail al-Usul and Rawiyat al-Usul. Note its literal meaning: 'apparent narration' indicating widespread, authentic transmission.
2
List the six books of Imam Muhammad
Memorize the six core books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir. These are the primary sources of Zahir al-Riwayah.
Sometimes al-Kafi and other books are mentioned, but these six are the standard.
3
Define Ashab al-Madhhab in this context
Ashab al-Madhhab here usually means the three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani. Occasionally others like Zufar or Hasan ibn Ziyad are included, but the prevalent view restricts it to the three.
This is a point of ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the restricted view.
4
Explain the evidentiary weight
Because the six books are well-known with trustworthy chains, Zahir al-Riwayah rulings are the strongest. They take precedence over Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah and later fatwa collections.
The mufti must give fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah if available.

مسائل کی بہ نسبت زیادہ ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ اصحاب مذہب سے مراد احناف کے علماء ثلاثہ یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد ہیں، بسا اوقات اصحاب مذہب میں ان کے ساتھ امام زفر حسن بن زیاد اور ان کے علاوہ ان فقہاء کو بھی شامل کر لیا جاتا ہے جنھوں نے امام ابوحنیفہ سے علم فقہ حاصل کیا ہے، لیکن ظاہر الروایہ کے سلسلہ میں غالب اور مروج بات یہی ہے کہ وہ یا تو علماء ثلاثہ کا متفق علیہ قول ہوتا ہے یا ان میں سے کسی ایک کا قول ہوتا ہے۔ دوسرا طبقہ: غیر ظاہر الروایہ مسائل کا دوسرا طبقہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ اور روایۃ النوادر کہلاتا ہے، اس طبقہ میں تین قسم کے مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جو درج ذیل ہیں: ا۔ وہ مسائل جو امام محمد کی مذکورہ کتابوں کے علاوہ امام محمد کی دوسری کتابوں یعنی رقیات، جرجانیات، ہارونیات اور کیسانیات وغیرہ میں منقول ہوں۔ فائدہ رقیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے رقہ شہر میں منصب قضاء پر فائز رہنے کے زمانہ میں جمع کیا تھا، ان مسائل کو آپ کے واسطے سے محمد بن سماعہ نے روایت کیا ہے، جرجانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے جُز فقہاء کے بقول مسائل کا جو مجموعہ آپ نے ہارون نامی شخص کے لئے جمع کیا تھا ان کو ہارونیات کہا جاتا ہے، کیسانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام ابو عمر وسلیمان بن شعیب بن سلیمان کیسانی (متوفی: ۲۷۸ھ) نے امام محمد کے واسطے سے نقل کیا ہے، یا ایک ضعیف قول کے مطابق مسائل کا وہ مجموعہ جو امام محمد نے شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا تھا اس کو کیسانیات کہا جاتا ہے اور ان دونوں اقوال میں تطبیق بھی دی جاسکتی ہے، بایں طور کہ امام محمد نے اس مجموعہ کو شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا ہو جس کو نقل کرنے والے امام کیسانی ہوں ۔ ( آسان اصول افتاء، دسواں باب) ۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم کے دیگر تلامذہ جیسے امام ابویوسف ، امام زفر اور حسن بن زیاد و غیرہ کی کتابوں میں منقول ہوں ۔ ۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم سے غیر معروف طریقہ سے منقول ہوں یا ان کو نقل کرنے والے تنہا ہوں، جیسے معلی بن منصور، ہشام بن عبید اللہ اور ابن رستم المروزی کی نوادرات۔
The mufti needs to be aware of the categories of Hanafi rulings. Some rulings of Hanafi fiqh are called Zahir al-Riwayah, some are called Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, and some are called Fatawa. These three categories differ in strength. Therefore, when giving a fatwa, it is necessary to consider the rank and evidentiary status of the ruling within the Hanafi school. According to the well-known view, there are three categories. First category: Zahir al-Riwayah. The first category is called Zahir al-Riwayah, Masail al-Usul, and Rawiyat al-Usul. It includes the rulings transmitted from the Ashab al-Madhhab in the six books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. Because these rulings are transmitted from Imam Muhammad in a well-known and famous manner, and the transmitters are reliable and trustworthy, they are called Zahir al-Riwayah, and thus their evidentiary status is higher than other rulings. Note that Ashab al-Madhhab refers to the three scholars of the Hanafis: Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad. Sometimes Imam Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and other jurists who acquired fiqh from Imam Abu Hanifa are also included. However, regarding Zahir al-Riwayah, the prevalent view is that it is either the unanimous opinion of the three scholars or the opinion of one of them. Second category: Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah. The second category is called Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Nawadir. It includes three types: (1) Rulings transmitted in Imam Muhammad's other books besides the six, such as al-Raqqiyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, and al-Kisaniyyat. Benefit: al-Raqqiyat refers to the collection of rulings Imam Muhammad compiled while serving as a judge in the city of Raqqa; these were narrated by Muhammad ibn Sam'ah. al-Jurjaniyyat refers to the collection compiled in the city of Jurjan, narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani. al-Haruniyyat refers to the collection compiled during the time of Harun al-Rashid; some jurists say it is named after a person named Harun. al-Kisaniyyat refers to the collection narrated by Imam Abu Umar Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb ibn Sulayman al-Kisani (d. 278 AH) from Imam Muhammad; according to a weak opinion, it is the collection Imam Muhammad prepared in the city of Kisan, and reconciliation is possible. (Asan Usul al-Ifta, chapter ten). (2) Rulings transmitted from other students of Imam A'zam such as Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad in their books. (3) Rulings transmitted from Imam A'zam through an obscure chain or by single narrators, such as the Nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur, Hisham ibn Ubaydullah, and Ibn Rustam al-Marwazi.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage from Naseem Ul Mufti discusses a fundamental rasm al-mufti rule: the mufti must know the hierarchical classification of Hanafi rulings. The text divides Hanafi rulings into three categories (tabaqat) based on their evidentiary strength. The first and strongest is Zahir al-Riwayah (also called Masail al-Usul or Rawiyat al-Usul), comprising the rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books (the 'six books of the school'). These are transmitted through well-known, authentic chains from the 'Ashab al-Madhhab'—primarily the three leading imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Occasional inclusion of other disciples like Imam Zufar or Hasan ibn Ziyad does not affect the mainstream understanding. The second category is Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah (also called Riwayat al-Nawadir), which is further subdivided into three types: (a) rulings from Imam Muhammad's non-core works (e.g., al-Raqqiyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, al-Kisaniyyat); (b) rulings from other major students' books (Abu Yusuf, Zufar, etc.); (c) rulings transmitted through obscure or solitary chains (e.g., the nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur). A third category, Fatawa (later fatwa collections), is mentioned but not elaborated here. The mufti must assign each ruling to its proper category to determine its precedence when conflicting reports exist. This classification is foundational for the methodology of ifta'.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The first and strongest category of Hanafi rulings, transmitted from the six core books of Imam Muhammad via well-known chains from the three senior imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
اصحاب مذہب (Ashab al-Madhhab): The senior scholars of the Hanafi school, primarily the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), and sometimes other disciples like Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which books are the primary sources of Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) The six books of Imam Muhammad
B) The books of Imam Abu Yusuf and Zufar
C) The collections of Fatawa from later scholars
D) The books of Hasan ibn Ziyad

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah, from the six books and three imams, is the strongest category and must be prioritized in fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah: The Secondary Category of Hanafi Rulings
Defining the second category of Hanafi rulings and its three subtypes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three subtypes of Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah and apply the hierarchy when conflicting rulings exist.

Core Idea
Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah includes non-core books, other students' works, and solitary transmissions.

When a mufti cannot find a ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah, he turns to Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah (Riwayat al-Nawadir). This lesson examines its three subtypes and their relative authority, ensuring the mufti knows when and how to use them.

Guided Path
1
Define Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah
Also called Riwayat al-Nawadir, it is the second category, weaker than Zahir al-Riwayah but still used when necessary.
The term 'Nawadir' means rare/solitary narrations.
2
List the three subtypes
Type A: Rulings from Imam Muhammad's non-core books (Raqqiyat, Jurjaniyyat, Haruniyyat, Kisaniyyat). Type B: Rulings from other students' books (Abu Yusuf, Zufar, etc.). Type C: Rulings transmitted through obscure or solitary chains.
Memorize examples for each type.
3
Give examples for each subtype
For Type A: al-Raqqiyat (compiled in Raqqa), al-Jurjaniyyat (Jurjan), etc. For Type B: rulings from Imam Abu Yusuf in his own books. For Type C: Nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur.
The text provides specific narrators for each.
4
Explain when a mufti may use Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah
Only when no Zahir al-Riwayah ruling exists on the issue. Even then, preference is given to the strongest subtype within Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah.
A mufti should not skip Zahir al-Riwayah.
