محمد نے رقہ شہر میں منصب قضاء پر فائز رہنے کے زمانہ میں جمع کیا تھا، ان مسائل کو آپ کے واسطے سے محمد بن سماعہ نے روایت کیا ہے، جرجانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے جُز جان شہر میں جمع کیا تھا، ان مسائل کو آپ کے واسطے سے علی بن صالح جرجانی نے روایت کیا ہے، ہارونیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں جمع کیا تھا، بعض فقہاء کے بقول مسائل کا جو مجموعہ آپ نے ہارون نامی شخص کے لئے جمع کیا تھا ان کو ہارونیات کہا جاتا ہے، کیسانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام ابو عمر وسلیمان بن شعیب بن سلیمان کیسانی (متوفی: ۲۷۸ھ) نے امام محمد کے واسطے سے نقل کیا ہے، یا ایک ضعیف قول کے مطابق مسائل کا وہ مجموعہ جو امام محمد نے شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا تھا اس کو کیسانیات کہا جاتا ہے اور ان دونوں اقوال میں تطبیق بھی دی جاسکتی ہے، بایں طور کہ امام محمد نے اس مجموعہ کو شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا ہو جس کو نقل کرنے والے امام کیسانی ہوں ۔ ( آسان اصول افتاء، دسواں باب) ۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم کے دیگر تلامذہ جیسے امام ابویوسف ، امام زفر اور حسن بن زیاد و غیرہ کی کتابوں میں منقول ہوں ۔ ۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم سے غیر معروف طریقہ سے منقول ہوں یا ان کو نقل کرنے والے تنہا ہوں، جیسے معلی بن منصور، ہشام بن عبید اللہ اور ابن رستم المروزی کی نوادرات۔
The mufti needs to be aware of the categories of Hanafi rulings. Some rulings of Hanafi fiqh are called Zahir al-Riwayah, some are called Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, and some are called Fatawa. These three categories differ in strength. Therefore, when giving a fatwa, it is necessary to consider the rank and evidentiary status of the ruling within the Hanafi school. According to the well-known view, there are three categories. First category: Zahir al-Riwayah. The first category is called Zahir al-Riwayah, Masail al-Usul, and Rawiyat al-Usul. It includes the rulings transmitted from the Ashab al-Madhhab in the six books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. Because these rulings are transmitted from Imam Muhammad in a well-known and famous manner, and the transmitters are reliable and trustworthy, they are called Zahir al-Riwayah, and thus their evidentiary status is higher than other rulings. Note that Ashab al-Madhhab refers to the three scholars of the Hanafis: Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad. Sometimes Imam Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and other jurists who acquired fiqh from Imam Abu Hanifa are also included. However, regarding Zahir al-Riwayah, the prevalent view is that it is either the unanimous opinion of the three scholars or the opinion of one of them. Second category: Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah. The second category is called Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Nawadir. It includes three types: (1) Rulings transmitted in Imam Muhammad's other books besides the six, such as al-Raqqiyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, and al-Kisaniyyat. Benefit: al-Raqqiyat refers to the collection of rulings Imam Muhammad compiled while serving as a judge in the city of Raqqa; these were narrated by Muhammad ibn Sam'ah. al-Jurjaniyyat refers to the collection compiled in the city of Jurjan, narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani. al-Haruniyyat refers to the collection compiled during the time of Harun al-Rashid; some jurists say it is named after a person named Harun. al-Kisaniyyat refers to the collection narrated by Imam Abu Umar Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb ibn Sulayman al-Kisani (d. 278 AH) from Imam Muhammad; according to a weak opinion, it is the collection Imam Muhammad prepared in the city of Kisan, and reconciliation is possible. (Asan Usul al-Ifta, chapter ten). (2) Rulings transmitted from other students of Imam A'zam such as Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad in their books. (3) Rulings transmitted from Imam A'zam through an obscure chain or by single narrators, such as the Nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur, Hisham ibn Ubaydullah, and Ibn Rustam al-Marwazi.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage from Naseem Ul Mufti discusses a fundamental rasm al-mufti rule: the mufti must know the hierarchical classification of Hanafi rulings. The text divides Hanafi rulings into three categories (tabaqat) based on their evidentiary strength. The first and strongest is Zahir al-Riwayah (also called Masail al-Usul or Rawiyat al-Usul), comprising the rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books (the 'six books of the school'). These are transmitted through well-known, authentic chains from the 'Ashab al-Madhhab'—primarily the three leading imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Occasional inclusion of other disciples like Imam Zufar or Hasan ibn Ziyad does not affect the mainstream understanding. The second category is Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah (also called Riwayat al-Nawadir), which is further subdivided into three types: (a) rulings from Imam Muhammad's non-core works (e.g., al-Raqqiyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, al-Kisaniyyat); (b) rulings from other major students' books (Abu Yusuf, Zufar, etc.); (c) rulings transmitted through obscure or solitary chains (e.g., the nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur). A third category, Fatawa (later fatwa collections), is mentioned but not elaborated here. The mufti must assign each ruling to its proper category to determine its precedence when conflicting reports exist. This classification is foundational for the methodology of ifta'.

Key Terms
غیر ظاہر الروایہ (Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah): The second category of Hanafi rulings, also called Riwayat al-Nawadir, including rulings from Imam Muhammad's non-core books, other students' works, and solitary transmissions.
رقیات (Raqqiyat): A collection of rulings Imam Muhammad compiled while serving as a judge in Raqqa, narrated by Muhammad ibn Sam'ah.
جرجانیات (Jurjaniyyat): A collection of rulings Imam Muhammad compiled in Jurjan, narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani.
ہارونیات (Haruniyyat): A collection of rulings Imam Muhammad compiled during the time of Harun al-Rashid or for a person named Harun.
کیسانیات (Kisaniyyat): A collection of rulings narrated by Imam al-Kisani from Imam Muhammad, or compiled by Imam Muhammad in Kisan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a subtype of Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) Rulings from Imam Muhammad's non-core books
B) Rulings from the six core books
C) Rulings from other students' books like Abu Yusuf
D) Rulings transmitted through solitary chains

Key Takeaway
Ghair Zahir al-Riwayah, with its three subtypes, serves as the secondary source when Zahir al-Riwayah is silent, but a hierarchy exists among its subtypes.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
8 min
The Three Types of Non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah Masā’il
Classification of non-zahir al-riwaya into three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah masā’il and apply the hierarchy of authority when issuing a fatwā.

Core Idea
Non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah rulings are used only when Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is silent.

In the Hanafī madhhab, not all transmitted rulings carry equal weight. The second layer, known as non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah or Riwāyat al-Nawādir, comprises three distinct categories. Understanding this classification is essential for a muftī to correctly prioritize sources when deriving a fatwā.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching layer
Recognize that Hanafī masā’il are classified into two major layers: Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) and non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. This lesson focuses on the latter.
The second layer is also called Riwāyat al-Nawādir.
2
List the three sub-categories
The passage divides non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah into three types: (a) issues from Imam Muhammad's other books (Raqqiyyāt, Jurjāniyyāt, Hārūniyyāt, Kisāniyyāt), (b) issues from other students of Imām Abū Hanīfah (e.g., Abū Yūsuf, Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyād), and (c) issues transmitted through obscure or single-narrator chains.
Each sub-category has its own transmission background and naming.
3
Understand the naming and narrators
For each named collection (Raqqiyyāt, etc.), note the reason for the name and key narrator. This helps evaluate the reliability of the transmission.
For example, Raqqiyyāt were compiled in Raqqa and narrated by Muhammad ibn Sama'ah.
4
Apply the hierarchy in fatwā practice
When no ruling is found in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, the muftī turns to non-Ẓāhir sources in order: first Imam Muhammad's other works, then other students' books, then obscure narrations. This order reflects decreasing authority.
Rulings from non-Ẓāhir are not automatically rejected; they are applied with caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرا طبقہ: غیر ظاہر الروایہ
مسائل کا دوسرا طبقہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ اور روایۃ النوادر کہلاتا ہے، اس طبقہ میں تین قسم کے مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جو درج ذیل ہیں:
ا۔ وہ مسائل جو امام محمد کی مذکورہ کتابوں کے علاوہ امام محمد کی دوسری کتابوں یعنی رقیات، جرجانیات، ہارونیات اور کیسانیات وغیرہ میں منقول ہوں۔ فائدہ رقیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے رقہ شہر میں منصب قضاء پر فائز رہنے کے زمانہ میں جمع کیا تھا، ان مسائل کو آپ کے واسطے سے محمد بن سماعہ نے روایت کیا ہے، جرجانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے جُز جان شہر میں جمع کیا تھا، ان مسائل کو آپ کے واسطے سے علی بن صالح جرجانی نے روایت کیا ہے، ہارونیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام محمد نے ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں جمع کیا تھا، بعض فقہاء کے بقول مسائل کا جو مجموعہ آپ نے ہارون نامی شخص کے لئے جمع کیا تھا ان کو ہارونیات کہا جاتا ہے، کیسانیات کا اطلاق ان مسائل کے مجموعہ پر ہوتا ہے جن کو امام ابو عمر وسلیمان بن شعیب بن سلیمان کیسانی (متوفی: ۲۷۸ھ) نے امام محمد کے واسطے سے نقل کیا ہے، یا ایک ضعیف قول کے مطابق مسائل کا وہ مجموعہ جو امام محمد نے شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا تھا اس کو کیسانیات کہا جاتا ہے اور ان دونوں اقوال میں تطبیق بھی دی جاسکتی ہے، بایں طور کہ امام محمد نے اس مجموعہ کو شہر کیسان میں تیار کیا ہو جس کو نقل کرنے والے امام کیسانی ہوں ۔ (آسان اصول افتاء، دسواں باب)
۲۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم کے دیگر تلامذہ جیسے امام ابویوسف ، امام زفر اور حسن بن زیاد و غیرہ کی کتابوں میں منقول ہوں ۔
۳۔ وہ مسائل جو امام اعظم سے غیر معروف طریقہ سے منقول ہوں یا ان کو نقل کرنے والے تنہا ہوں، جیسے معلی بن منصور، ہشام بن عبید اللہ اور ابن رستم المروزی کی نوادرات۔
Second Layer: Non-Zahir al-Riwaya. The second layer of issues is called non-Zahir al-Riwaya and Riwayat al-Nawadir. In this layer, three types of issues are included, which are as follows:
1. Those issues that are transmitted in Imam Muhammad's other books besides the mentioned books, i.e., Raqqiyyat, Jurjaniyyat, Haruniyyat, and Kisaniyyat, etc. Benefit: The term Raqqiyyat applies to the collection of issues that Imam Muhammad compiled during his tenure as a judge in the city of Raqqa; these issues were narrated from him by Muhammad ibn Sama'ah. Jurjaniyyat applies to the collection of issues that Imam Muhammad compiled in the city of Juzjan; these issues were narrated from him by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani. Haruniyyat applies to the collection of issues that Imam Muhammad compiled during the time of Harun al-Rashid; according to some jurists, the collection that he compiled for a person named Harun is called Haruniyyat. Kisaniyyat applies to the collection of issues that Imam Abu Umr Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb ibn Sulayman al-Kisani (d. 278 AH) narrated from Imam Muhammad, or according to a weak opinion, the collection that Imam Muhammad prepared in the city of Kisan is called Kisaniyyat; and reconciliation can be made between these two statements, such that Imam Muhammad prepared this collection in the city of Kisan and the narrator was Imam al-Kisani. (Asan Usul al-Ifta, Chapter 10)
2. Those issues that are transmitted in the books of other students of Imam A'zam, such as Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Zafar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad, etc.
3. Those issues that are transmitted from Imam A'zam through an unknown method or whose narrators are single, such as the Nawadir of Mu'alla ibn Mansur, Hisham ibn Ubaydullah, and Ibn Rustam al-Marwazi.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the second layer of masā’il (legal issues) in the Hanafī madhhab, known as non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah or Riwāyat al-Nawādir. The author divides it into three types. The first type consists of issues found in other books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybānī beyond his six core works (the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah). These include the Raqqiyyāt (compiled in Raqqa), Jurjāniyyāt (compiled in Juzjān), Hārūniyyāt (compiled during Hārūn al-Rashīd's time or for a person named Hārūn), and Kisāniyyāt (transmitted by or compiled in Kīsān). The text explains the naming and narrators of each. The second type includes issues transmitted in the books of other direct students of Imām Abū Hanīfah, such as Abū Yūsuf, Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyād. The third type covers issues transmitted through obscure chains or by single narrators, like the Nawādir of Muʿallā ibn Manṣūr, Hishām ibn ʿUbaydullāh, and Ibn Rustam al-Marwazī. This classification helps the muftī understand the authority weight of different rulings within the madhhab.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybānī (al-Mabsūt, al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr, al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr, al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr, al-Siyar al-Kabīr, al-Ziyādāt).
روایۃ النوادر (Riwāyat al-Nawādir): Rare transmissions that are not part of the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.
رقیات (Raqqiyyāt): A collection of masā’il compiled by Imam Muhammad while he was a judge in Raqqa, narrated by Muhammad ibn Sama'ah.
جرجانیات (Jurjāniyyāt): A collection compiled by Imam Muhammad in Juzjan, narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani.
ہارونیات (Hārūniyyāt): A collection compiled during Harun al-Rashid's time or for a person named Harun.
کیسانیات (Kisāniyyāt): A collection transmitted by Imam al-Kisani or compiled in the city of Kisan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three types of non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah masā’il?
A) Issues from Imam Muhammad's other books (Raqqiyyāt, etc.)
B) Issues from the books of other students of Imam A'zam
C) Issues from the books of later Hanafī jurists like al-Karkhī
D) Issues transmitted through obscure chains or single narrators

Key Takeaway
Non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah masā’il are classified into three types: other works of Imam Muhammad, works of other students, and obscure transmissions; they are consulted only when no Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah ruling exists.

The Third Layer: Fatāwā, Wāqiʿāt, and Takhrījāt
Description of the third category of masail: fatāwā, wāqiʿāt, and takhrījāt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third layer of Hanafi masāʾil (fatāwā, wāqiʿāt, takhrījāt) and explain its authority relative to the earlier layers.

Core Idea
Fatāwā and wāqiʿāt are rulings of later mujtahids when earlier books are silent—still part of the madhhab.

In the Hanafi school, not every ruling comes directly from Abū Ḥanīfah or his two disciples. Later scholars faced new cases and derived answers through ijtihād, forming a third layer of authority. This lesson introduces that layer, its scholars, and its place in the fatwa hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three terms
Recognize that the third layer is called fatāwā, wāqiʿāt, and takhrījāt al-mashāyikh. Understand each term's nuance.
Fatāwā are given in response to queries; wāqiʿāt are events; takhrījāt are extensions.
2
Understand when this layer applies
This layer is used when a later mujtahid is asked about a case not found in the books of Abū Ḥanīfah or the Ṣāḥibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad al-Shaybānī).
It is a last resort before independent ijtihād outside the madhhab.
3
Recognize the scholars
The passage names direct students of the Ṣāḥibayn (e.g., ʿIṣām ibn Yūsuf) and their students (e.g., Muhammad ibn Salamah). These are the mujtahidīn mutaʾakhkhirūn.
Their number is large; they are documented in books of ṭabaqāt.
4
Note the authority
Even if they oppose earlier masters, their opinions are considered part of the madhhab as long as they are based on evidence. They are not outside the madhhab.
This is crucial for understanding the hierarchy.

تیسرا طبقہ: فتاوی اور واقعات
مسائل کے تیسرے طبقہ پر فتاوی، واقعات اور تخریجات مشائخ کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے، اس طبقہ میں ان مسائل کو شامل کیا جاتا ہے جن کا استنباط مجہتدین متاخرین نے اس وقت کیا جب ان سے ان مسائل کی بابت سوال کیا گیا اور انہوں نے ان مسائل کا جواب اپنے امام کی کتابوں میں نہیں پایا تو بذات خود اجتہاد کر کے ان کا جواب دیا، ان مسائل کو مستنبط کرنے والے صاحبین کے بالواسطہ یا بلا واسطہ شاگرد ہوتے ہیں، ان کی تعداد بہت زیادہ ہے اور ان کے تفصیلی احوال جاننے کے لئے ہمارے اصحاب کی طبقات اور تاریخ کی کتابیں ہیں۔ صاحبین کے شاگردوں میں عصام بن یوسف، ابراہیم بن رستم المروزی، محمد بن سماعه ابوسليمان الجوز جانی اور ابو حفص البخاری کے اسماء قابل ذکر ہیں اور صاحبین کے شاگردوں کے شاگردوں میں محمد بن سلمہ محمد بن مقاتل بنصیر بن یحیی اور ابوالنصر قاسم بن سلام کے اسماء تذکرہ کے قابل ہیں، یہ حضرات بسا اوقات دلائل میں غور و فکر کی بنیاد پر اصحاب مذہب کی مخالفت بھی کرتے ہیں اور ان کے اقوال مذہب سے خارج نہیں کہلاتے ہیں۔
شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٦٧-١١)
Third Layer: Fatāwā and Wāqiʿāt. The third layer of issues is called Fatāwā, Wāqiʿāt, and Takhrījāt al-Mashāyikh. In this layer, those issues are included which later mujtahids deduced when they were asked about them and did not find the answer in their imam's books, so they themselves performed ijtihād and answered. Those who deduced these issues are direct or indirect students of the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad). Their number is very large, and for their detailed conditions, there are our companions' books of classes and history. Among the students of the two companions, the names of ʿIṣām ibn Yūsuf, Ibrāhīm ibn Rustam al-Marwazī, Muhammad ibn Samāʿah, Abū Sulaymān al-Jawzjānī, and Abū Ḥafṣ al-Bukhārī are noteworthy. And among the students of the students of the two companions, the names of Muhammad ibn Salamah, Muhammad ibn Muqātil, Naṣīr ibn Yaḥyā, and Abū al-Naṣr Qāsim ibn Sallām are worthy of mention. These persons sometimes oppose the companions of the madhhab based on reflection on the evidences, and their statements are not considered outside the madhhab.
Sharḥ ʿUqūd Rasm al-Muftī: 67-71.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage introduces the third and least authoritative layer of masā’il in the Hanafī madhhab: the fatāwā, wāqiʿāt, and takhrījāt of the later scholars (mutaʾakhkhirūn). When later mujtahids were asked about issues not found in the works of Imām Abū Hanīfah, Abū Yūsuf, or Muhammad al-Shaybānī, they performed ijtihād to derive answers. These scholars were direct or indirect students of the Ṣāḥibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad). The text mentions notable figures among the direct students (e.g., ʿIṣām ibn Yūsuf, Ibrāhīm ibn Rustam, Muhammad ibn Samāʿah) and the next generation (e.g., Muhammad ibn Salamah, Naṣīr ibn Yaḥyā). Importantly, their opinions are considered part of the madhhab even if they oppose the earlier masters, as long as they are based on evidence. This layer is used when no ruling exists in the higher categories.

Key Terms
فتاوی (Fatāwā): Rulings given by later mujtahids in response to queries, not found in earlier texts.
واقعات (Wāqiʿāt): Events or cases that occurred for which later scholars derived rulings.
تخریجات مشائخ (Takhrījāt al-Mashāyikh): Rulings extracted by later scholars through extension of principles.
مجہتدین متاخرین (Mujtahidīn Mutaʾakhkhirūn): Later mujtahids who derived rulings after the early imams.
صاحبین (Ṣāḥibayn): Imām Abū Yūsuf and Imām Muhammad al-Shaybānī, the two main disciples of Abū Hanīfah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes the third layer (Fatāwā and Wāqiʿāt) from the first two layers?
A) They are derived from the Qurʾān and Sunnah directly
B) They are rulings of later mujtahids when no explicit text exists in earlier works
C) They are only from the six books of Imam Muhammad
D) They are less authoritative and cannot be used for fatwā

Key Takeaway
The third layer of Hanafi masāʾil—fatāwā, wāqiʿāt, and takhrījāt—contains rulings of later mujtahids and remains part of the madhhab.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Eighth Principle: Fatwa by Students' Sayings
Explaining the eighth rasm al-mufti principle on fatwa by students' sayings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why it is permissible for a Hanafi muqallid to give fatwa according to the sayings of the Sahibayn and apply this principle to identify the scope of taqlid within the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa authorized his students to follow his weaker saying if evidence supported it — making their sayings part of the madhhab.

This lesson addresses a critical question in Hanafi fatwa methodology: How can a muqallid who follows only Imam Abu Hanifa validly act on the opinions of his students? The eighth principle of Rasm al-Mufti, as explained by Ibn Abidin, provides the answer by tracing the students' opinions back to the Imam himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
A Hanafi muqallid has only committed to taqlid of Imam Abu Hanifa. Following the Sahibayn appears to be leaving the madhhab.
The contradiction arises from a narrow view of taqlid.
2
Recognize the Imam's authorization
Imam Abu Hanifa instructed his students that if they find any of his weaker (marjuh) sayings stronger in evidence, they should act on that saying and leave his stronger (rajih) saying.
This instruction is key to the resolution.
3
Understand the teaching method
The Imam's teaching method involved presenting multiple possibilities (ihtimalat) with their evidences, then selecting one as preferred. Students with special ijtihad could adopt another possibility with the Imam's permission.
Possibilities were first raised by the Imam himself.
4
Acknowledge the students' own statement
The Sahibayn and other students recognized that their sayings in opposition to the Imam are in reality the Imam's own sayings from which he had retracted.
This makes their sayings part of the Hanafi madhhab.
5
Conclude the permissibility
Acting on the students' sayings remains within the Hanafi school; it does not constitute leaving the madhhab.
This principle is widely applied in fatwa.

Source Text

آٹھواں اصول
امام اعظم کے شاگردوں کے قول پر فتوی دینا

فقہ حنفی میں بے شمار مسائل ایسے ہیں جن میں قوت دلیل ، عرف و عادت اور ضرورت وغیرہ کی بنیاد پر امام اعظم کے قول پر فتوی دینے کے بجائے صاحبین یا امام اعظم کے دوسرے شاگردوں کے اقوال پر فتوی دیا جاتا ہے، اب یہاں سوال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ جب فقہ حنفی کے مقلد نے صرف امام ابوحنیفہ کی تقلید کا التزام کیا ہے،صاحبین وغیرہ کی تقلید کا وہ پابند نہیں ہے (اسی لئے امام ابوحنیفہ کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے اس کو حنفی کہا جاتا ہے، صاحبین کی طرف منسوب کر کے اس کو ابو یوسفی و محمدی نہیں کہا جاتا ) تو اس کے لئے صاحبین کے قول پر عمل کرنا اور فتوی دینا کیسے جائز ہوگا ؟ یہ تو اپنے مذہب کے خلاف دوسرے مذہب کے علماء کے اقوال پر فتوی دینا ہوگا جو جائز نہیں ہے۔
علامہ ابن عابدین شامی نے بہت تفصیل سے اس کا جواب دیا ہے جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے اپنے شاگردوں کو یہ ہدایت کی تھی کہ اگر میرے کسی مرجوح قول کو دلیل کے اعتبار سے تم مضبوط سمجھو تو تم اسی قول پر عمل کرنا اور میرے راجح قول کو چھوڑ دینا، اور امام ابو حنیفہ کا طریقہ تدریس یہ تھا کہ وہ کسی مسئلہ کے بارے میں اپنے شاگردوں کے سامنے مختلف احتمالات رکھتے تھے اور ہر ایک کے دلائل بھی بیان کرتے تھے، اس کے بعد انھیں احتمالات میں سے کسی ایک احتمال کو راجح قرار دیتے ہوئے مسئلہ کی بنیاد اس پر رکھ دیتے تھے اور دوسرے احتمالات کو ضعیف یا رد کر دیتے تھے لیکن شاگردوں میں سے بعض شاگرد کو اپنے خصوصی اجتہاد کی بنا پر امام صاحب کا بیان کردہ دوسرا احتمال ہی قوی معلوم ہوتا تھا اور وہ اسی مرجوح احتمال پر فتوی دیتے تھے، کیوں کہ اس کی اجازت انھیں خود امام اعظم کی طرف سے ملی ہوئی تھی، چنانچہ امام صاحب کے تمام شاگرد اس بات کا اعتراف کرتے تھے کہ انھوں نے جس مسئلہ میں بھی امام اعظم کے قول کے خلاف دوسرے قول کو اختیار کیا ہے تو ان کا قول در حقیقت امام اعظم ہی کا قول ہے جس سے انھوں نے رجوع کرلیا تھا، تو چوں کہ اس دوسرے احتمال کو سب سے پہلے امام صاحب نے ہی پیدا کیا اس لئے شاگردوں کے وہ اقوال امام صاحب ہی کے اقوال شمار ہوں گے اور ان کے اقوال پر بھی فقہ حنفی کا اطلاق ہوگا اور شاگردوں کے اقوال پر عمل کرنے کی وجہ سے کوئی مقلد حنفی حنفی مسلک حنفیت سے خارج نہیں ہوگا۔

شرح عقود رسم المفتی : ۹۲-۹۳
Eighth Principle: Giving fatwa on the saying of Imam A‘zam's students.

In Hanafi fiqh there are countless issues in which, on the basis of strength of evidence, custom, and necessity etc., instead of giving fatwa on Imam A‘zam's saying, fatwa is given on the sayings of the Two Companions (Sahibayn) or other students of Imam A‘zam. Now here the question arises: When a muqallid of Hanafi fiqh has committed only to taqlid of Imam Abu Hanifa, and he is not bound to taqlid of the Two Companions etc. (for this reason, by attributing to Imam Abu Hanifa he is called Hanafi; by attributing to the Two Companions he is not called Abu Yusufi or Muhammadi), then how is it permissible for him to act upon and give fatwa on the saying of the Two Companions? This would be giving fatwa on the sayings of scholars of another madhhab contrary to his own madhhab, which is not permissible.
Allama Ibn Abidin Shami has answered this in great detail, the summary of which is: Imam Abu Hanifa had instructed his students: “If you consider any of my weak (marjuh) sayings to be strong in terms of evidence, then act upon that saying and leave my strong (rajih) saying.” And Imam Abu Hanifa's method of teaching was that he would present various possibilities (ihtimalat) to his students regarding a issue and also explain the evidence for each. Afterwards, he would declare one of those possibilities as preferred (rajih) and base the issue upon it, and would declare the other possibilities weak (da‘if) or reject them. But some of the students, on the basis of their own special ijtihad, would find the other possibility presented by Imam sahib to be strong and would give fatwa on that weak possibility, because they had permission from Imam A‘zam himself. Thus all of Imam Sahib's students acknowledged that in whichever issue they adopted a saying contrary to Imam A‘zam's saying, their saying in reality is Imam A‘zam's own saying from which he had retracted. So since that second possibility was first created by Imam Sahib himself, therefore those sayings of the students will be counted as Imam Sahib's own sayings and Hanafi fiqh will apply to their sayings as well. And due to acting on the sayings of the students, no Hanafi muqallid will leave the Hanafi school.

Sharh ‘Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 92-93
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth principle in the context of Rasm al-Mufti, addressing a critical question in Hanafi fatwa methodology: How can a Hanafi muqallid, who is bound to follow Imam Abu Hanifa, validly give fatwa according to the sayings of the Imam's students (especially the Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani)? The author first identifies the apparent contradiction: the muqallid has only undertaken taqlid of Imam Abu Hanifa, not his students; thus acting on the students' sayings might seem like leaving the Hanafi madhhab. The answer, summarized from Allama Ibn Abidin al-Shami, resolves this by showing that Imam Abu Hanifa himself authorized such practice. The Imam instructed his students to follow a weaker (marjuh) saying of his if they found it stronger based on evidence. Moreover, the Imam's teaching method involved presenting multiple possibilities with their evidences, then choosing one as preferred (rajih). Students with special ijtihad might adopt an alternative possibility with the Imam's permission. Consequently, the students' sayings are actually the Imam's own sayings from which he retracted, because the possibility was first raised by the Imam. Thus, acting on the students' sayings remains within the Hanafi school. This principle is fundamental for understanding the internal hierarchy within the Hanafi madhhab and the permissibility of adopting the opinions of the Sahibayn over Imam Abu Hanifa in certain cases, especially when evidence, custom, or necessity dictate so.

Key Terms
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two primary students of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani
مرجوح (marjuh): A saying that is considered weaker or less preferred in terms of evidence or strength
اجتہاد (ijtihad): The effort of a qualified scholar to derive a legal ruling from the sources

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eighth principle discussed in the passage, why is it permissible for a Hanafi muqallid to give fatwa according to the saying of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) instead of Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Because the Sahibayn were mujtahids in their own right and their school is independent of Imam Abu Hanifa.
B) Because Imam Abu Hanifa instructed his students to follow his weaker sayings if they found them stronger in evidence, and the Sahibayn's opinions are considered as Imam's own retracted sayings.
C) Because the Sahibayn's opinions are based on ijma and therefore binding on all Hanafis.
D) Because the Hanafi madhhab officially changed to follow the Sahibayn in all matters after Imam Abu Hanifa's death.

Key Takeaway
The eighth principle allows Hanafis to follow the Sahibayn's opinions without leaving the madhhab, because their sayings are considered the Imam's retracted sayings.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

8 min
Are Sahibayn's Opinions Part of Hanafi Fiqh?
Defining the scope of Hanafi fiqh regarding Sahibayn's opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scope of Hanafi fiqh and apply the rule that opinions of the Sahibayn and later mashayikh are included when based on Imam Abu Hanifa's principles and accepted by reliable authorities.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab includes student and later scholar opinions derived from Abu Hanifa's usul — staying within the school is broad.

This passage addresses a crucial methodological question for the Hanafi mufti: how far does the madhhab extend? While Imam Abu Hanifa's statements are the foundation, his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as well as later authoritative scholars (mashayikh), also contributed rulings that are considered part of the school. Understanding this dynamic is essential for correctly issuing fatwa and maintaining the school's coherence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What is the exact question being asked? Are the opinions of the Sahibayn within the Hanafi madhhab? This is a rasm al-mufti issue.
2
State the first opinion
The passage indicates two opinions. The first: their opinions are included because they are based on the Imam's own principles and possibilities.
3
Analyze the evidence
How does the text justify this? It says the Imam himself created the alternative possibilities, and the disciples' statements are in reality the Imam's statements from which he had retracted.
4
Consider the second opinion and Allama Shami's elaboration
Some hold only direct statements count. But Shami argues that if reliable mashayikh deem a disciple's opinion preponderant, it becomes part of the madhhab. Also, rulings based on changed customs are included if based on the Imam's rules.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does this make? A muqallid can follow Sahibayn's opinion without leaving the madhhab.

م المفتى فى حل من
شي عقود رسم المف
کرتے تھے کہ انھوں نے جس مسئلہ میں بھی امام اعظم کے قول کے خلاف دوسرے قول کو اختیار کیا ہے تو ان کا قول در حقیقت امام اعظم ہی کا قول ہے جس سے انھوں نے رجوع کرلیا تھا، تو چوں کہ اس دوسرے احتمال کو سب سے پہلے امام صاحب نے ہی پیدا کیا اس لئے شاگردوں کے وہ اقوال امام صاحب ہی کے اقوال شمار ہوں گے اور ان کے اقوال پر بھی فقہ حنفی کا اطلاق ہوگا اور شاگردوں کے اقوال پر عمل کرنے کی وجہ سے کوئی مقلد حفی مسلک حفیت سے خارج نہیں ہوگا۔

نواں اصول
فقہ حنفی میں صاحبین کے اقوال شامل ہیں یا نہیں؟
فقہ حنفی میں امام اعظم کے علاوہ صاحبین اور مشائخ احناف کے اقوال شامل ہوں
ا۔
گے یا نہیں؟ اس سلسلہ میں قدرے اختلاف ہے اور بنیادی طور پر دو اقوال ملتے ہیں: پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ اصحاب کے اقوال چوں کہ امام صاحب ہی کے اقوال ہیں اور انھیں کے اصول و قواعد پر مبنی ہیں اس لئے ان کے اقوال بھی فقہ حنفی میں شامل ہوں
گے، علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں: اور اس بحث کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب کے شاگردوں نے اپنے امام اعظم کی مخالفت . مخالفت ہے تو وہ قول امام صاحب کے مذہب سے خارج نہیں ہوگا جبکہ معتبر مشائخ اس قول کو راجح قرار دیں، اسی طرح وہ مسائل جن کی بنیاد مشائخ نے زمانہ میں تبدیلی، ضرورت و حاجت یا اس کے علاوہ کسی اور سبب سے جدید عرف پر رکھا ہو ایسے مسائل بھی مذہب سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے، کیوں کہ مشائخ نے جس قول کو اپنے نزدیک دلائل کے رائج ہونے کی وجہ سے راجح قرار دیا ہے اس کی اجازت انھیں امام کی طرف سے دی گئی ہے، اسی طرح مشائخ نے جن مسائل کا دارو مدار بدلے ہوئے زمانہ اور عرف پر رکھا ہے یہ خیال کرتے ہوئے کہ اگر امام صاحب زندہ ہوتے تو امام صاحب بھی وہی بات فرماتے جو ان مشائخ نے کہی ہے ( تو ایسے مسائل بھی مذہب حنفی سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے ) کیوں کہ مشائخ نے جو کچھ کہا ہے وہ امام صاحب ہی کے قواعد پر مبنی ہے، لہذا یہ قول امام صاحب کے مذہب کا مقتضی ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ٩٦)
علامہ شامی مزید فرماتے ہیں: لیکن مناسب یہ ہے کہ " قال ابو حنيفة كذا “ صرف ان مسائل کے متعلق کہا
The mufti in resolving... They used to say that in whichever issue they adopted an opinion contrary to the statement of Imam A'zam, their statement is in reality the statement of Imam A'zam from which he had retracted. So since this other probability was first created by Imam Sahib himself, therefore those statements of the disciples will be counted as the statements of Imam Sahib himself, and the label of Hanafi fiqh will apply to their statements, and due to acting on the disciples' statements, no Hanafi muqallid will exit from the Hanafi school. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 92-93) (Page 88) ... (Page 89) ... Are the statements of the Sahibayn included in Hanafi fiqh or not? In Hanafi fiqh, besides Imam A'zam, are the statements of the Sahibayn and the Hanafi mashayikh included or not? In this regard, there is some difference, and basically two opinions are found: The first opinion is that since the statements of the Ashab are the statements of Imam Sahib himself and are based on his principles and rules, therefore their statements will also be included in Hanafi fiqh. Allama Shami says: And the summary of this discussion is that in an issue where the disciples of Imam Sahib have opposed their Imam A'zam, that statement will not be outside the madhhab of Imam Sahib, provided that reliable mashayikh deem that statement as preponderant. Similarly, those issues whose basis the mashayikh have placed on new custom due to change of time, necessity and need, or any other cause, such issues will also not be outside the madhhab, because the mashayikh have deemed a statement as preponderant due to the prevalence of proofs in their view, and permission for that has been granted to them by the Imam. Similarly, those issues whose determination the mashayikh have placed on changed time and custom, considering that if Imam Sahib were alive, he would also say the same thing that these mashayikh have said (so such issues will also not be outside the Hanafi madhhab), because what the mashayikh have said is based on the rules of Imam Sahib. Therefore, this statement is the requirement of the madhhab of Imam Sahib. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 96) Allama Shami further says: But it is appropriate to say 'Abu Hanifa said such and such' only regarding those issues...
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage addresses a fundamental methodological question in Hanafi jurisprudence: are the opinions of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and later Mashayikh considered part of the Hanafi madhhab? The text presents two opinions. The first, attributed to many scholars, holds that since the disciples derived their rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa's own principles and often based them on alternative possibilities he himself had considered, their opinions are effectively extensions of the Imam's own views. Therefore, acting on them does not take one out of the Hanafi school. Allama Shami is then quoted to elaborate that the disciples' opposition to the Imam is only apparent; in reality, if reliable scholars deem their statement preponderant, it becomes part of the madhhab. Moreover, rulings based on changed customs and needs, derived from the Imam's principles, also remain within the madhhab. The passage thus establishes a rasm rule: the scope of Hanafi fiqh is not limited to the direct statements of Abu Hanifa but includes the ijtihad of his leading students and later scholars, provided it is based on his usul and accepted by the trustworthy authorities.

Key Terms
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim) and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
مشائخ (Mashayikh): The later authoritative Hanafi scholars after the Sahibayn, especially those who compiled the madhhab and gave fatwa.
مذہب حنفی (Hanafi madhhab): The body of legal rulings attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and his school, including the positions of his students and later scholars that are based on his methodology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition do the opinions of the Sahibayn remain within the Hanafi madhhab?
A) When they perfectly match the Quran and Sunnah.
B) When they are based on Imam Abu Hanifa's principles and deemed preponderant by reliable mashayikh.
C) When they are issued as fatwa by a living scholar.
D) When they are unanimously agreed upon by all Hanafis.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab is not limited to Abu Hanifa's literal words; it includes the derived opinions of his students and later scholars when they adhere to his usul and are endorsed by authoritative jurists.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Inclusion of Sahibayn's Opinions in the Hanafi Madhhab
Dispute on the scope of Hanafi madhhab including Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main positions on whether Sahibayn's opinions are part of the Hanafi madhhab and apply Allamah Shami's distinction between explicit and derivative rulings.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab includes both explicit rulings from Abu Hanifa and derivative rulings based on his principles.

This passage tackles a foundational question in Hanafi fatwa methodology: who speaks for the madhhab? Scholars differ on whether the opinions of Abu Hanifa's major students, the Sahibayn, and later jurists are considered part of the school. Understanding this dispute is critical for a mufti when weighing evidence and issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage and locate the two distinct views: Allamah Shami's inclusive view and Dr. Bakdash's restrictive view. Note the scholars associated with each.
Allamah Shami represents the mainstream later Hanafi position.
2
Distinguish explicit from derivative rulings
Allamah Shami explains that rulings explicitly reported from Abu Hanifa can be said as 'Abu Hanifa said such and such', while rulings derived from his principles should be called 'the requirement of the madhhab'. Identify this terminological distinction.
This distinction is key to understanding how far the madhhab extends.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence for a Hanafi judge or mufti. If a judge follows a Sahibayn opinion, is he violating his madhhab? According to Allamah Shami, no; according to Dr. Bakdash, possibly yes.
This affects fatwa compilation and hierarchy.
4
Evaluate the evidence for each position
Allamah Shami relies on the fact that Sahibayn's views are based on Abu Hanifa's principles. Dr. Bakdash points to early textual usage like 'Zahir al-Riwayah' which separates their views. Compare the strength of the evidence.
Neither position is declared definitively tarjih in the passage.
5
Apply to a hypothetical mufti scenario
Imagine a Hanafi mufti is asked about a contemporary transaction. The only relevant Hanafi opinion is from a Sahib. According to each position, can he issue a fatwa based on that opinion? Explain.
This hones the student's ability to operationalize the dispute.

فقہ حنفی میں صاحبین کے اقوال شامل ہیں یا نہیں؟

فقہ حنفی میں امام اعظم کے علاوہ صاحبین اور مشائخ احناف کے اقوال شامل ہوں گے یا نہیں؟ اس سلسلہ میں قدرے اختلاف ہے اور بنیادی طور پر دو اقوال ملتے ہیں: پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ اصحاب کے اقوال چوں کہ امام صاحب ہی کے اقوال ہیں اور انھیں کے اصول و قواعد پر مبنی ہیں اس لئے ان کے اقوال بھی فقہ حنفی میں شامل ہوں گے، علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں: اور اس بحث کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب کے شاگردوں نے اپنے امام اعظم کی مخالفت . مخالفت ہے تو وہ قول امام صاحب کے مذہب سے خارج نہیں ہوگا جبکہ معتبر مشائخ اس قول کو راجح قرار دیں، اسی طرح وہ مسائل جن کی بنیاد مشائخ نے زمانہ میں تبدیلی، ضرورت و حاجت یا اس کے علاوہ کسی اور سبب سے جدید عرف پر رکھا ہو ایسے مسائل بھی مذہب سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے، کیوں کہ مشائخ نے جس قول کو اپنے نزدیک دلائل کے رائج ہونے کی وجہ سے راجح قرار دیا ہے اس کی اجازت انھیں امام کی طرف سے دی گئی ہے، اسی طرح مشائخ نے جن مسائل کا دارو مدار بدلے ہوئے زمانہ اور عرف پر رکھا ہے یہ خیال کرتے ہوئے کہ اگر امام صاحب زندہ ہوتے تو امام صاحب بھی وہی بات فرماتے جو ان مشائخ نے کہی ہے ( تو ایسے مسائل بھی مذہب حنفی سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے ) کیوں کہ مشائخ نے جو کچھ کہا ہے وہ امام صاحب ہی کے قواعد پر مبنی ہے، لہذا یہ قول امام صاحب کے مذہب کا مقتضی ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ٩٦)

علامہ شامی مزید فرماتے ہیں: لیکن مناسب یہ ہے کہ " قال ابو حنيفة كذا " صرف ان مسائل کے متعلق کہا جائے جو امام صاحب سے صراحتاً مروی ہیں، اور اس قسم کے مسائل کے متعلق یہ کہا جائے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے مذہب کا مقتضی یہ ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے کہا، اور یہی تعبیر ان مسائل میں بھی ہونی چاہئے جن کی تخریج مشائخ نے امام صاحب کے قواعد یا امام صاحب کے قول پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے کی ہے ، اسی کو فقہاء اس طرح کہتے ہیں: امام صاحب کے فلاں قول پر قیاس کے مطابق اس مسئلہ کا حکم یہ ہے ، تو ان تمام مسائل کے بارے میں یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ نے یہ کہا ہے، ہاں ! یہ بات درست ہے کہ ان اقوال کو امام صاحب کے مذہب کا نام دیا جائے گا بایں معنی کہ وہ امام کے مذہب کی اتباع کرنے والوں کا قول ہے یا امام کے مذہب کا مقتضی ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے جب الدر والغرر کے مصنف نے کتاب القضاء میں یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا کہ جب قاضی مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں اپنے مذہب کے خلاف فیصلہ کر دے تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوگا ( تو انھوں نے اس کی وضاحت اس طرح کی ہے ) یعنی قاضی جب اپنے اصل مذہب کے خلاف فیصلہ کر دے، جیسے کہ حنفی قاضی امام شافعی یا ان جیسے کسی اور مجتہد کے مذہب کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دے یا اس کے برعکس، اور بہر حال ! جب حنفی قاضی امام ابویوسف یا امام محمد یا امام صاحب کے دیگر شاگردوں کے اقوال کے مطابق فیصلہ کرے تو یہ امام صاحب کی رائے کے خلاف فیصلہ کرنا نہیں ہے، الدرر والغرر کے مصنف کی بات پوری ہوگئی۔

(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٩٦)

شیخ عوامہ کے دامادڈاکٹر سائد بکداش ( جو فقہ حنفی کی ایک درجن سے زائد کتب پر تحقیق و تعلیق کا کام کر چکے ہیں ان کی رائے یہ ہے کہ فقہ حنفی کا اطلاق صرف امام ابو حنیفہ کے اقوال پر ہوگا، کیوں کہ متقدمین فقہائے حنفیہ کی عبارات میں ایسی کوئی صراحت نہیں ملتی جو اس بات پر دلالت کرے کہ فقہ حنفی کے اطلاق میں صاحبین کے اقوال بھی شامل ہیں، اس کے برعکس متقدمین ہی کی کتابوں اور طرز تصنیف میں بہت سے اشارات ایسے ملتے ہیں جن سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صاحبین کے اقوال فقہ حنفی میں شامل نہیں ہیں، مثلا ظاہر الروایہ
Are the opinions of the Sahibayn included in Hanafi fiqh or not?

Is it that in Hanafi fiqh, besides Imam A'zam, the opinions of the Sahibayn and the Mashayikh of the Hanafis are included or not? There is some difference in this regard and essentially two opinions are found: The first opinion is that since the opinions of the companions are themselves the opinions of Imam Sahib and are based on his principles and rules, therefore their opinions will also be included in Hanafi fiqh. Allamah Shami says: And the summary of this discussion is that in a matter where the students of Imam Sahib opposed their Imam A'zam, that opinion will not be excluded from the madhhab of Imam Sahib as long as reliable Mashayikh deem that opinion to be preponderant. Similarly, matters that the Mashayikh based on changed times, necessity, or custom due to some other reason — such matters are also not excluded from the madhhab, because the Mashayikh deemed an opinion preponderant due to the prevalence of evidence in their view, and this permission was given to them by the Imam. Similarly, matters that the Mashayikh have based on changed times and customs, considering that if Imam Sahib were alive he would have said the same thing that these Mashayikh said — such matters are also not excluded from the Hanafi madhhab, because whatever the Mashayikh said is based on the principles of Imam Sahib. Therefore, this opinion is a requirement of the madhhab of Imam Sahib. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 96)

Allamah Shami further says: But it is appropriate that "Abu Hanifa said such and such" should only be said for matters that are explicitly reported from Imam Sahib, and for such matters it should be said that the requirement of the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is this, as we have said. And this same expression should also be used for matters whose derivation the Mashayikh made based on the principles of Imam Sahib or analogizing from his statement. Thus the jurists say: According to analogy from such and such statement of Imam Sahib, the ruling on this matter is such. So for all these matters it will not be said that Imam Abu Hanifa said this. Yes! It is correct that these opinions will be called the madhhab of Imam Sahib in the sense that they are the statement of those who follow his madhhab or are the requirement of his madhhab. And for this reason, when the author of al-Durr wa al-Ghurar mentioned in Kitab al-Qada' that when a judge passes a ruling contrary to his madhhab in a matter of ijtihad, his ruling will not be implemented — then he clarified it thus: that is, when the judge passes a ruling contrary to his original madhhab, like a Hanafi judge passes a ruling according to the madhhab of Imam Shafi'i or another mujtahid like him, or vice versa. And in any case, when a Hanafi judge passes a ruling according to the statements of Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, or other students of Imam Sahib, this is not passing a ruling contrary to the opinion of Imam Sahib. The statement of the author of al-Durr wa al-Ghurar is complete.

(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 96)

The son-in-law of Shaykh 'Awwamah, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash (who has done research and annotation on more than a dozen Hanafi fiqh books), his opinion is that the term Hanafi fiqh applies only to the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa, because in the expressions of the early Hanafi jurists there is no such explicit indication that the statements of the Sahibayn are included in the scope of Hanafi fiqh. On the contrary, in the books and style of authorship of the early scholars there are many indications suggesting that the statements of the Sahibayn are not included in Hanafi fiqh, for example, Zahir al-Riwayah...
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage discusses a foundational question: what is the scope of the Hanafi madhhab? Specifically, are the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) and later Hanafi scholars considered part of the madhhab? The author presents two positions. The first, from 'Allamah Ibn Abidin al-Shami in his commentary 'Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', holds that the opinions of the Sahibayn are indeed included, as they are derived from Abu Hanifa's principles. He distinguishes between explicit rulings that can be attributed directly to Abu Hanifa and derivative rulings that are called 'requirement of the madhhab' or 'madhhab of followers'. He provides an example from al-Durr wa al-Ghurar: a judge following a Sahibayn view is not acting against his madhhab. The second position, from Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, is that Hanafi fiqh strictly refers only to Abu Hanifa's own statements. He argues that early texts like 'Zahir al-Riwayah' consistently separate the views of the founding imam from those of his students. This passage thus clarifies the internal hierarchy and definition of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
فقہ حنفی (Fiqh Hanafi): The body of legal rulings attributed to the Hanafi school; disputed whether it includes only Imam Abu Hanifa's statements or also those of his students.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
مشائخ (Mashayikh): Later authoritative Hanafi scholars (e.g., those who compiled fatwas and commentaries).
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted opinions of Imam Abu Hanifa, as compiled by Muhammad al-Shaybani in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allamah Shami, when can a ruling be directly attributed to Abu Hanifa with 'قال أبو حنيفة كذا'?
A) For any ruling derived from his principles.
B) Only for rulings explicitly reported from Abu Hanifa.
C) For all opinions of the Sahibayn.
D) For rulings of later Mashayikh that are based on custom.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab is broader than Abu Hanifa's direct statements, including derivative rulings from the Sahibayn and later scholars when based on his principles and deemed preponderant.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Rule of Ascribing Opinions to Imam Abu Hanifa
Explains when to use direct attribution versus madhhab-based expression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Hanafi rulings as explicit or derived and apply the correct attribution formula in fatwa.

Core Idea
Directly attribute explicit rulings to Imam; for derived rulings, say 'muqtada al-madhhab'.

This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti establishes a crucial principle for muftis: how to properly attribute rulings to the Hanafi school. It distinguishes between rulings explicitly transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa and those derived by later scholars through takhrij and qiyas. Understanding this distinction ensures precision in fatwa language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Separate rulings into those explicitly transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa (sarahatan marwiyy) and those derived by later scholars (takhrij al-mashayikh).
The source of the ruling determines how you phrase the fatwa.
2
Understand the derivation method
Derived rulings are based on qiyas on Imam's principles or his statements. They are not his direct words but logical extensions.
Takhrij often uses qiyas or istihsan on the Imam's qawa'id.
3
Apply the correct expression
For explicit rulings: 'Imam Abu Hanifa said…' For derived rulings: 'The requirement of the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is…' or 'According to analogy on Imam Abu Hanifa's statement…'
Never say 'Imam said' for derived rulings.
4
Recognize the scope of the madhhab
Rulings of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad are considered part of the madhhab, not contrary to Imam's opinion. A Hanafi judge applying their views does not rule against the madhhab.
This is illustrated by the quote from al-Durar wa al-Ghurar.
5
Practice formulation
Given a hypothetical case, choose the proper attribution phrase and justify it by identifying the source category.
This reinforces the rule through application.

م المفتى فى حل من (19) شرح عقود رسم المفتى جائے جو امام صاحب سے صراحتاً مروی ہیں، اور اس قسم کے مسائل کے متعلق یہ کہا جائے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے مذہب کا مقتضی یہ ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے کہا، اور یہی تعبیر ان مسائل میں بھی ہونی چاہئے جن کی تخریج مشائخ نے امام صاحب کے قواعد یا امام صاحب کے قول پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے کی ہے ، اسی کو فقہاء اس طرح کہتے ہیں: امام صاحب کے فلاں قول پر قیاس کے مطابق اس مسئلہ کا حکم یہ ہے ، تو ان تمام مسائل کے بارے میں یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ نے یہ کہا ہے، ہاں ! یہ بات درست ہے کہ ان اقوال کو امام صاحب کے مذہب کا نام دیا جائے گا بایں معنی کہ وہ امام کے مذہب کی اتباع کرنے والوں کا قول ہے یا امام کے مذہب کا مقتضی ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے جب الدر والغرر کے مصنف نے کتاب القضاء میں یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا کہ جب قاضی مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں اپنے مذہب کے خلاف فیصلہ کر دے تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوگا ( تو انھوں نے اس کی وضاحت اس طرح کی ہے ) یعنی قاضی جب اپنے اصل مذہب کے خلاف فیصلہ کر دے، جیسے کہ حنفی قاضی امام شافعی یا ان جیسے کسی اور مجتہد کے مذہب کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دے یا اس کے برعکس، اور بہر حال ! جب حنفی قاضی امام ابویوسف یا امام محمد یا امام صاحب کے دیگر شاگردوں کے اقوال کے مطابق فیصلہ کرے تو یہ امام صاحب کی رائے کے خلاف فیصلہ کرنا نہیں ہے، الدرر والغرر کے مصنف کی بات پوری ہوگئی۔
The Mufti in the Solution of... (19) Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. The place [i.e., rulings] that are explicitly transmitted from Imam Sahib, and concerning such kinds of issues it should be said: 'The requirement of the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is such as we have said.' And this same expression should also be used in those issues that the mashayikh have derived (takhrij) by analogy (qiyas) upon Imam Sahib's principles or upon his statement. Thus the fuqaha say: 'According to analogy upon such-and-such statement of Imam Sahib, the ruling of this issue is such-and-such.' So for all these issues it will not be said that 'Imam Abu Hanifa said such-and-such.' Yes, it is correct that these sayings will be called the madhhab of Imam Sahib, meaning they are the saying of those who follow his madhhab or the requirement of his madhhab. And for this reason, when the author of al-Durar wa al-Ghurar mentioned in Kitab al-Qada' the issue that when a judge gives a ruling in a mujtahad fih matter contrary to his own madhhab, his ruling is not enforceable, he clarified it thus: meaning when the judge gives a ruling contrary to his own original madhhab, such as a Hanafi judge ruling according to the madhhab of Imam Shafi'i or someone like him, or vice versa. However, when a Hanafi judge rules according to the sayings of Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, or other students of Imam Sahib, this is not ruling contrary to the opinion of Imam Sahib. The statement of the author of al-Durar wa al-Ghurar is complete.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti addresses a crucial rasm al-mufti rule: the precise language a mufti should use when issuing fatwas. The author distinguishes between rulings explicitly transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa himself and those derived by later scholars (mashayikh) through takhrij (extrapolation) based on his principles (qawa'id) or analogy on his statements. For explicit transmissions, one can say 'Imam Abu Hanifa said.' For derived rulings, one must use phrases like 'the requirement of the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa' or 'according to analogy upon Imam Abu Hanifa's statement.' This precision matters because a fatwa's authority depends on its source. The author illustrates with a quote from al-Durar wa al-Ghurar: a Hanafi judge who rules according to Abu Yusuf or Muhammad is not ruling contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa's madhhab, because those scholars' opinions are considered part of the madhhab's requirements, even if not directly from Abu Hanifa. This lesson teaches muftis to be careful in attribution, reflecting the hierarchical structure of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
صراحتاً مروی (sarahatan marwiyy): Rulings explicitly transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa through established chains
تخریج مشائخ (takhrij al-mashayikh): Extrapolation of rulings by later Hanafi scholars based on Imam's principles
مقتضی المذهب (muqtada al-madhhab): What the madhhab logically requires even if not explicitly stated

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how should a mufti express a ruling derived by qiyas on Imam Abu Hanifa's principles?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa said this
B) The requirement of the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is this
C) This is the opinion of the Sahibayn
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Precision in attribution (explicit vs. derived) is a fundamental rasm al-mufti discipline that upholds the integrity of Hanafi fatwa.

Defining Hanafi Fiqh: Does It Include Sahibayn?
Presents a contemporary scholar's argument that only Imam Abu Hanifa's sayings constitute Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions on whether Sahibayn's opinions are part of the Hanafi madhhab, identify the evidence for each, and evaluate the practical implications for fatwa.

Core Idea
The definition of 'Hanafi fiqh' itself is disputed: early scholars limited it to Imam Abu Hanifa; later practice includes Sahibayn via tarjih.

This lesson examines a foundational rasm al-mufti debate: what exactly constitutes 'Hanafi fiqh'? Dr. Sa'id Bakdash argues that only Imam Abu Hanifa's statements qualify, citing the practice of early authorities. However, starting with al-Hidayah, later Hanafi scholars integrated the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, subjecting them to tarjih. Understanding this debate is crucial for a mufti who must determine which opinions are authoritative within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the Two Definitions
Identify the early view (only Imam Abu Hanifa) and the later view (all three imams).
This is the core dispute.
2
Examine the Early Evidence
Look at examples from Zahir al-Riwayah, al-Mukhtar, and Kanz al-Daqa'iq that show only Imam's sayings considered madhhab.
Bakdash relies on these.
3
Trace the Shift to Inclusivity
Note al-Hidayah's role in mixing and preferring among the three, followed by later authorities like Qadikhan, Ibn Humam, etc.
This became the standard.
4
Analyze the Practical Consequence
A fatwa on Sahibayn's opinion: valid in the later view, but not part of the madhhab in the early view.
Crucial for mufti's methodology.
5
Evaluate the Operative Position
Despite the debate, in practice the later view prevails; Bakdash's view is a minority but historically important.
Consider how this affects fatwa today.

٢۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ٩٦) شیخ عوامہ کے داماد ڈاکٹر سائد بکداش ( جو فقہ حنفی کی ایک درجن سے زائد کتب پر تحقیق و تعلیق کا کام کر چکے ہیں ان کی رائے یہ ہے کہ فقہ حنفی کا اطلاق صرف امام ابو حنیفہ کے اقوال پر ہوگا، کیوں کہ متقدمین فقہائے حنفیہ کی عبارات میں ایسی کوئی صراحت نہیں ملتی جو اس بات پر دلالت کرے کہ فقہ حنفی کے اطلاق میں صاحبین کے اقوال بھی شامل ہیں، اس کے برعکس متقدمین ہی کی کتابوں اور طرز تصنیف میں بہت سے اشارات ایسے ملتے ہیں جن سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صاحبین کے اقوال فقہ حنفی میں شامل نہیں ہیں، مثلا ظاہر الروایہ میں امام محمد کا طرز یہ ہے کہ وہ چیخین اور اپنے قول کے لئے الگ الگ مذہب کا لفظ استعمال کرتے ہیں اور ہر ایک کے اقوال کو تقابلی انداز میں پیش کرتے ہیں، نیز علامہ موصلی کی المختار اور امام نسفی کی کنز الدقائق میں صرف اقوال امام کو فقہ حنفی میں شامل کیا گیا ہے، اس کے علاوہ دیگر متون میں بھی قول امام کو راجح قرار دینے کا التزام کیا گیا ہے، گرچہ بعض مسائل میں عرف اور ضرورت وغیرہ کی بنیاد پر صاحبین کے قول کی طرف بھی عدول کیا گیا ہے، لیکن یہ عدول تو ہر ایک مسلک میں ہوتا ہے، اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ صاحبین کے اقوال بھی فقہ حنفی میں شامل ہوں گے۔ (مستفاد از تكوين المذهب الحنفى مع تاملات فى ضوابط المفتی به سائد بكداش) محقق سائد بلداش کے بقول صاحبین کے اقوال کو فقہ حنفی میں شامل کر کے صاحبین و امام صاحب کے اقوال میں تصحیح و ترجیح کی داغ بیل صاحب ہدایہ نے ڈالی ہے، انھوں نے ہدایہ میں صاحبین اور امام صاحب کے اقوال میں خلط کرتے ہوئے مختلف مسائل میں تینوں ائمہ کے اقوال میں تحیح وترجیح کا طرز اپنایا، صاحب ہدایہ کے بعد قاضی خان نے فتاوی قاضی خان میں علامہ ابن ہمام نے فتح القدیر میں، ابن نجیم نے البحر الرائق میں اور ابن عابدین نے حاشیہ رد المحتار میں اسی طرز کو اپنایا اور یوں متقدمین کے بجائے ان متاخرین کا طرز ہی اصل قرار پایا اور آج صورت حال یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کے اقوال کو باقاعدہ فقہ حنفی کا جز وسمجھا جاتا ہے، صاحبین کے اقوال پر فتوی کو کسی صورت خروج عن المذ ہب نہیں سمجھا جاتا، حالاں کہ یہ متقدمین اور اصحاب متون و مختصرات کے طرز کے بالکل خلاف ہے۔ (مستفاد از تكوين المذهب الحنفى مع تاملات في ضوابط المفتی به از سائد بكداش
2. (Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 96) The son-in-law of Shaykh 'Awwamah, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash (who has researched and commented on more than a dozen books on Hanafi fiqh) is of the opinion that the term 'Hanafi fiqh' applies only to the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa, because the expressions of the early Hanafi jurists (mutaqaddimin) contain no explicit indication that the statements of the two Companions (Sahibayn) are included in the scope of Hanafi fiqh. On the contrary, there are many indications in the books and style of composition of the early scholars that the statements of the Sahibayn are not included in Hanafi fiqh. For example, in Zahir al-Riwayah, Imam Muhammad's style is that he uses the word 'madhhab' separately for the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and for his own statement, and he presents each one's statements comparatively. Also, in al-Mukhtar of 'Allamah Mawsili and Kanz al-Daqa'iq of Imam Nasafi, only the statements of Imam (Abu Hanifa) are included in Hanafi fiqh. Besides, in other texts, the commitment to declare the Imam's statement as preponderant (rajih) is observed. Although in some issues, due to custom (urf) and necessity (darurah), deviation to the statement of the Sahibayn occurs, but such deviation occurs in every school; this does not necessitate that the statements of the Sahibayn are included in Hanafi fiqh. (Benefited from Takwin al-Madhhab al-Hanafi ma'a Ta'mmulat fi Dawabit al-Mufti bih by Sa'id Bakdash) According to researcher Sa'id Bakdash, it was the author of al-Hidayah who initiated the inclusion of the Sahibayn's statements in Hanafi fiqh and the process of correction and preference (tashih wa tarjih) among the statements of the Sahibayn and the Imam. In al-Hidayah, he mixed the statements of the Sahibayn and the Imam, adopting a style of correction and preference among the statements of the three imams in various issues. After the author of al-Hidayah, Qadikhan in Fatawa Qadikhan, 'Allamah Ibn Humam in Fath al-Qadir, Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and Ibn 'Abidin in Hashiyat Radd al-Muhtar adopted the same style. Thus, instead of the early scholars' style, the style of these later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) became the basis, and today the situation is that the statements of the Sahibayn are regularly considered part of Hanafi fiqh. A fatwa based on the Sahibayn's statements is in no way considered leaving the madhhab (khuruj 'an al-madhhab), although this is completely contrary to the style of the early scholars and the authors of matn and mukhtasar works. (Benefited from Takwin al-Madhhab al-Hanafi ma'a Ta'mmulat fi Dawabit al-Mufti bih by Sa'id Bakdash)
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This lesson presents a significant rasm al-mufti debate about the very definition of the Hanafi school. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash argues strictly that only Imam Abu Hanifa's statements constitute 'Hanafi fiqh.' He bases this on the practice of early Hanafi authorities: Imam Muhammad in Zahir al-Riwayah distinguished between the 'madhhab' of the two shaykhs and his own; early matn authors like Mawsili and Nasafi only included Imam Abu Hanifa's sayings. Bakdash contends that the later practice—starting with al-Hidayah and followed by Qadikhan, Ibn Humam, Ibn Nujaym, and Ibn 'Abidin—of mixing and preferring among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad changed the school's character. According to him, the early view was that only Abu Hanifa's saying is the madhhab; deviation to the Sahibayn due to custom or necessity does not make their sayings part of the madhhab. However, the later practical consensus has treated Sahibayn's opinions as integral, such that a fatwa on their authority is not considered leaving the madhhab. This lesson highlights the tension between the theoretical definition and practical evolution of the Hanafi school. For a mufti, understanding this debate is crucial because it affects how one weighs different opinions and what it means to follow the 'Hanafi madhhab.' The passage does not take a position but presents Bakdash's argument, leaving the reader to consider the implications for ifta.

Key Terms
فقہ حنفی (fiqh hanafi): The legal rulings attributed to the Hanafi school; disputed whether includes only Abu Hanifa or also Sahibayn
صاحبین (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa
تصحیح و ترجیح (tashih wa tarjih): The process of determining the correct or preferred opinion among multiple narrations
عدول (udool): Deviation from the main view of the madhhab due to necessity or custom

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, which scholar initiated the practice of including and preferring among the opinions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn?
A) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
B) The author of al-Hidayah (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani)
C) Qadikhan
D) Ibn 'Abidin

Key Takeaway
The definition of Hanafi fiqh has evolved; early scholars limited it to Imam Abu Hanifa, but later practice integrates Sahibayn through tashih wa tarjih, a shift initiated by al-Hidayah.

The Inclusion of Sahibayn's Opinions: A Historical Shift
Historical analysis of madhhab boundaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key historical shift in the Hanafi madhhab regarding the inclusion of the Sahibayn's opinions and evaluate its implications for the mufti's hierarchy of authority.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi scholars expanded the madhhab from solely Imam Abu Hanifa's rulings to include the Sahibayn's opinions, fundamentally changing fatwa practice.

This lesson examines a critical development in Hanafi legal history: the transition from a madhhab defined exclusively by Imam Abu Hanifa's statements to one that integrates the opinions of his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). Understanding this shift is essential for any mufti because it determines which rulings are considered authoritative for fatwa today. The passage traces this change from early texts like al-Mukhtar and Kanz al-Daqa'iq to the later tradition of tarjih initiated by the author of al-Hidayah and consolidated by major Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the early Hanafi approach
Locate in the text the method of Imam Muhammad, al-Mawsili, and al-Nasafi. What was their criterion for including a ruling in Hanafi fiqh?
Early scholars used the word 'madhhab' separately for the Sahibayn and only considered Imam Abu Hanifa's statements as the core madhhab.
2
Recognize the shift introduced by al-Hidayah
Find the passage that credits the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) with initiating the mixing of opinions and the practice of correction and preference (tashih wa tarjih) among the three imams.
This was a deliberate methodological change, not merely occasional deviation.
3
Trace the later consolidation
List the scholars who followed al-Hidayah's style: Qadi Khan, Ibn al-Humam, Ibn Nujaym, and Ibn Abidin. Understand that their works became the standard for fatwa.
These muta'akhkhirin scholars established the integrative approach as the norm.
4
Contrast early and later norms
Compare the early position (only Imam Abu Hanifa's opinions are Hanafi fiqh) with the later position (Sahibayn's opinions are regular parts of the madhhab). Note the practical consequence for fatwa.
Today, giving fatwa based on the Sahibayn is not seen as a departure from the madhhab.
5
Evaluate the implications for the mufti
Reflect on what this means for a mufti's hierarchy: which opinions are mufta bihi? How does one determine tarjih among the three imams?
The later scholars developed a sophisticated system of preference, affecting fatwa in numerous cases.

من المفتى فى حل مباد
شي عقود رسم المفى
میں امام محمد کا طرز یہ ہے کہ وہ چیخین اور اپنے قول کے لئے الگ الگ مذہب کا لفظ استعمال کرتے ہیں اور ہر ایک کے اقوال کو تقابلی انداز میں پیش کرتے ہیں، نیز علامہ موصلی کی المختار اور امام نسفی کی کنز الدقائق میں صرف اقوال امام کو فقہ حنفی میں شامل کیا گیا ہے، اس کے علاوہ دیگر متون میں بھی قول امام کو راجح قرار دینے کا التزام کیا گیا ہے، گرچہ بعض مسائل میں عرف اور ضرورت وغیرہ کی بنیاد پر صاحبین کے قول کی طرف بھی عدول کیا گیا ہے، لیکن یہ عدول تو ہر ایک مسلک میں ہوتا ہے، اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ صاحبین کے اقوال بھی فقہ حنفی میں شامل ہوں گے۔ (مستفاد از تكوين المذهب الحنفى مع تاملات فى ضوابط المفتی به سائد بكداش)
محقق سائد بلداش کے بقول صاحبین کے اقوال کو فقہ حنفی میں شامل کر کے صاحبین و امام صاحب کے اقوال میں تصحیح و ترجیح کی داغ بیل صاحب ہدایہ نے ڈالی ہے، انھوں نے ہدایہ میں صاحبین اور امام صاحب کے اقوال میں خلط کرتے ہوئے مختلف مسائل میں تینوں ائمہ کے اقوال میں تحیح وترجیح کا طرز اپنایا، صاحب ہدایہ کے بعد قاضی خان نے فتاوی قاضی خان میں علامہ ابن ہمام نے فتح القدیر میں، ابن نجیم نے البحر الرائق میں اور ابن عابدین نے حاشیہ رد المحتار میں اسی طرز کو اپنایا اور یوں متقدمین کے بجائے ان متاخرین کا طرز ہی اصل قرار پایا اور آج صورت حال یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کے اقوال کو باقاعدہ فقہ حنفی کا جز وسمجھا جاتا ہے، صاحبین کے اقوال پر فتوی کو کسی صورت خروج عن المذ ہب نہیں سمجھا جاتا، حالاں کہ یہ متقدمین اور اصحاب متون و مختصرات کے طرز کے بالکل خلاف ہے۔
(مستفاد از تكوين المذهب الحنفى مع تاملات في ضوابط المفتی به از سائد بكداش
From the mufti in the solution of matters relating to the contract of Rasm al-Mufti: The style of Imam Muhammad is that he uses the word 'madhhab' separately for the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and for his own statement, and presents each one's statements in a comparative manner. Also, in al-Mukhtar by Allamah al-Mawsili and in Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Imam al-Nasafi, only the statements of Imam (Abu Hanifa) are included in Hanafi fiqh. Besides, in other texts, the commitment to deem the statement of Imam as preponderant (rajih) is maintained. Although in some issues, based on custom (urf) and necessity (darurah) etc., deviation to the statement of the two shaykhs occurred, but this deviation occurs in every school; from this it does not necessarily follow that the statements of the two shaykhs are included in Hanafi fiqh. (Benefited from Takwin al-Madhhab al-Hanafi ma'a Ta'mulat fi Dawabit al-Mufti bihi by Sa'id Bakdash). According to the researcher Sa'id Bikdash, the one who laid the foundation for including the statements of the two shaykhs in Hanafi fiqh and for correction and preference between the statements of the two shaykhs and Imam was the author of al-Hidayah. He, in al-Hidayah, mixed the statements of the two shaykhs and Imam and adopted a style of correction and preference among the statements of the three imams in various issues. After the author of al-Hidayah, Qadi Khan in his Fatawa Qadi Khan, Allamah Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir, Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and Ibn Abidin in his Hashiyah Radd al-Muhtar adopted this same style. Thus, instead of the early scholars (mutaqaddimin), the style of these later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) became established as the original, and today the situation is that the statements of the two shaykhs are regularly considered part of Hanafi fiqh, and giving fatwa based on their statements is not considered a departure from the madhhab in any way, whereas this is completely contrary to the style of the early scholars and the authors of primary texts and abridgments. (Benefited from Takwin al-Madhhab al-Hanafi ma'a Ta'mulat fi Dawabit al-Mufti bihi by Sa'id Bakdash).
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage discusses a critical historical development in the Hanafi madhhab: the inclusion of the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) as part of the established fiqh. It contrasts the approach of early scholars like Imam Muhammad, al-Mawsili, and al-Nasafi, who only considered the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa as the madhhab, with the later approach starting from al-Hidayah author (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani) who began to mix and correct between the three imams. This later approach was followed by major figures like Qadi Khan, Ibn al-Humam, Ibn Nujaym, and Ibn Abidin, and it eventually became the norm. The passage notes that this shift is fundamentally different from the early style, but today it is widely accepted that fatwa can be given based on Sahibayn's opinions without being considered a departure from the madhhab. The discussion is extracted from a work by Sa'id Bakdash on the formation of the Hanafi school and its fatwa criteria.

Key Terms
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): The two companions, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the primary students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
فقہ حنفی (Fiqh Hanafi): The body of legal rulings attributed to the Hanafi school.
متقدمین (mutaqaddimin): The early Hanafi scholars from the first generations after the founder imams.
متاخرین (muta'akhkhirin): The later Hanafi scholars, from around the time of al-Hidayah onwards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is credited with initiating the practice of systematically including the Sahibayn's opinions in Hanafi fiqh and performing tarjih among the three imams?
A) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
B) The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani)
C) Allamah Ibn Abidin
D) Imam al-Nasafi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab's scope expanded from Imam Abu Hanifa alone to include the Sahibayn's opinions through the later scholars' integrative approach, which is now the operative standard for fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Mufti's Knowledge of the Imam's Proof
Explaining the eighth principle: must the mufti know the proof of the Imam?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of the Imam's statement, apply the Hanafi mufti hierarchy, and determine when knowledge of proof is required for fatwa.

Core Idea
Knowledge of the proof is only required for the absolute mujtahid; others give fatwa by taqlid.

This lesson examines a key principle of Hanafi fatwa: must a mufti know the proof behind the Imam's ruling? The text from Ibn 'Abidin's Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti presents a dispute over the interpretation of a famous statement attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. By the end, you will understand how the Hanafi school determines who is qualified to give fatwa and on what basis.

Guided Path
1
Parse the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa
Identify the exact Arabic phrase 'لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا' and its apparent meaning: that no one may give fatwa without knowing the proof.
Focus on the verb 'يعلم' (know) and the source 'من أين' (from where).
2
Identify the two interpretations
List the two possible meanings: (1) mufti must know the proof itself, (2) knowledge of proof is only required for the absolute mujtahid.
Ibn 'Abidin considers the first far-fetched; the second is the preferred view.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind the preferred interpretation
Understand that the first interpretation would demand ijtihad mutlaq capabilities, which a mujtahid fi al-madhhab does not possess. Taqlid, by definition, is following without knowing proof.
Ibn al-Humam's statement in al-Tahrir supports that taqlid is binding on non-mujtahid mutlaq.
4
Apply the mufti hierarchy
Define mujtahid mutlaq, mujtahid fi al-madhhab, and muqallid. Determine which category requires knowledge of proof.
Only the mujtahid mutlaq must independently verify proofs; others may rely on the madhhab.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
State the relied-upon position: a mufti who is not a mujtahid mutlaq may give fatwa based on taqlid without knowing the detailed proof.
This is the position of Ibn 'Abidin and the majority of later Hanafis.
