دسواں اصول: مفتی کا امام کے دلائل سے واقف ہونا
شي عقود رسم المفر
مفتی جس مسئلہ کے متعلق جواب دے رہا ہے تو کیا اس کے لیے اس مسئلہ میں اپنے مجتہد کے قول کی دلیل سے واقف ہونا بھی شرط ہے یا دلیل سے واقف ہوئے بغیر مجتہد کے محض قول کی بنیاد پر ہی فتوی دینا جائز ہے؟
امام ابن عابدین شامی نے شرح عقود رسم المفتی میں اس کا بہت تفصیلی جواب دیا ہے جو کسی قدر حذف واضافہ اور ترمیم کے ساتھ یہاں نقل کیا جارہا ہے، وہ فرماتے ہیں: امام اعظم اور دیگر مجتہدین کا جو یہ قول مروی ہے "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتى بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا" ( کہ کسی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ ہمارے قول پر فتوی دے جب تک کہ اسے ہمارے قول کی دلیل کا علم نہ ہو جائے ) اس جملہ میں دو معنوں کا احتمال ہے: اس جملہ کا پہلا مطلب تو وہ ہے جو عبارت کا ظاہری اور متبادر معنی ہے، اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جب اس کے نزدیک کسی مسئلہ میں اپنے امام کا مذہب ثابت ہو جائے ( مثلاً امام اعظم کے نزدیک وتر کی نماز واجب ہے ) تو اس کے لئے اس پر فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب وہ امام صاحب کے قول کی دلیل بھی جان لے، اور کوئی شک نہیں ہے کہ یہ صورت مجتہد مفتی کے ساتھ خاص ہے نہ کہ مقلد محض کے ساتھ، کیوں کہ تقلید کسی کا قول اس کی دلیل جانے بغیر لینے کا نام ہے (چنانچہ فقہاء فرماتے ہیں: امام کے قول کو دلیل جان کر لینا تقلید نہیں ہے، کیوں کہ یہ تو دلیل سے مسئلہ اخذ کرنا ہے، مجتہد سے مسئلہ اخذ کرنا نہیں ہے، بلکہ یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے کہ امام کے قول کی دلیل جان کر اس قول کو اختیار کرنا اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہے، اس لئے کہ دلیل کی معرفت تو صرف مجتہد ہی کو ہوسکتی ہے، کیوں کہ دلیل کا جاننا اس بات پر موقوف ہے کہ وہ دلیل معارض دلیل سے محفوظ ہے، اور یہ بات تمام دلائل کے جان لینے پر موقوف ہے، اور اس پر صرف مجتہد آدمی ہی قدرت رکھ سکتا ہے، اور صرف یہ جان لینا کہ فلاں مجتہد نے فلاں حکم فلاں دلیل سے اخذ کیا ہے تو اس کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے لہذا مفتی کے لئے دلیل جاننا ضروری ہے" کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ مفتی اس دلیل کی حالت سے بھی واقف ہو، تا کہ اس کے لئے اس مسئلہ میں یقین کے ساتھ امام کی تقلید اور دوسروں کو اس پر فتوی دینا درست ہو، اور یہ بات مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی ہی کے لئے ممکن ہے، کیوں کہ وہی درحقیقت مفتی ہے، دوسرے لوگ تو ناقل فتوی ہیں۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۱۱)
لیکن اس مطلب کو خود امام ابن عابدین شامی نے بعید قرار دیا ہے، فرماتے ہیں: لیکن قول امام کا یہ مطلب مراد لینا بعید ہے، کیوں کہ یہ ( مجتہد فی المذہب) مفتی جب اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ تک نہیں پہنچا تو اس پر اس شخص کی تقلید لازم ہے جو اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ کو پہنچ چکا ہے اور مقلد پر اپنے امام کے قول کی دلیل جانا لازم نہیں ہے مگر ایک قول کے مطابق، علامہ ابن الہمام " التحریر میں فرماتے ہیں: جو آدمی مجتہد مطلق نہیں ہے اس پر تقلید لازم ہے اگر چہ وہ فقہ کے بعض مسائل یا بعض علوم جیسے کہ فرائض میں مجتہد ہو، اجتہاد میں تجری کے جواز کے قول کی بناء پر ، اور یہی قول برحق ہے، لہذا جن مسائل میں وہ اجتہاد پر قادر نہیں ہے تو وہ دوسروں کی تقلید کرے گا، اور عالم کے بارے میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اس پر تقلید اس شرط کے ساتھ لازم ہے کہ اس پر مجتہد کے دلیل کی صحت واضح ہو جائے، ورنہ عالم کے لئے اس کی تقلید جائز نہیں ہے، ابن الہام کی بات پوری ہوگئی تو ابن الہمام کا یہ قول " کہ اس پر تقلید لازم ہے اور تقلید کی وہ تعریف جو ہم نے اوپر ذکر کیا ؟ اس بات پر دلالت کرتے ہیں کہ دلیل کا جاننا صرف مجتہد مطلق کے لئے ضروری ہے، دوسروں پر یہ بات لازم نہیں ہے اگر چہ دوسرا مجتہد فی المذہب ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۱۲)
Eighth principle: The mufti's familiarity with the proofs of the Imam. [From] Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: When a mufti is answering a question, is it a condition for him to be familiar with the proof of his mujtahid's statement in that matter, or is it permissible to give fatwa based merely on the statement of the mujtahid without being familiar with the proof? Imam Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami gave a very detailed answer in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, which is being transmitted here with some omission, addition and modification. He says: The statement narrated from Imam A'zam and other mujtahidun, 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa based on our statement until he knows from where we said it,' has two possible meanings. The first meaning is the apparent and understood meaning of the expression, which is that when the madhhab of his Imam is established for him in a matter (e.g., according to Imam A'zam, the witr prayer is wajib), then it is permissible for him to give fatwa upon it only when he also knows the proof of the Imam's statement. There is no doubt that this situation is specific to a mujtahid mufti, not a mere muqallid, because taqlid is to take someone's statement without knowing his proof. Thus, the fuqaha say: Taking the Imam's statement after knowing its proof is not taqlid, because that is deriving the ruling from the proof, not deriving it from the mujtahid. Rather, it has been said that opting for the Imam's statement after knowing its proof is a result of ijtihad, because knowledge of the proof is only possible for a mujtahid, as knowing the proof depends on the fact that the proof is safe from opposing proof, and that is dependent on knowing all proofs, and only a mujtahid has the ability for that. Merely knowing that a particular mujtahid derived a particular ruling from a particular proof is of no benefit. Therefore, 'knowing the proof is necessary for the mufti' would mean that the mufti is aware of the state of the proof, so that his taqlid of the Imam and his giving fatwa to others upon it can be correct with certainty. This is possible only for a mujtahid fi al-madhhab mufti, because he is truly the mufti; others are merely transmitters of fatwa. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 111) But Imam Ibn 'Abidin himself considered this meaning to be far-fetched. He said: But taking this meaning from the Imam's statement is far-fetched, because when this (mujtahid fi al-madhhab) mufti has not reached the level of absolute ijtihad, taqlid of the person who has reached absolute ijtihad is necessary for him, and it is not necessary for the muqallid to know the proof of his Imam's statement, except according to one opinion. 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir says: For a person who is not a mujtahid mutlaq, taqlid is necessary, even if he is a mujtahid in some issues of fiqh or some sciences like fara'id, based on the opinion permitting tajzi'ah in ijtihad. And this is the correct opinion. Therefore, in matters where he is not capable of ijtihad, he will follow others. About the 'alim, it has been said that taqlid is necessary for him on the condition that the soundness of the mujtahid's proof becomes clear to him; otherwise, taqlid is not permissible for the 'alim. So the statement of Ibn al-Humam – that 'taqlid is necessary for him' and the definition of taqlid we mentioned above – indicates that knowledge of the proof is necessary only for the mujtahid mutlaq; it is not necessary for others, even if the other is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 112)
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the rasm al-mufti: whether a mufti must know the proof behind the Imam's statement. The author presents Ibn 'Abidin's detailed treatment from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. The text quotes the famous narration from Abu Hanifa: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa based on our statement until he knows from where we said it.' Two interpretations are given. The first, apparent meaning: the mufti must know the actual proof and its soundness, which would require him to be a mujtahid fi al-madhhab at least. However, Ibn 'Abidin deems this far-fetched because it would demand ijtihad mutlaq capabilities. The second interpretation, preferred by Ibn 'Abidin and supported by Ibn al-Humam, is that knowledge of the proof is only necessary for the mujtahid mutlaq. For anyone else—whether a mujtahid fi al-madhhab or a mere muqallid—taqlid is sufficient; they do not need to investigate the proof itself. The passage thus clarifies the hierarchy of muftis: the absolute mujtahid, the mujtahid within the madhhab, and the muqallid transmitter. The relied-upon position is that the mufti who is not a mujtahid mutlaq can give fatwa based on the Imam's statement without knowing its detailed proof, as long as he knows that the statement represents the madhhab.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlid): To accept the statement of another without knowing the proof.
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): One who is capable of ijtihad within the principles of the Hanafi madhhab but not an absolute mujtahid.
مجتہد مطلق (mujtahid mutlaq): An independent mujtahid who can derive rulings directly from the primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred interpretation in this passage, for whom is it necessary to know the proof behind the Imam's statement?
A) For any mufti, including a mujtahid fi al-madhhab
B) Only for a mujtahid mutlaq
C) For every muqallid
D) Only for a scholar (alim) who gives fatwa

Key Takeaway
A mufti who is not an absolute mujtahid may give fatwa based on taqlid of his Imam without independently verifying the proof.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

The Mufti's Need to Know the Proof: Two Interpretations
Explaining two interpretations of Imam's statement on knowing dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of the Imam's statement regarding knowing the dalil, and apply the Hanafi rule that only the mujtahid fil-madhhab requires such knowledge when performing takhrij.

Core Idea
Knowing the proof is obligatory only for the mujtahid fil-madhhab when deriving rulings; mere transmitters need not know the dalil.

This lesson explores a foundational rule in Hanafi ifta: the requirement for a mufti to know the proof (dalil) of the Imam's ruling. We examine two interpretations of the famous statement, 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our saying until he knows the proof of our saying.' The first interpretation would burden every mufti, while the second, accepted view restricts it to those performing takhrij. Understanding this distinction clarifies the hierarchy of muftis and their responsibilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
What does the Imam's statement mean? Is the requirement for all muftis or only some?
2
First Interpretation
Some scholars take the statement literally, saying every mufti must know the dalil. Note why Ibn Abidin rejects this as far-fetched.
3
Second Interpretation
Ibn Abidin and others restrict it to the mujtahid fil-madhhab when doing takhrij. Understand the rationale: a non-mujtahid is obligated to follow (taqlid) without needing proof.
Ibn al-Humam's text is key: a non-absolute mujtahid must do taqlid.
4
Role of Taqlid
Non-mujtahid muftis are obligated to follow without knowing the proof. This is the basis for allowing mere transmitters.
5
Practical Application
Use the rule to classify a given mufti's level: does he need to know the proof?
Remember: the requirement applies to takhrij, not transmission.

Source Text

من المفتى فِى حَلْ مَبَاء مباحث
شي عقود رسم المفى
لینے پر موقوف ہے، اور اس پر صرف مجتہد آدمی ہی قدرت رکھ سکتا ہے، اور صرف یہ جان لینا کہ فلاں مجتہد نے فلاں حکم فلاں دلیل سے اخذ کیا ہے تو اس کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے لہذا مفتی کے لئے دلیل جاننا ضروری ہے" کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ مفتی اس دلیل کی حالت سے بھی واقف ہو ، تا کہ اس کے لئے اس مسئلہ میں یقین کے ساتھ امام کی تقلید اور دوسروں کو اس پر فتوی دینا درست ہو، اور یہ بات مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی ہی کے لئے ممکن ہے، کیوں کہ وہی درحقیقت مفتی ہے، دوسرے لوگ تو ناقل فتوی ہیں۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۱۱)
لیکن اس مطلب کو خود امام ابن عابدین شامی نے بعید قرار دیا ہے، فرماتے ہیں: لیکن قول امام کا یہ مطلب مراد لینا بعید ہے، کیوں کہ یہ ( مجتہد فی المذہب) مفتی جب اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ تک نہیں پہنچا تو اس پر اس شخص کی تقلید لازم ہے جو اجتہاد مطلق کے درجہ کو پہنچ چکا ہے اور مقلد پر اپنے امام کے قول کی دلیل جانا لازم نہیں ہے مگر ایک قول کے مطابق، علامہ ابن الہمام " التحریر میں فرماتے ہیں: جو آدمی مجتہد مطلق نہیں ہے اس پر تقلید لازم ہے اگر چہ وہ فقہ کے بعض مسائل یا بعض علوم جیسے کہ فرائض میں مجتہد ہو، اجتہاد میں تجری کے جواز کے قول کی بناء پر ، اور یہی قول برحق ہے، لہذا جن مسائل میں وہ اجتہاد پر قادر نہیں ہے تو وہ دوسروں کی تقلید کرے گا، اور عالم کے بارے میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اس پر تقلید اس شرط کے ساتھ لازم ہے کہ اس پر مجتہد کے دلیل کی صحت واضح ہو جائے ، ورنہ عالم کے لئے اس کی تقلید جائز نہیں ہے، ابن الہام کی بات پوری ہوگئی تو ابن الہمام کا یہ قول " کہ اس پر تقلید لازم ہے اور تقلید کی وہ تعریف جو ہم نے اوپر ذکر کیا؟ اس بات پر دلالت کرتے ہیں کہ دلیل کا جاننا صرف مجتہد مطلق کے لئے ضروری ہے، دوسروں پر یہ بات لازم نہیں ہے اگر چہ دوسرا مجتہد فی المذہب ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۱۲)
امام کے قول کے دو احتمالوں میں سے دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ اس قول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام کے اصولوں سے تخریج کر کے فتوی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب کہ وہ اپنے امام کے ان قواعد کے دلائل سے بھی واقف ہو۔
علامہ ابن الہمام التحریر میں اور ابن امیر حاج التحریر کی شرح میں فرماتے ہیں که غیر مجتهد مفتی کسی مجتہد کے مذہب کے مطابق اس کے اصول و قواعد پر تخریج کر کے اس وقت فتوی دے سکتا ہے، جبکہ یہ غیر مجتہد مفتی اپنے مجتہد امام کے احکام کے مآخذ کو جانتا ہو، ان آخذ میں غور و فکر کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو، مجتہد کے قواعد سے جزئیات تفریع کرنے پر قادر ہو، مشابہ مسائل میں ) فرق وجمع کی اس کے اندر صلاحیت ہو اور اس بارے میں بحث و مباحثہ کرنے پر وہ قادر ہو، اس طرح کہ وہ نئے مسائل جن میں صاحب مذہب سے کوئی قول منقول نہیں ہوتا ہے تو یہ ان مسائل کے احکام کو اپنے امام کے اصول کی روشنی میں مستحبط کرنے پر مکمل قدرت رکھتا ہو اور اسی کو مجتہد فی المذہب بھی کہتے ہیں، اور اگر اس مفتی میں مذکورہ بالا صفات نہیں ہیں تو اس کے لئے اصول وکلیات سے جزئیات کا استنباط درست نہیں ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتی : ۱۱۳)
امام ابن عابدین شامی خلاصہ کے طور پر فرماتے ہیں: مذکورہ بالا گفتگو سے یہ بات واضح ہوگئی کہ امام اور ان کے شاگردوں کا یہ قول کہ کسی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ ہمارے قول پر فتوی دے، جب تک کہ اسے ہمارے قول کی دلیل معلوم نہ ہو جائے" کا مصداق وہ صورت ہے جب کہ مجتہد فی المذہب مفتی اپنے امام کے اصول سے استنباط اور تخریج کر کے فتوی دے، اور ظاہر بات یہ ہے کہ مجتہد فی المذہب میں تیسرے، چوتھے اور پانچویں طبقہ کے فقہاء بھی شامل ہیں، اور ان کے علاوہ دیگر حضرات کو صرف نقل کرنے پر اکتفا کرنا چاہئے ، اور ہمارے ذمہ واجب ہے کہ ہم ان حضرات کی پیروی کریں ان مسائل میں بھی جن کو وہ ہمارے سامنے بیان کریں، یعنی ان کے مستنبط شدہ ایسے
From al-Mufti fi Hall... The meaning of the Imam's statement that a mufti must know the proof is that the mufti should be aware of the state of the proof, so that he may confidently follow the Imam and give fatwa accordingly. This is only possible for a mujtahid fil-madhhab mufti, because he is the real mufti; others are mere transmitters of fatwa. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 111) However, Imam Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami considered this interpretation unlikely. He said: It is unlikely that the Imam's statement means this, because a mujtahid fil-madhhab, when he has not reached the level of absolute ijtihad, is obligated to follow one who has reached that level, and a follower is not required to know the proof of his Imam's statement, except according to one opinion. Allamah Ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir said: A person who is not an absolute mujtahid is obligated to follow (taqlid), even if he is a mujtahid in some fiqh issues or some sciences like inheritance, based on the ruling permitting taqlid for the mujtahid; and this is the correct view. So in matters where he is not capable of ijtihad, he will follow others. About an 'alim, it is said that taqlid is obligatory on the condition that the correctness of the proof of the mujtahid is evident to him; otherwise, taqlid is not permissible for the 'alim. Thus Ibn al-Humam's statement indicates that knowing the proof is only necessary for the absolute mujtahid, not for others, even if they are mujtahid fil-madhhab. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 112) The second of the two probabilities of the Imam's statement is that it means: to give fatwa through takhrij from the Imam's principles is permissible only when one is also aware of the proofs of those principles. Allamah Ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir and Ibn Amir al-Haj in the commentary of al-Tahrir state that a non-mujtahid mufti can give fatwa according to a mujtahid's madhhab by way of takhrij on his principles when he knows the sources of the mujtahid's rulings, has the ability to ponder over them, can derive particulars from his principles, has the ability to differentiate and combine between similar issues, and can debate concerning them. That is, he must have complete ability to extract the rulings of new issues for which no explicit ruling from the Imam is transmitted, in light of the Imam's principles. Such a person is called a mujtahid fil-madhhab. If the mufti does not possess these qualities, it is not valid for him to derive particulars from principles. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 113) Imam Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami summarizes: From the above discussion it becomes clear that the statement of the Imam and his students, "It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our saying until he knows the proof of our saying," applies to the case where the mujtahid fil-madhhab mufti gives fatwa by deriving and extracting from the Imam's principles. And obviously, the mujtahid fil-madhhab includes fuqaha of the third, fourth, and fifth strata. Others besides them should be content with mere transmission, and it is incumbent upon us to follow them even in the issues they present to us, that is, their derived rulings.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage discusses a key rule of Hanafi ifta: the requirement for a mufti to know the proof (dalil) behind the Imam's ruling. The author presents two interpretations of the well-known statement of the Imam and his students: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa on our saying until he knows the proof of our saying.' The first interpretation, attributed to some, is that every mufti must know the dalil. However, Imam Ibn Abidin rejects this as far-fetched because it would impose an impossible burden on most muftis. He argues that only a mujtahid fil-madhhab—one who can derive rulings from the Imam's principles—needs to know the proof. The second interpretation, which is accepted, limits this requirement to the mujtahid fil-madhhab when he performs takhrij (derivation). For others, it suffices to transmit the established rulings. The passage clarifies the hierarchy of muftis (tabaqat), stating that those in the third, fourth, and fifth strata (mujtahidun fil-madhhab) may engage in takhrij, while lower-level muftis must only transmit. This is a foundational rasm rule for understanding the responsibilities of a mufti.

Key Terms
مجتهد فی المذہب (mujtahid fil-madhhab): A mufti who can derive rulings from the Imam's principles and proofs, belonging to the third, fourth, or fifth stratum.
ناقل فتوی (naqil fatwa): A mufti who merely transmits the established rulings of the madhhab without derivation.
تقلید (taqlid): Following the ruling of a mujtahid without knowing the proof.
تخریج (takhrij): Deriving rulings for new cases from the mujtahid's principles and rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in this passage, which type of mufti is required to know the proof (dalil) of the Imam's ruling?
A) Every mufti, regardless of level
B) The mujtahid fil-madhhab when performing takhrij
C) Only the absolute mujtahid (mujtahid mutlaq)
D) The naqil fatwa (transmitter)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the mujtahid fil-madhhab, who must know proofs for derivation, and the mere transmitter, who can rely on taqlid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Eleventh Principle: Answering Non-Textual Cases
Rules for mufti when no explicit ruling exists from earlier scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchy a mufti must follow when encountering a non-textual case and apply the correct procedure based on his level of qualification.

Core Idea
A mufti cannot give personal opinion; he must follow the madhhab hierarchy: texts, principles, later consensus, ijtihad, or referral.

This lesson introduces the eleventh principle of Rasm al-Mufti, which governs how a mufti should respond when faced with a case for which no explicit ruling is recorded from the Hanafi imams. The passage provides a clear procedure, emphasizing that conjecture is forbidden and that the mufti must either exert ijtihad or defer to a more learned scholar. This principle safeguards the integrity of fatwa and ensures that even novel cases are answered within the methodological framework of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core problem
Recognize that the passage addresses cases lacking explicit textual ruling (ghayr mansus). Note the condition: no statement from Imam A'zam, Sahibayn, early or later scholars.
These are cases for which no nass (explicit text) is transmitted.
2
Trace the hierarchy of procedures
Follow the order: first check conformity with the principles of the Imams (usul wa dhawabit); second, if later scholars (muta'akhkhirīn) have consensus, follow that; third, if they differ, the mufti should perform ijtihad if qualified; fourth, if the mufti is a muqallid, he must adopt the saying of the most learned scholar, even contacting by letter.
The hierarchy is: principles → later ijma → qualified ijtihad → referral.
3
Distinguish between mufti's qualifications
Understand the different duties of a mujtahid mufti versus a muqallid mufti. The muqallid cannot give his own opinion; he must defer to a more learned scholar and attribute the answer to that scholar.
The mufti's own ijtihad is only allowed if he is a mujtahid within the madhhab.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a hypothetical non-textual case, determine the mufti's procedure based on his qualification and the availability of later consensus. For example, if later scholars are silent and the mufti is a muqallid, he must find the most learned Hanafi scholar and contact him.
This demonstrates the practical application of the hierarchy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفتى فى حل مباد ۹۴ شى عقود رسم المفى مسائل جن کے بارے میں متقدمین سے کوئی صراحت نہیں ہے اور ان کی ترجیحات میں بھی ان کی پیروی کرنا لازم ہے، اگر چہ یہ فقہاء کسی غیر مجتہد کے قول کو ہی راجح قرار دیں، جیسا کہ ہم نے اس بات کو اس بحث کے آغاز میں بیان کر دیا ہے، اس لئے کہ ان لوگوں نے جس قول کو راج قرار دیا ہے محض اٹکل سے اس کو راج نہیں قرار دیا ہے، بلکہ ان کے مآخذ سے واقف ہونے کے بعد ہی اسے ترجیح دی ہے، جیسا کہ ان کی تصنیفات اس بات پر شاہد ہیں۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى : ۱۱۳)
يم المفتى فى حل من =(90) گیارہواں اصول غیر منصوص مسائل کا جواب دینا شي عقود رسم المفر مفتی کے سامنے کبھی کبھی ایسانیا واقعہ بھی پیش آتا ہے جس میں امام اعظم، صاحبین ، مشائخ مذہب اور دیگر متقدمین و متاخرین فقہاء سے کوئی صریح قول منقول نہیں ہوتا ہے ، تو اس واقعہ کی بابت مفتی کے لئے اپنی رائے پر فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا یا نہیں؟ علامہ شامی اس سوال کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں: اور اگر بعد کے مشائخ سے بھی قطعاً کوئی صریح حکم مروی نہ ہو، تو مفتی اس واقعہ میں خوب غور و فکر اور کوشش کرے، تا کہ وہ اس مسئلہ کا کوئی ایسا حکم دریافت کر سکے جس کے ذریعہ وہ اپنی ذمہ داری سے عہدہ برآ ہو سکے، اور اپنے منصب اور اس کی حرمت کے پیش نظر اس مسئلہ میں اٹکل سے گفتگو نہ کرے، اور اللہ تعالی سے ڈرے اور اس کا خوف رکھے، کیوں کہ فتوی دینا نہایت اہم معاملہ ہے، اس کی جسارت وہی کرتا ہے جو جاہل اور بد بخت ہوتا ہے۔ (شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۲۱) فتاوی قاضی خان میں ہے: اگر کوئی مسئلہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو تو اگر وہ مسئلہ ہمارے ائمہ کے اصول وضوابط کے موافق ہو تو مفتی اس پر عمل کرے، اور اگر کوئی مفتی کسی مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ سے کوئی روایت نہ پائے اور اس مسئلہ میں متاخرین کسی بات پر متفق ہوں تو مفتی اسی پر عمل کرے، اور اگر ان کا اختلاف ہو تو مفتی اجتہاد کرے، اور اس کے نزدیک جو بات درست ہو اسی پر فتوی دے، اور اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہو تو اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہو اس کے قول کو اختیار کرے اور جواب کو اسی کی طرف منسوب کرے، پس اگر اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہے وہ دوسرے شہر میں رہتا ہو تو اس سے خط کے ذریعہ رابطہ کرے، اور اس کے
Issues regarding which there is no explicit statement from the early scholars, and it is necessary to follow them even in their preferences, even if these jurists have given preference to the saying of a non-mujtahid, as we have stated this at the beginning of this discussion, because those people did not give preference to a saying based on mere conjecture, but they gave preference only after being acquainted with its sources, as their works bear witness to this. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 113)
Eleventh Principle: Answering non-textual cases. A mufti is sometimes confronted with an event regarding which there is no explicit transmitted saying from Imam A'zam, the Sahibayn, the scholars of the madhhab, and other early and later jurists. So regarding this event, is it permissible for the mufti to give a fatwa based on his own opinion or not? 'Allama Shami, while answering this question, says: If even from the later scholars there is absolutely no explicit ruling transmitted, then the mufti should reflect and exert effort in this event, so that he may discover some ruling for this issue by which he can discharge his responsibility, and in view of his position and its sanctity he should not speak about this issue based on conjecture, and he should fear Allah and have awe of Him, because giving fatwa is a very serious matter; only one who is ignorant and ill-fated dares to do it. (Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 121)
In Fatawa Qadi Khan: If a case is from non-Zahir al-Riwayah, then if that case conforms to the principles and rules of our Imams, the mufti should act upon it. And if a mufti finds no narration from our Imams regarding a case, and the later scholars are agreed on something in that case, then the mufti should act upon that. And if they differ, then the mufti should exert ijtihad, and give fatwa according to what he considers correct. And if the mufti is a muqallid and not a mujtahid, then he should adopt the saying of the one he considers the most learned and attribute the answer to him. Then if the one he considers the most learned lives in another city, he should contact him by letter, and his...
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh principle (گیارہواں اصول) from a work on the rules of issuing fatwas (Rasm al-Mufti). It addresses the situation where a mufti is faced with a case for which no explicit ruling is found in the transmitted texts of the Hanafi school — not from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, nor from the later scholars of the madhhab. The text first lays a foundation: even in cases where early scholars (متقدمین) did not explicitly rule, their preferences must be followed because they were based on knowledge of sources, not conjecture. Then it moves to the core question: can a mufti give his own opinion? The answer, from 'Allama Shami, is that if no later scholar has transmitted a ruling, the mufti must exert utmost effort (ijtihad) to derive a ruling, while fearing Allah and avoiding conjecture. Fatawa Qadi Khan provides a detailed hierarchy: for non-Zahir al-Riwayah cases, if the case matches the principles of the Imams, act on it; if later scholars agree, follow their agreement; if they differ, the mufti does ijtihad if qualified; if not qualified (muqallid), he follows the most learned scholar, even contacting him by letter if needed. This principle ensures that even in novel cases, the mufti does not give fatwa based on mere personal opinion but adheres to the methodology of the madhhab.

Key Terms
غیر منصور (ghayr mansus): Cases for which there is no explicit textual ruling (nass) in the Hanafi school sources.
متقدمین (mutaqaddimīn): Early Hanafi jurists, primarily those from the first few centuries (e.g., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
متاخرین (muta'akhkhirīn): Later Hanafi jurists, typically from the 6th century onwards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eleventh principle, what should a mufti do if he encounters a case for which there is no explicit transmitted ruling from the Hanafi imams or later scholars, and he is not a mujtahid?
A) Give fatwa based on his own reasoning (ijtihad) since no text exists.
B) Leave the question unanswered and refuse to issue a fatwa.
C) Choose the saying of the most learned Hanafi scholar he knows, even if that scholar is in another city, and contact him by letter if needed.
D) Follow the opinion of the majority of contemporary scholars regardless of madhhab.

Key Takeaway
When no explicit Hanafi ruling exists, the mufti must follow a strict hierarchy: principles of the Imams, consensus of later scholars, ijtihad if qualified, else referral to the most learned scholar – never personal conjecture.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Eleventh Principle: Non-Textual Issues and the Mufti's Obligation
Initial ruling on non-textual issues by Allamah Shami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufti's obligation when facing a non-textual issue and identify the prohibition of conjecture (atkal) in fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must never give a fatwa based on conjecture; when no text exists, he must strive to derive a ruling from principles or admit ignorance.

This lesson introduces the eleventh principle of mufti conduct, which addresses situations where no explicit textual ruling exists from the Hanafi Imams. The passage from Allamah Shami establishes that the mufti must exert deep reflection and effort, avoid baseless conjecture, and fear Allah due to the gravity of fatwa. This principle safeguards the integrity of Islamic law by preventing arbitrary opinions.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
Identify that the mufti is confronted with a case for which no explicit statement (nass) from Imam Abu Hanifa, the two Sahibayn, or earlier and later scholars has been transmitted.
This is the 'ghayr mansus' condition.
2
State the primary obligation
The mufti must exert utmost effort (taharrin wa tafakkur) to discover a ruling that allows him to discharge his responsibility. He is not free to give a personal opinion without foundation.
The verb 'yajtahid' implies a disciplined search, not arbitrary choice.
3
Apply the prohibition of conjecture
The mufti must avoid atkal (baseless conjecture) and fear Allah, recognizing that fatwa is a serious matter only the ignorant and ill-fated dare to treat lightly.
Atkal is strictly prohibited; the mufti must have a textual or analogical basis.
4
Internalize the gravity
Understand that giving fatwa without knowledge is a form of fabrication against Allah, making halal haram or haram halal. The mufti must maintain taqwa.
This is a warning against arrogance and heedlessness.

گیارہواں اصول
غیر منصوص مسائل کا جواب دینا

مفتی کے سامنے کبھی کبھی ایسا واقعہ بھی پیش آتا ہے جس میں امام اعظم، صاحبین، مشائخ مذہب اور دیگر متقدمین و متاخرین فقہاء سے کوئی صریح قول منقول نہیں ہوتا ہے، تو اس واقعہ کی بابت مفتی کے لئے اپنی رائے پر فتوی دینا جائز ہوگا یا نہیں؟
علامہ شامی اس سوال کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں: اور اگر بعد کے مشائخ سے بھی قطعاً کوئی صریح حکم مروی نہ ہو، تو مفتی اس واقعہ میں خوب غور و فکر اور کوشش کرے، تا کہ وہ اس مسئلہ کا کوئی ایسا حکم دریافت کر سکے جس کے ذریعہ وہ اپنی ذمہ داری سے عہدہ برآ ہو سکے، اور اپنے منصب اور اس کی حرمت کے پیش نظر اس مسئلہ میں اٹکل سے گفتگو نہ کرے، اور اللہ تعالی سے ڈرے اور اس کا خوف رکھے، کیوں کہ فتوی دینا نہایت اہم معاملہ ہے، اس کی جسارت وہی کرتا ہے جو جاہل اور بد بخت ہوتا ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۲۱)

فتاوی قاضی خان میں ہے: اگر کوئی مسئلہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو تو اگر وہ مسئلہ ہمارے ائمہ کے اصول وضوابط کے موافق ہو تو مفتی اس پر عمل کرے، اور اگر کوئی مفتی کسی مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ سے کوئی روایت نہ پائے اور اس مسئلہ میں متاخرین کسی بات پر متفق ہوں تو مفتی اسی پر عمل کرے، اور اگر ان کا اختلاف ہو تو مفتی اجتہاد کرے، اور اس کے نزدیک جو بات درست ہو اسی پر فتوی دے، اور اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہو تو اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہو اس کے قول کو اختیار کرے اور جواب کو اسی کی طرف منسوب کرے، پس اگر اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہے وہ دوسرے شہر میں رہتا ہو تو اس سے خط کے ذریعہ رابطہ کرے، اور اس کے بعد جواب لکھے، حلال کو حرام بنا کر یا حرام کو حلال بنا کر اللہ تعالی پر افترا پردازی سے ڈرتے ہوئے اٹکل سے (بے تکی باتیں) نہ کرے۔ فتاوی قاضی خان کی بات مکمل ہو گئی۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۲۱)

قاضی خان کی اس عبارت پر تبصرہ کرتے ہوئے ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں: میں کہتا ہوں: اور قاضی خان کے اس قول "وإن كان المفتى مقلّداً غيرَ مجتھد" سے یہ فائدہ حاصل ہوتا ہے کہ جن مسائل میں کسی فقیہ سے صراحتاً کوئی حکم مروی نہ ہو تو مقلد محض کے لئے ان مسائل میں فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتی : ۱۲۲)

اور اس کی تائید اس قول سے بھی ہوتی ہے جو البحرالرائق میں فتاوى تاتارخانیہ کے حوالہ سے منقول ہے:
اور اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی کسی ایک قول کو لے لے، پس اگر متاخرین میں سے کسی کا قول نہ پائے تو وہ خود اجتہاد کرے جب کہ وہ فقہ کی وجوہ (تفصیلات) جانتا ہو، اور فقہاء سے مشورہ بھی کرلے۔ البحر الرائق کی بات مکمل ہوگئی۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ۱۲۲)

علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں: تو تاتارخانی کا قول "إذا كان يعرف" الخ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ جو مفتی اس کو نہیں جانتا ہو، بلکہ اس نے فقہ کی ایک یا چند کتابیں پڑھ لی ہو اور اس کو سمجھ لیا ہو، اور اس میں کتابوں کی مراجعت کرنے کی صلاحیت پیدا ہوگئی ہو، اور مشہور قابل اعتماد کتابوں میں وہ مسئلہ کہاں ملے گا اس کی استعداد اس میں پیدا ہوگئی ہو، تو ایسا شخص جب کوئی واقعہ کسی کتاب میں نہ پائے تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اپنی رائے سے فتوی دے، بلکہ اس پر واجب ہے کہ وہ کہدے میں یہ مسئلہ نہیں جانتا جیسا کہ اس سے بڑے مرتبہ والوں نے لاعلمی کا اظہار کیا ہے، یعنی مجتہدین صحابہ اور ان کے بعد کے مجتہدین نے، بلکہ اس ہستی نے جس کی
The Eleventh Principle: Answering Non-Textual Issues

Sometimes a situation comes before the mufti concerning which no explicit statement is transmitted from Imam A'zam, the two companions (Sahibayn), the mashayikh of the madhhab, and other earlier and later jurists. So regarding this situation, is it permissible for the mufti to give a fatwa based on his own opinion or not?
Allamah Shami, while answering this question, says: And if even from the later mashayikh there is absolutely no explicit ruling transmitted, then the mufti should exert deep reflection and effort in this situation, so that he may discover some ruling for this matter by which he can discharge his responsibility. And with regard to his position and its sanctity, he should not speak from conjecture. And he should fear Allah and hold His awe, because giving fatwa is a very serious matter. Only the ignorant and ill-fated dare to do it.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 121)

In Fatawa Qadi Khan: If there is a matter that is from ghayr zahir al-riwaya, then if that matter is in accordance with the principles and rules of our Imams, the mufti should act upon it. And if a mufti does not find any narration from our Imams in a matter, and the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) are agreed upon something, then the mufti should act upon that. And if they differ, then the mufti should do ijtihad, and give fatwa upon what he considers correct. And if the mufti is a muqallid and not a mujtahid, then he should adopt the saying of the person who is most learned (afqah) in his view, and attribute the answer to him. Then if that person who is most learned in his view lives in another city, he should contact him by letter, then write the answer after that, fearing fabrication against Allah by making halal haram or haram halal, and not speak from conjecture (baseless talk). The statement of Fatawa Qadi Khan is complete.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 121)

Commenting on this statement of Qadi Khan, Ibn Abidin Shami says: I say: And from this saying of Qadi Khan, 'And if the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid,' the benefit is derived that in matters where no explicit ruling is transmitted from any jurist, it is not permissible for a pure muqallid to give fatwa in those matters.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 122)

And this is also supported by the statement quoted in al-Bahr al-Raiq from Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya:
And if there is difference among the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin), then the mufti should take one saying. Then if he does not find any saying from the later scholars, he should do ijtihad himself, provided that he knows the reasons (details) of fiqh, and also consults the jurists. The statement of al-Bahr al-Raiq is complete.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 122)

Allamah Shami says: So the saying of Tatarkhani, 'If he knows...' etc., is evidence that the mufti who does not know this, rather he has read one or several books of fiqh and understood them, and has developed the ability to refer to books, and has acquired the capacity to know where that matter will be found in famous reliable books, then such a person, when he does not find a situation in any book, it is not permissible for him to give a fatwa from his own opinion. Rather, it is wajib upon him to say, 'I do not know this matter,' just as those greater in rank have expressed ignorance, i.e., the mujtahid Companions and the mujtahids after them, rather even that personality whose...
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh principle of mufti conduct, which addresses how to handle cases where no explicit textual ruling exists from the Hanafi Imams. The author begins by posing the central question: when a mufti encounters a situation where no explicit statement is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa, the two Sahibayn, or any early or later Hanafi authority, may he give a fatwa based on his own opinion? Allamah Shami responds that the mufti must exert utmost effort and reflection to derive a ruling that fulfills his responsibility. He must avoid conjecture, fear Allah, and recognize the gravity of issuing fatwas. This is followed by a quotation from Fatawa Qadi Khan, which outlines a hierarchical process: first, check if the matter is from ghayr zahir al-riwaya and whether it aligns with the principles of the Imams; then look for consensus among later scholars; if they differ, the mufti may perform ijtihad. However, if the mufti is a muqallid (not a mujtahid), he must follow the opinion of the most learned scholar, even if that scholar is in another city, and attribute the fatwa to him. He must not speak from conjecture. Ibn Abidin Shami comments that this implies a pure muqallid cannot give fatwa in matters where no explicit ruling exists. Additional support from al-Bahr al-Raiq and Tatarkhani states that if the mufti knows the details of fiqh and has consulted jurists, he may do ijtihad; otherwise, he must say 'I do not know,' following the example of the greater mujtahids. The lesson emphasizes the strict limitations on muftis who are not fully qualified mujtahids, especially in non-textual issues.

Key Terms
غیر منصوص (ghayr mansus): Cases for which no explicit text (nass) from the Hanafi Imams is found.
مقلد (muqallid): A jurist who follows the rulings of a mujtahid without being qualified to perform ijtihad themselves.
مجتہد (mujtahid): A jurist qualified to derive rulings independently from primary sources.
اٹکل (atkal): Baseless conjecture or arbitrary opinion without proper evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allamah Shami, what is the mufti's primary obligation when no explicit ruling from the Hanafi Imams exists?
A) He should remain silent and not answer.
B) He should exert deep reflection and effort to discover a ruling.
C) He may give a fatwa based on his general knowledge.
D) He must refer the question to the ruler.

Key Takeaway
In non-textual issues, the mufti must strive to derive a ruling from principles and avoid conjecture; a muqallid must refer to a more learned scholar or admit ignorance.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Hierarchy of Authority in Non-Textual Issues
Detailed hierarchy from Fatawa Qadi Khan and commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchical steps (principles, consensus, ijtihad, referral) that a mufti must follow when no explicit text exists from Hanafi Imams.

Core Idea
When no explicit text exists, the mufti follows a hierarchy: principles, then later consensus, then ijtihad; a muqallid must refer to the most learned scholar.

This lesson details the procedural hierarchy outlined by Qadi Khan and expanded by Ibn Abidin for dealing with non-textual issues. The mufti must first check if the issue aligns with the Imams' principles, then look for consensus among later scholars, and only then perform ijtihad if qualified. A muqallid mufti is strictly limited to following a more learned scholar or admitting ignorance.

Guided Path
1
First check: alignment with Imams' principles
If the case is from ghayr zahir al-riwaya, the mufti should first see if it agrees with the usul and dawabit of the Hanafi Imams. If yes, act on that.
This step ensures consistency with the madhhab's framework.
2
Second check: consensus of later scholars
If no narration from the Imams exists, the mufti looks for ijma' among the muta'akhkhirin (later scholars). If they agree, he follows that.
Ijma' of later scholars is a binding source in the fatwa hierarchy.
3
Third step: ijtihad by qualified mufti
If later scholars differ, the mufti may perform ijtihad if he is a mujtahid. He must know the details of fiqh and consult others.
Only a mujtahid can exercise ijtihad; others must stop here.
4
Referral for the muqallid mufti
If the mufti is a muqallid (not a mujtahid), he must adopt the opinion of the most learned scholar (afqah) in his view, even if that scholar is in another city. He should correspond and attribute the fatwa to that scholar.
The muqallid cannot give his own opinion; he must rely on a higher authority.
5
Final safeguard: admit ignorance
If the mufti cannot find any authority or is uncertain, he must say 'I do not know,' following the example of the greater scholars.
This is not a failure but a protection of the religion.

(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۲۱)

فتاوی قاضی خان میں ہے: اگر کوئی مسئلہ غیر ظاہر الروایہ میں ہو تو اگر وہ مسئلہ ہمارے ائمہ کے اصول وضوابط کے موافق ہو تو مفتی اس پر عمل کرے، اور اگر کوئی مفتی کسی مسئلہ میں ہمارے ائمہ سے کوئی روایت نہ پائے اور اس مسئلہ میں متاخرین کسی بات پر متفق ہوں تو مفتی اسی پر عمل کرے، اور اگر ان کا اختلاف ہو تو مفتی اجتہاد کرے، اور اس کے نزدیک جو بات درست ہو اسی پر فتوی دے، اور اگر مفتی مقلد ہو مجتہد نہ ہو تو اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہو اس کے قول کو اختیار کرے اور جواب کو اسی کی طرف منسوب کرے، پس اگر اس کے نزدیک جو شخص زیادہ فقیہ ہے وہ دوسرے شہر میں رہتا ہو تو اس سے خط کے ذریعہ رابطہ کرے، اور اس کے بعد جواب لکھے، حلال کو حرام بنا کر یا حرام کو حلال بنا کر اللہ تعالی پر افترا پردازی سے ڈرتے ہوئے اٹکل سے (بے تکی باتیں) نہ کرے۔ فتاوی قاضی خان کی بات مکمل ہو گئی۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتى: ۱۲۱)

قاضی خان کی اس عبارت پر تبصرہ کرتے ہوئے ابن عابدین شامی فرماتے ہیں: میں کہتا ہوں: اور قاضی خان کے اس قول "وإن كان المفتى مقلّداً غيرَ مجتھد" سے یہ فائدہ حاصل ہوتا ہے کہ جن مسائل میں کسی فقیہ سے صراحتاً کوئی حکم مروی نہ ہو تو مقلد محض کے لئے ان مسائل میں فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتی : ۱۲۲)

اور اس کی تائید اس قول سے بھی ہوتی ہے جو البحرالرائق میں فتاوى تاتارخانیہ کے حوالہ سے منقول ہے:
اور اگر متاخرین میں اختلاف ہو تو مفتی کسی ایک قول کو لے لے، پس اگر متاخرین میں سے کسی کا قول نہ پائے تو وہ خود اجتہاد کرے جب کہ وہ فقہ کی وجوہ (تفصیلات) جانتا ہو، اور فقہاء سے مشورہ بھی کرلے۔ البحر الرائق کی بات مکمل ہوگئی۔
(شرح عقود رسم المفتی: ۱۲۲)

علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں: تو تاتارخانی کا قول "إذا كان يعرف" الخ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ جو مفتی اس کو نہیں جانتا ہو، بلکہ اس نے فقہ کی ایک یا چند کتابیں پڑھ لی ہو اور اس کو سمجھ لیا ہو، اور اس میں کتابوں کی مراجعت کرنے کی صلاحیت پیدا ہوگئی ہو، اور مشہور قابل اعتماد کتابوں میں وہ مسئلہ کہاں ملے گا اس کی استعداد اس میں پیدا ہوگئی ہو، تو ایسا شخص جب کوئی واقعہ کسی کتاب میں نہ پائے تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اپنی رائے سے فتوی دے، بلکہ اس پر واجب ہے کہ وہ کہدے میں یہ مسئلہ نہیں جانتا جیسا کہ اس سے بڑے مرتبہ والوں نے لاعلمی کا اظہار کیا ہے، یعنی مجتہدین صحابہ اور ان کے بعد کے مجتہدین نے، بلکہ اس ہستی نے جس کی
The Eleventh Principle: Answering Non-Textual Issues

Sometimes a situation comes before the mufti concerning which no explicit statement is transmitted from Imam A'zam, the two companions (Sahibayn), the mashayikh of the madhhab, and other earlier and later jurists. So regarding this situation, is it permissible for the mufti to give a fatwa based on his own opinion or not?
Allamah Shami, while answering this question, says: And if even from the later mashayikh there is absolutely no explicit ruling transmitted, then the mufti should exert deep reflection and effort in this situation, so that he may discover some ruling for this matter by which he can discharge his responsibility. And with regard to his position and its sanctity, he should not speak from conjecture. And he should fear Allah and hold His awe, because giving fatwa is a very serious matter. Only the ignorant and ill-fated dare to do it.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 121)

In Fatawa Qadi Khan: If there is a matter that is from ghayr zahir al-riwaya, then if that matter is in accordance with the principles and rules of our Imams, the mufti should act upon it. And if a mufti does not find any narration from our Imams in a matter, and the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) are agreed upon something, then the mufti should act upon that. And if they differ, then the mufti should do ijtihad, and give fatwa upon what he considers correct. And if the mufti is a muqallid and not a mujtahid, then he should adopt the saying of the person who is most learned (afqah) in his view, and attribute the answer to him. Then if that person who is most learned in his view lives in another city, he should contact him by letter, then write the answer after that, fearing fabrication against Allah by making halal haram or haram halal, and not speak from conjecture (baseless talk). The statement of Fatawa Qadi Khan is complete.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 121)

Commenting on this statement of Qadi Khan, Ibn Abidin Shami says: I say: And from this saying of Qadi Khan, 'And if the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid,' the benefit is derived that in matters where no explicit ruling is transmitted from any jurist, it is not permissible for a pure muqallid to give fatwa in those matters.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 122)

And this is also supported by the statement quoted in al-Bahr al-Raiq from Fatawa Tatarkhaniyya:
And if there is difference among the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin), then the mufti should take one saying. Then if he does not find any saying from the later scholars, he should do ijtihad himself, provided that he knows the reasons (details) of fiqh, and also consults the jurists. The statement of al-Bahr al-Raiq is complete.
(Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 122)

Allamah Shami says: So the saying of Tatarkhani, 'If he knows...' etc., is evidence that the mufti who does not know this, rather he has read one or several books of fiqh and understood them, and has developed the ability to refer to books, and has acquired the capacity to know where that matter will be found in famous reliable books, then such a person, when he does not find a situation in any book, it is not permissible for him to give a fatwa from his own opinion. Rather, it is wajib upon him to say, 'I do not know this matter,' just as those greater in rank have expressed ignorance, i.e., the mujtahid Companions and the mujtahids after them, rather even that personality whose...
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh principle of mufti conduct, which addresses how to handle cases where no explicit textual ruling exists from the Hanafi Imams. The author begins by posing the central question: when a mufti encounters a situation where no explicit statement is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa, the two Sahibayn, or any early or later Hanafi authority, may he give a fatwa based on his own opinion? Allamah Shami responds that the mufti must exert utmost effort and reflection to derive a ruling that fulfills his responsibility. He must avoid conjecture, fear Allah, and recognize the gravity of issuing fatwas. This is followed by a quotation from Fatawa Qadi Khan, which outlines a hierarchical process: first, check if the matter is from ghayr zahir al-riwaya and whether it aligns with the principles of the Imams; then look for consensus among later scholars; if they differ, the mufti may perform ijtihad. However, if the mufti is a muqallid (not a mujtahid), he must follow the opinion of the most learned scholar, even if that scholar is in another city, and attribute the fatwa to him. He must not speak from conjecture. Ibn Abidin Shami comments that this implies a pure muqallid cannot give fatwa in matters where no explicit ruling exists. Additional support from al-Bahr al-Raiq and Tatarkhani states that if the mufti knows the details of fiqh and has consulted jurists, he may do ijtihad; otherwise, he must say 'I do not know,' following the example of the greater mujtahids. The lesson emphasizes the strict limitations on muftis who are not fully qualified mujtahids, especially in non-textual issues.

Key Terms
غیر منصوص (ghayr mansus): Cases for which no explicit text (nass) from the Hanafi Imams is found.
مقلد (muqallid): A jurist who follows the rulings of a mujtahid without being qualified to perform ijtihad themselves.
مجتہد (mujtahid): A jurist qualified to derive rulings independently from primary sources.
اٹکل (atkal): Baseless conjecture or arbitrary opinion without proper evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Qadi Khan, if a mufti does not find any narration from the Imams and later scholars differ, what is the next step?
A) He must remain silent and not give a fatwa.
B) He may perform ijtihad if he is a mujtahid.
C) He should choose the opinion of the majority of later scholars.
D) He must refer the matter to the government.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow a strict hierarchy in non-textual issues: principles, later consensus, ijtihad (if qualified), referral (if muqallid), or admission of ignorance.

The Muqallid Mufti's Authority and Conditions for Ijtihad
Commentary on muqallid mufti's fatwa limits and ijtihad conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for a muqallid mufti's fatwa authority: identify when he must say 'I do not know' and when he may perform ijtihad, and construct the appropriate fatwa response.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti must not guess; if no ruling exists, he says 'I do not know' or, if qualified, performs ijtihad.

In this passage from the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', Ibn Abidin clarifies the boundaries of a muqallid mufti's authority. While such a mufti cannot invent rulings, the text acknowledges a narrow path for ijtihad when specific conditions are met. Understanding these limits is essential for responsible fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rule
The muqallid mufti, not being a mujtahid, cannot give a fatwa from his own opinion; he must rely on transmitted rulings. Ibn Abidin extracts this from Qadi Khan's statement.
This is the default position: no independent reasoning.
2
Recognize the exception
If later scholars (mutakhkhirun) differ, the muqallid may adopt one of their views. If he finds no transmitted ruling and knows the detailed aspects of fiqh (wujuh al-fiqh) and consults jurists, he may perform ijtihad.
The exception is conditional: knowledge + consultation.
3
Apply the condition check
Does the mufti have sufficient knowledge and research ability? If not, he must say 'I do not know'. Ibn Abidin emphasizes that reading a few books does not qualify one for ijtihad.
Saying 'I do not know' is obligatory for the unqualified.
4
Consider the rarity factor
It is extremely rare for a case to be entirely unaddressed; either the exact ruling or a general maxim (qa'ida kulliya) covers it. The mufti should search thoroughly before concluding no ruling exists.
This prevents premature claims of missing rulings.

The mufti in the commentary on Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. After writing the answer, he should not speak nonsense, fearing slander against Allah by declaring halal haram or haram halal. The statement of Qadi Khan's fatwas is complete. Commenting on Qadi Khan's statement, Ibn Abidin al-Shami says: I say: From Qadi Khan's saying 'And if the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid', the benefit obtained is that in cases where no ruling is explicitly transmitted from any jurist, it is not permissible for a mere muqallid to give a fatwa in those cases. And this is also supported by the statement transmitted in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq from Tatar Khaniyya: 'And if the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid, and if the later scholars disagree, he may adopt one of them. If he does not find a statement of the later scholars, then he may exercise ijtihad if he knows the aspects of fiqh and consults the jurists.' Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Allama Shami says: So Tatar Khani's saying 'if he knows...' etc. is proof that a mufti who does not know that, but has read and understood one or several books of fiqh, and has developed the ability to refer to books, and has the capacity to know where the issue is found in reliable books, such a person, when he does not find an incident in any book, it is not permissible for him to give a fatwa from his own opinion. Rather, it is obligatory upon him to say: 'I do not know this issue', just as those of higher rank (i.e., the mujtahid Sahaba and later mujtahids, even the one who was supported by revelation, may Allah have mercy and peace upon them) expressed ignorance. Allama Shami further says: And the predominant assumption is that the mufti's not finding the expression (i.e., the statements of jurists) in a case is due to his lack of searching or because he does not know the place where that issue is mentioned. Because it is very rare and uncommon that an incident occurs and its mention is not found in the books of the madhhab; either exactly that same issue is mentioned, or a general maxim is mentioned that includes that incident.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' discusses the limits of a muallid mufti's authority. The text first quotes Qadi Khan's ruling that a muqallid mufti, who is not a mujtahid, must not engage in speculative statements. Ibn Abidin al-Shami then draws an important inference: such a mufti cannot give a fatwa in matters where no explicit ruling from a jurist is transmitted. This is then supported by a quotation from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (citing Tatar Khaniyya), which adds an exception: if later scholars (mutakhkhirun) disagree, the muqallid mufti may choose one of them; if no such opinion exists, he may perform ijtihad provided he knows the detailed aspects of fiqh and consults jurists. Ibn Abidin clarifies that this exception does not apply to a muqallid who merely read a few books; such a mufti must admit ignorance and say 'I do not know', following the example of great scholars. The passage concludes with the observation that it is extremely rare to find a case not addressed in madhhab books; either the exact case is there or a general maxim covers it.

Key Terms
مقلد (muqallid): A person who follows a madhhab without being a mujtahid; in this context, a mufti who is not an independent jurist but relies on transmitted rulings.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A scholar capable of deriving rulings from primary sources through independent reasoning (ijtihad).
متأخرون (mutakhkhirun): Later scholars of the madhhab, as opposed to early authorities like Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
فتوى (fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Refer the questioner to another madhhab.
D) Remain silent.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti is bound by transmitted rulings; in their absence, he must either say 'I do not know' or, if qualified, engage in ijtihad.

The Twelfth Principle: Mafhum Mukhalif and Hanafi Textual Classification
Explains the twelfth principle and compares Hanafi vs Shafi'i textual classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of mafhum mukhalif to fiqh texts and distinguish the four Hanafi types of textual indication from the Shafi'i two-type classification.

Core Idea
A restrictive condition in a text implies the opposite ruling when absent — a mufti must recognise this.

This lesson introduces a key principle for muftis: when a fiqh text restricts a ruling to a specific condition or description, the absence of that restriction yields a different ruling. Understanding how texts convey meaning is essential for accurate fatwa. The lesson also presents the Hanafi classification of textual indications, which is more detailed than the Shafi'i approach, affecting how rulings are derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the restrictive element
Read the fiqh text and pinpoint any condition (shart) or description (sifat) that qualifies the ruling. This is the trigger for mafhum mukhalif.
In the triple divorce example, 'consummated' is the restrictive description.
2
Infer the opposite ruling
Apply mafhum mukhalif: when the restriction is absent, the opposite ruling applies. For the non-consummated wife, triple divorce does not occur; only one divorce takes effect.
This inference is wajib for the mufti unless there is explicit text (manqul) stating otherwise.
3
Classify the textual indication
Determine which of the four Hanafi categories (ibara, ishara, dalala, iqtida) the derived meaning falls under. The explicit wording gives ibara; the implied opposite is ishara or dalala depending on the link.
Hanafis treat implied meanings as separate categories, while Shafi'is subsume them under mafhum.
4
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i classification
Note that Hanafis recognise four types of dalalat al-nass: ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. Shafi'is and others recognise only two: mantiq (explicit) and mafhum (implicit). Understand the practical implication: Hanafis can extract more rulings from a single text.
The difference is methodological and affects fatwa derivation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سم المفتى فى حل مباد بارہواں اصول مفتی کا مفہوم مخالف کا اعتبار کرنا شن عقود رسم المفى ا فقہی کتابوں کا ایک خاص اسلوب ہوتا ہے جس کے تحت شرعی مسائل کو نقل کیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ عبارت میں کسی مسئلہ کو کسی شرط یا صفت وغیرہ کی قید سے مقید کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس صفت اور شرط کے نہ پائے جانے کی صورت میں دونوں کا حکم الگ الگ ہوگا۔ مثلا فقہی کتابوں میں ایک مسئلہ لکھا ہوا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص اپنی مدخولہ بیوی سے انت طالق انت طالق انت طالق کہے اور تاکید کی نیت نہ ہوتو اس کی بیوی پر تین طلاق واقع ہوگی تو اس عبارت میں مدخولہ کی قید سے اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ بیوی اگر غیر مدخول بہا ہو تو تین طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی بلکہ ایک ہی طلاق سے وہ بائنہ ہو جائے گی۔ لہذا ایک مفتی کے لئے نصوص اور فقہی عبارات کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے طریقہ کار کو سمجھنا انتہائی ضروری امر ہے ، ذیل میں اس ضابطہ کی مزید تشریح کی جاتی ہے: معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے نصوص کے اقسام فقہاء احناف کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے ۴ قسمیں ہیں جو درج ذیل ہیں : عبارة النص ، اشارۃ النص، دلالۃ النص اور اقتضاء النص ، جب کہ شوافع اور دیگر اصولیین کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے صرف ۲ قسمیں ہیں: منطوق اور مفہوم ۔ (التحرير في أصول الفقه : ۲۸ ، التقرير والتحبير : ١٤٥،١٤٠/١، اصول الفقه الاسلامي للزحيلي: ٤٣٨/١ ، اصول الفقه لابی زهره: ۱۳۹) ذیل میں ان میں سے ہر ایک قسم کا مختصر تعارف مع مثال کے تحریر کیا جارہا ہے۔
The mufti's duty in solving… The Twelfth Principle: The mufti's consideration of the opposite meaning (mafhum mukhalif). Fiqh books have a particular style to transmit legal rulings. So, when an issue is restricted by a condition or description, it implies that in the absence of that description or condition, the ruling is different. For example, in fiqh books it is written: If a man says to his wife with whom he has consummated marriage: 'You are divorced, you are divorced, you are divorced' without intention of emphasis, then three divorces occur. The restriction 'consummated' indicates that if she is not consummated, three divorces do not occur; rather, one divorce makes her bain (irrevocably separate). Therefore, a mufti must understand the method by which texts and fiqh phrases indicate their meanings. Below is further explanation of this rule. Types of texts with respect to indication of meaning: According to Hanafi jurists, there are four types: ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, and iqtida' al-nass. According to Shafi'is and other usuliyyun, there are only two types: mantiq and mafhum. (References: al-Tahrir fi Usul al-Fiqh: 28, al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir: 1/145,140, Usul al-Fiqh al-Islami li al-Zuhayli: 1/438, Usul al-Fiqh li Abi Zahra: 139) Below, each type is briefly introduced with examples.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage introduces the twelfth principle of fatwa: the mufti must consider mafhum mukhalif (opposite implication). It explains that fiqh texts often use restrictive language (conditions, descriptions), which indicates that the ruling changes when the restriction is absent. The example of triple divorce with a consummated wife illustrates this: the mention of 'consummated' implies that for a non-consummated wife, only one divorce occurs. The passage then highlights the importance for a mufti to understand how texts convey meaning. It presents the Hanafi classification of four types of textual indications (ibara, ishara, dalala, iqtida) versus the Shafi'i classification into two (mantiq and mafhum). This distinction is crucial because it affects how rulings are derived from texts. The references given are from major works of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
عبارة النص (ibārat al-naṣṣ): The explicit meaning derived directly from the wording of the text.
اشارة النص (ishārat al-naṣṣ): An implied meaning that is alluded to by the text but not explicitly stated.
دلالة النص (dalālat al-naṣṣ): A meaning derived from the text by inference or reasoning, not directly from wording.
اقتضاء النص (iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ): A necessary condition or requirement for the text to make sense or be applied.
منطوق (manṭūq): The explicitly stated meaning of the text (mantiq).
مفہوم (mafhūm): The implied meaning derived from the text, including mafhum muwafiq and mukhalif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many types of textual indication (dalalat al-nass) do Hanafi jurists recognize?
A) Two: mantiq and mafhum
B) Three: ibara, ishara, and iqtida
C) Four: ibara, ishara, dalala, and iqtida
D) Five: including qiyas

Key Takeaway
A mufti must consider mafhum mukhalif (opposite implication) when a text restricts a ruling with a condition or description, and must be aware of the four Hanafi types of textual indication to derive accurate rulings.

The Twelfth Principle: Mafhum Mukhalif and Hanafi Textual Indications
Defines mufti's principle of mafhum mukhalif and introduces Hanafi classification of textual indications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Twelfth Principle of Rasm al-Mufti regarding mafhum mukhalif and identify the four types of textual indication according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The mufti must infer opposite rulings from conditions in texts — a skill rooted in Hanafi textual typology.

This lesson explains a fundamental principle for muftis: when a fiqh ruling is conditioned or described, the opposite case carries a different ruling. The passage then lays out the Hanafi classification of how texts convey meaning — four types vs. the Shafi'i two — beginning with 'ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass with Quranic examples.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the principle of mafhum mukhalif
The passage's key rule: any condition or attribute in a text implies its opposite has a different ruling. Example: the word 'madkhula' in the talaq case implies a non-consummated wife receives only one talaq.
This principle is specific to mufti's methodology.
2
Identify the Hanafi fourfold classification
The passage lists: 'ibarah (direct), isharah (implied necessary meaning), dalalah (indication by context), iqtida' (requisite meaning). Understand their definitions.
Only 'ibarah and isharah are defined in this passage.
3
Compare with Shafi'i classification
Shafi'is use only mantiq (expressed) and mafhum (understood). This difference matters for deriving rulings.
The Hanafi system is more granular.
4
Apply to the Quranic example of trade and usury
From 2:275, via 'ibarah we derive that trade and usury are distinct (primary) and trade is halal, usury haram (secondary).
Shows how 'ibarah yields both primary and secondary intended meanings.
5
Apply to the Quranic example of breastfeeding mother
From 2:233, via 'ibarah we get that father supports mother and child is attributed to father. The second is isharah — not directly intended but necessary for ruling.
Distinguishes direct from implied indication.

بارہواں اصول
مفتی کا مفہوم مخالف کا اعتبار کرنا
فقہی کتابوں کا ایک خاص اسلوب ہوتا ہے جس کے تحت شرعی مسائل کو نقل کیا جاتا ہے، چنانچہ عبارت میں کسی مسئلہ کو کسی شرط یا صفت وغیرہ کی قید سے مقید کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس صفت اور شرط کے نہ پائے جانے کی صورت میں دونوں کا حکم الگ الگ ہوگا۔ مثلا فقہی کتابوں میں ایک مسئلہ لکھا ہوا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص اپنی مدخولہ بیوی سے انت طالق انت طالق انت طالق کہے اور تاکید کی نیت نہ ہوتو اس کی بیوی پر تین طلاق واقع ہوگی تو اس عبارت میں مدخولہ کی قید سے اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ بیوی اگر غیر مدخول بہا ہو تو تین طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی بلکہ ایک ہی طلاق سے وہ بائنہ ہو جائے گی۔
لہذا ایک مفتی کے لئے نصوص اور فقہی عبارات کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے طریقہ کار کو سمجھنا انتہائی ضروری امر ہے ، ذیل میں اس ضابطہ کی مزید تشریح کی جاتی ہے: معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے نصوص کے اقسام
فقہاء احناف کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے ۴ قسمیں ہیں جو درج ذیل ہیں : عبارة النص ، اشارۃ النص، دلالۃ النص اور اقتضاء النص ، جب کہ شوافع اور دیگر اصولیین کے نزدیک نصوص کی اپنے معنی پر دلالت کے اعتبار سے صرف ۲ قسمیں ہیں:
منطوق اور مفہوم ۔
ذیل میں ان میں سے ہر ایک قسم کا مختصر تعارف مع مثال کے تحریر کیا جارہا ہے۔
عبارة الحص کی تعریف مع مثال
نص کا ایسے معنی پر دلالت کرنا جو نص سے بغیر غور وفکر کے سمجھ میں آجائے اور اس نص سے وہی معنی مقصود بھی ہو اس کو عبارۃ النص کہتے ہیں، خواہ وہ معنی اس نص سے مستقل طور پر مقصود ہو یا ضمنی طور پر، جیسے اللہ تعالی کا ارشاد ہے اَحَلَّ اللهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الربوا (سورة البقرة: ۲۷۵) (ترجمہ: اللہ نے بیع کو حلال قرار دیا اور سود کو حرام قرار دیا ) اس آیت سے عبارۃ اس کے طور پر دو معانی سمجھ میں آتے ہیں: پہلا معنی یہ ہے کہ پیچ اور رہو دونوں الگ الگ چیزیں ہیں ایک نہیں ہیں، جیسا کہ مشرکین کا خیال ہے اور یہ معنی اس آیت کا مقصود اصلی ہے، کیوں کہ یہ آیت انہیں لوگوں کی تردید میں وارد ہوئی ہے جو بیع اور ربوکو ایک ہی شی ء قرار دیتے تھے، دوسرا معنی یہ سمجھ میں آرہا ہے کہ بیع حلال ہے اور ر بو حرام ہے اور یہ معنی اس آیت کا مقصود تبھی ہے۔
اشارة النص کی تعریف مع مثال
نص کا ایسے معنی پر دلالت کرنا جو معنی اس کلام سے نہ تو مستقل طور پر مقصود ہو اور نہ ہی ضمنی طور پر لیکن وہ معنی اس حکم کو تلزم ہو جس حکم کی وضاحت کے لئے وہ کلام لایا گیا ہے اس کو اشارة النص کہا جاتا ہے، بسا اوقات وہ لازمی معنی نص میں غور وفکر کئے بغیر سمجھ میں آجاتا ہے اور کبھی کبھی معمولی غور و فکر کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے، اس کی مثال اللہ تعالی کا یہ ارشاد ہے ﴿وَعلَی المَوْلُوْدِلَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوف ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۳۳) (اور جس باپ کا وہ بچہ ہے اس پر لازم ہے کہ وہ معروف طریقے پر ان ماؤں کے کھانے اور لباس کا خرچ اٹھائے ) اس آیت میں عبارة النص سے یہ معنی سمجھ میں آیا کہ دودھ پلانے والی ماؤں کا خرچہ باپ کے ذمہ ہے اور یہ کہ اولاد کی نسبت والد کی طرف ہوتی ہے ماں کی طرف نہیں، اور یہ دونوں معانی اس آیت سے مقصود ہیں، پہلا معنی مستقل طور پر اور دوسرا معنی ضمنی طور پر مقصود ہے، اس لئے
The Twelfth Principle: The Mufti's Consideration of the Opposite Meaning (Mafhum Mukhalif)
Fiqh books have a particular style in which legal rulings are transmitted. Therefore, when a ruling in a text is qualified by a condition or attribute, it implies that in the absence of that condition or attribute, the ruling will be different. For example, in fiqh books it is written that if a person says to his wife whom he has consummated marriage with: 'You are divorced, you are divorced, you are divorced,' and he did not intend emphasis, then three divorces will occur. In this text, the qualification 'madkhula' (consummated) indicates that if the wife is non-consummated, three divorces will not occur; rather, she will become bainah (irrevocably divorced) with one divorce.
Therefore, for a mufti it is extremely essential to understand the method by which texts and fiqh expressions indicate their meanings. Below is further explanation of this principle: Types of texts in terms of indication to meaning.
According to Hanafi jurists, in terms of indication to meaning, there are four types of texts: 'ibarat al-nass (direct indication), isharat al-nass (implied indication), dalalat al-nass (indicative indication), and iqtida' al-nass (requisite indication). Whereas according to Shafi'is and other usul scholars, there are only two types: mantiq (expressed) and mafhum (understood).
Below is a brief introduction with examples of each type.
Definition and example of 'ibarat al-nass:
A text indicating a meaning that is understood from the text without reflection and that meaning is intended from the text—this is called 'ibarat al-nass, whether that meaning is intended independently or subordinately. For example, Allah's saying: 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' (Surah al-Baqarah: 275). From this verse, as 'ibarah, two meanings are understood: first, that trade and usury are two separate things, not the same, as the polytheists thought; this meaning is the primary intent of the verse, as it was revealed in refutation of those who considered trade and usury the same. The second meaning understood is that trade is permissible and usury is forbidden, and this meaning is also intended by the verse.
Definition and example of isharat al-nass:
A text indicating a meaning that is neither independently nor subordinately intended by the speech, but that meaning is necessary for the ruling for which the speech was brought—this is called isharat al-nass. Sometimes that necessary meaning is understood without reflection, and sometimes it requires slight reflection. An example is Allah's saying: 'And upon the father [of the child] is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable' (Surah al-Baqarah: 233). From this verse, through 'ibarah, it is understood that the expenses of the breastfeeding mothers are upon the father, and also that the child is attributed to the father, not the mother. Both meanings are intended: the first independently and the second subordinately. Therefore...

Commentary
This passage presents a crucial principle for a mufti: when a ruling in a fiqh text is qualified by a condition (shart) or attribute (sifah), it implies that the ruling changes if that condition or attribute is absent. This is known as mafhum mukhalif (opposite meaning). The example given is the case of uttering triple talaq to a wife with whom consummation has occurred (madkhula). The mention of 'madkhula' indicates that if the wife is non-consummated (ghayr madkhula), the ruling differs: only one talaq occurs, and it is bain (irrevocable). Thus, a mufti must recognize these implications.

The text then explains that understanding this requires knowledge of the four types of textual indication according to the Hanafis: 'ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, and iqtida' al-nass. In contrast, the Shafi'is and other usul scholars categorize into only two: mantiq (the uttered expression) and mafhum (what is understood). This difference impacts how rulings are derived.

The definition of 'ibarat al-nass is given: the direct meaning that comes from the text without need for reflection, and it is the intended meaning—either primary (as the refutation of the polytheists) or secondary (the permissibility of trade and prohibition of usury). 

Isharat al-nass is defined as a meaning that is not directly intended by the text, but is necessary for the ruling to be valid. For example, from the verse about the father's obligation to provide for the breastfeeding mother, we derive two meanings through 'ibarah: (1) the father must provide for her, and (2) the child is attributed to the father. The second meaning (attribution to the father) is not the primary purpose of the verse, but it necessarily follows from it. This is indicated by 'isharah. 

The passage prepares the mufti to identify and apply these types of indication when issuing fatwas.

Key Terms
عبارة النص (‘ibārat al-naṣṣ): The direct indication of a text to a meaning that is understood without reflection and is intended (either primarily or subordinately).
اشارة النص (ishārat al-naṣṣ): The indication of a text to a meaning that is not directly intended but is necessary for the ruling to be valid; it may require slight reflection.
مفہوم مخالف (mafhūm mukhālif): The opposite understanding derived from a condition or attribute mentioned in the text; e.g., if a condition is stated, its absence implies a different ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the implication of the condition 'madkhula' in the triple talaq example?
A) It does not affect the ruling.
B) It implies that if the wife is non-consummated, only one talaq occurs.
C) It means the talaq must be verbalized three times.
D) It requires the presence of witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must master the Hanafi classification of textual indications — 'ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida' — to correctly apply the principle of mafhum mukhalif.
